Perfect! I have all the context. You're at the sunken Temple of Zeboim, about 
to begin Phase 1 of the Dragon Army fleet operation-recovering the Tempest 
Scepter. Let me set the scene.
 
THE SUNKEN TEMPLE OF ZEBOIM
Phase 1: Artifact Recovery
The Stormbreaker rocks gently at anchor, positioned precisely above the 
coordinates Admiral Kethren provided. The water here is deeper than your 
coastal sahuagin mission-120 feet down-but clearer. Sunlight penetrates the 
first fifty feet, then fades to a murky twilight.
Captain Andra stands at the rail beside you, studying the water. "Temple's 
been down there about 280 years, since the Cataclysm. Zeboim's priests knew 
it was coming-sealed the inner sanctum before the city sank. That's why the 
Scepter survived." She glances at you. "Most artifacts of the gods were lost in 
the Cataclysm. Those that remain..." She doesn't finish, but the implication is 
clear: they're powerful, and they're dangerous.
Kessa checks her gear one more time-the +1 ceremonial daggers, her bracers, 
the harpoon. "So we're looking for a sealed sanctum inside a temple that's 
been underwater for three centuries. Should be in pristine condition, right?" 
Her tone is dry, but you catch the excitement beneath it.
Cyrus adjusts his holy symbol. "Zeboim is the goddess of storms, tempests, 
and the sea-temperamental, vengeful, but also... protective of those who 
respect her domain." He looks at the water with something like reverence. "If 
the Scepter is there, it will be guarded. By what, I cannot say."
Your equipment check:
*	Cloak of Manta Ray (swim 60 ft, water breathing-unlimited duration)
*	Trident of Warning (+1, advantage on initiative, party can't be 
surprised)
*	Ring of Mind Shielding (mental protection-important if there are 
aberrations down there)
*	2 Potions of Greater Healing (4d4+4)
*	1 Potion of Superior Healing (8d4+8)
*	1 Aboleth Mucus Vial (probably not relevant here, but you never know)
*	2 Dimension Door scrolls (emergency escape)
*	Signal flares (red/green/black)
Kessa has:
*	Bracers of Defense (AC 17)
*	Potion of Gaseous Form (emergency escape)
*	Potion of Superior Healing (8d4+8)
*	Her usual arsenal of daggers and weapons
Cyrus has:
*	Amulet of the Depths (swim speed, water breathing, cold resistance, 
speak with dead 1/day)
*	Pearl of Power (recover 1st-level slot)
*	His full complement of 4th-level spells
Captain Andra produces a sealed leather case. "Intelligence from the Ak-Thyln 
archives. What they know about the temple's layout." She hands it to you.
THE MAP (rough sketch):
*	Upper Plaza: Collapsed columns, open to water, former public 
worship area
*	Main Sanctuary: Large chamber, double doors (possibly sealed)
*	Inner Sanctum: Behind the sanctuary-this is where the Scepter 
should be
*	Side Chambers: Purpose unknown, possibly priest quarters or storage
*	Warnings: "Structural integrity questionable," "Guardian spirits 
reported," "Strong magical wards confirmed"
Captain Andra watches you review the information. "My crew will maintain 
position here. Signal flares if you need emergency extraction-red for trouble, 
green for success. If you send up black..." She pauses. "Black means you're not 
coming back. We'll know to leave."
The water looks calm. Deceptively so.
What's your approach?
1.	Descend as a group, stay together for safety
2.	Johannes scouts ahead using invisibility (One with Shadows), 
reports back
3.	Send Cyrus down first to assess spiritual/divine elements before 
committing
4.	Something else?
And do you want to buff before descending (Armor of Agathys, Hex 
prepared, etc.), or save spell slots until you know what you're dealing with?
Save slots, but have water breathing cast on Kessa, so they can follow me after 
I scout around first. Wait at around 80 feet down?
Dec 9
DESCENT TO THE TEMPLE
Cyrus nods and begins the ritual casting of Water Breathing. It takes ten 
minutes, his hands moving through precise gestures as divine energy 
coalesces. When he touches Kessa's shoulder, she gasps slightly-then grins.
"That's... weird. Good weird, but weird." She inhales deeply, testing the magic. 
"Okay, I can work with this."
"The spell lasts eight hours," Cyrus confirms. "More than sufficient for the 
operation."
You give final instructions: "I'll scout ahead using the cloak. Give me a twenty-
minute window-if I'm not back by then, assume something's wrong and be 
ready to adapt. Stay at eighty feet, keep watch for my signal."
Kessa checks her daggers one more time. "Eighty feet. Twenty minutes. Got 
it."
Cyrus clasps your shoulder briefly. "Mishakal's grace go with you, my friend."
 
THE DESCENT
You step off the Stormbreaker's rail and plunge into the clear blue water. The 
Cloak of Manta Ray activates instantly-you feel your body streamline, your 
breathing shift to drawing oxygen from the water itself. It's effortless, natural.
60 feet down: The sunlight is still strong here, but dimming. Schools of fish 
scatter at your approach. The water is surprisingly clear-visibility is good, 
maybe 60-70 feet in all directions.
80 feet down: The light has faded to twilight blue. You pause, looking up-
Kessa and Cyrus are visible as dark shapes against the brighter water above, 
treading water and waiting. Kessa waves. You wave back, then continue.
100 feet down: The twilight deepens. The water is cooler here. Your Cloak 
maintains comfortable temperature and breathing, but you feel the pressure of 
the depth psychologically if not physically.
120 feet down: The temple emerges from the gloom below you.
 
THE SUNKEN TEMPLE - FIRST SIGHT
It's more intact than you expected.
The structure is built from white marble-now stained with algae and 
encrusted with barnacles, but still recognizable as architecture. It must have 
been beautiful once. The roof has collapsed in places, letting water flow freely 
through the interior, but the main walls still stand.
What you see:
The Upper Plaza:
*	Broad stone platform, roughly 80 feet across
*	Collapsed columns forming a rough perimeter-some still upright, most 
fallen
*	A central pathway leads toward the main doors
*	Scattered debris: broken statues, overturned braziers, fallen stonework
*	Seaweed sways in the gentle current
*	Small fish dart between the ruins
The Main Doors:
*	Massive bronze doors, green with verdigris
*	Ornate reliefs showing storms, waves, ships
*	The doors are closed, but one hangs slightly askew on its hinges
*	Faint magical glow around the frame-wards, possibly
Movement: You immediately notice three shapes patrolling the plaza. 
They're humanoid but wrong-drowned ones, by the look of them. Undead 
sailors or priests, bloated and pale, drifting through the water with unnatural 
grace. They move in a pattern, circling the temple entrance.
Detail check (Perception): The drowned ones are armed-rusty weapons, 
but still dangerous. They don't seem particularly alert, but they're definitely on 
patrol. Corporeal undead, vulnerable to Cyrus's Turn Undead ability when he 
gets down here.
Side structures: To the left and right of the main temple, you spot smaller 
buildings-partially collapsed, but with openings. Possibly side entrances, or 
storage chambers. Darker, less visible.
The water here: Colder. The current is gentle but persistent, coming from 
the northwest. You can feel... something. Not quite magical, but present. This 
place still has power in it.
 
YOUR OPTIONS:
1.	Continue scouting the perimeter - Check those side structures, get 
a full picture
2.	Approach the main doors - Test the wards, see if you can get inside
3.	Observe the drowned ones - Watch their patrol pattern, gather 
intelligence
4.	Return to Kessa and Cyrus now - You have basic layout; bring them 
down for the assault
5.	Something else?
Current status:
*	You're at 120 feet depth, near the plaza edge
*	The drowned ones haven't noticed you yet
*	You have about 15 minutes left on your 20-minute window
*	Your invisibility (One with Shadows) won't work underwater-there's no 
darkness deep enough, just dim light
*	You're not attuned to the Trident of Warning yet, so you have normal 
initiative
What's your move?
I should be. I spent downtime training with it; I believed that included 
attunement.
Dec 9

Corrected status:
*	Trident of Warning (attuned): +1 weapon, advantage on initiative,

*	You have the trident in hand as you survey the temple
The weapon feels comfortable in your grip after your training sessions. Theros 
drilled you on underwater combat techniques-the resistance of water, the 
different angles of attack, how to use the current rather than fight it.
 
With the corrected information, you're at the plaza edge observing three 
drowned ones patrolling the main entrance.

Scout the full perimeter, especially looking for inconspicuous entry points that 
wouldn't trigger the Drowned Ones.
Dec 9
PERIMETER RECONNAISSANCE
You grip the Trident of Warning and begin a slow, careful circuit of the temple 
complex, staying low and using the scattered debris for cover. Your swimming 
is smooth and efficient thanks to the Cloak-60 feet per round, silent and 
streamlined.
 
EASTERN SIDE STRUCTURE
You approach the first side building cautiously. It's smaller than the main 
temple-maybe a priest's quarters or preparation chamber.
What you find:
*	The roof has partially collapsed, creating a large opening
*	Interior is filled with silt and debris
*	A doorway connects to the main temple-but it's blocked by rubble
*	No movement, no guards
*	Several clay vessels scattered inside, broken and empty
*	Not a viable entry point unless you want to spend significant time 
clearing rubble
You note it and continue.
 
SOUTHERN PERIMETER (Rear of Temple)
Moving around the back, the terrain slopes downward slightly. The temple's 
rear wall is more intact than you expected.
What you find:
*	A small service entrance-wooden door, mostly rotted away, leaving a 
4-foot gap
*	This leads into what looks like a storage or preparation area
*	The opening is partially obscured by fallen stonework and heavy kelp 
growth
*	No drowned ones visible back here-they're focused on the main 
plaza
*	You can see into the interior: a narrow corridor, some amphora and 
storage jars, dim but navigable
*	The corridor appears to lead toward the main sanctuary, bypassing the 
warded front doors
This looks promising. Concealed, unguarded, avoids the main entrance 
entirely.
But you continue your circuit to get the full picture.
 
WESTERN SIDE STRUCTURE
The western building is in worse shape-more collapsed than the eastern one.
What you find:
*	Mostly rubble
*	One wall still standing, but the interior is completely exposed
*	You can see straight through to the main temple's interior wall
*	That wall has a large crack-maybe 2 feet wide, running floor to 
ceiling
*	Could potentially squeeze through, but it would put you directly into the 
main sanctuary
*	One drowned one drifts past the crack occasionally-you see it 
through the gap, patrolling inside
*	Higher risk, but more direct access to the sanctuary
 
NORTHERN PERIMETER (Front Plaza - from distance)
You circle wide around the front, staying at the edge of visibility.
What you observe:
*	The three drowned ones patrol in a predictable pattern
*	They complete a full circuit of the plaza every 3-4 minutes
*	They never all face the same direction simultaneously-always 
overlapping coverage
*	The main doors' magical glow is definitely a ward-you can see it 
more clearly now, a faint blue-green shimmer
*	Approaching the main entrance without dealing with the guards would 
be risky
*	There's a large statue toppled near the doors-appears to be Zeboim 
herself, broken but recognizable
 
ASSESSMENT COMPLETE
You've circled the entire temple. Time check: about 12 minutes elapsed. 
You have 8 minutes before Kessa and Cyrus start worrying.
Entry Options:
1.	Southern service entrance (RECOMMENDED)
*	Concealed, unguarded
*	Bypasses front door wards
*	Leads to storage area, then presumably toward sanctuary
*	Safest infiltration route
2.	Western crack in wall
*	Direct access to main sanctuary
*	Risky-drowned one patrols nearby
*	Would put you immediately into potentially hostile space
*	Fast but dangerous
3.	Main doors
*	Would trigger wards (unknown effect)
*	Three drowned ones to deal with
*	Most direct route to sanctum
*	Could bring full party, fight through
4.	Eastern blocked entrance
*	Requires significant time clearing rubble
*	Would make noise underwater (vibrations)
*	Not practical for stealth approach
Additional observations:
*	The temple interior appears to be flooded but structurally sound-
walls mostly intact

*	Water temperature near the temple is noticeably colder-maybe 5-10

What do you do?
1.	Return to Kessa and Cyrus now with this intelligence

4.	Test the main door wards somehow (carefully)
5.	Something else?
You have about 8 minutes before your window closes.
Arcana check re: Zeboim. What do we know about the goddess's

Dec 9
KNOWLEDGE: ZEBOIM
You pause near the fallen statue, studying the broken features of the goddess. 
Even shattered and encrusted with barnacles, there's something fierce about 
her expression-wild, untamed.
Arcana Check (INT +3): 16
Your knowledge of divine entities and religious lore comes together:
 
ZEBOIM - THE SEA QUEEN
Domain & Nature:
*	Goddess of storms, tempests, the sea, and strife
*	Chaotic Neutral alignment-temperamental and unpredictable
*	Sister to Chislev (nature), daughter of Takhisis (though she rejected her 
mother's evil)
*	Known as "The Darkling Sea" and "The Dragon Turtle"
Temperament:
*	Mercurial and passionate-capable of both devastating fury and 
unexpected mercy
*	Rewards those who respect the sea's power but destroys those who 
show arrogance
*	Fiercely protective of her domain and her sacred items
*	Not evil, but dangerous-like the sea itself
*	Values strength, courage, and proper tribute
Her Priests:
*	Often sailors, storm-callers, coastal defenders
*	Conducted rituals involving offerings to calm or invoke storms
*	The temple being sealed before the Cataclysm suggests her 
priests knew and tried to preserve what was sacred
Critical Insight: Zeboim would likely view the Scepter's removal based 
on intent and necessity:
She would APPROVE if:
*	You show proper respect for her power
*	You need the Scepter for a worthy cause (defending against tyranny, 
protecting the innocent)
*	You acknowledge her authority and make an offering or tribute
*	You demonstrate courage and strength in claiming it
She would be FURIOUS if:
*	You show arrogance or entitlement
*	You steal the Scepter for selfish gain or power
*	You desecrate her temple
*	You show cowardice or disrespect
The Dragon Army Connection: The fact that the Dragon Army wants the 
Scepter is telling. Highlord Lucien likely plans to use it as a weapon of 
conquest-storm magic to destroy fleets, devastate coastlines, demonstrate 
power. This would be an abuse of Zeboim's gift, using her sacred artifact for 
tyranny.
Your mission, by contrast: You intend to use the Scepter to stop the 
Dragon Army fleet-to prevent invasion, protect the innocent, and preserve 
freedom. This is much more aligned with proper use of the goddess's power.
 
PRACTICAL IMPLICATIONS
What this means for your mission:
1.	Offering/Tribute: It would be wise to leave something of value when 
you take the Scepter. Not payment-tribute. Recognition of her 
authority. (Coins, a weapon, something precious to you personally)
2.	Respectful approach: Treat the temple with reverence, not as a 
dungeon to loot. You're not thieves-you're petitioners seeking aid 
against tyranny.
3.	The wards: Likely keyed to intent. Someone approaching with greed 
or arrogance might trigger hostile response. Someone approaching with 
respect and legitimate need might find easier passage.
4.	The drowned ones: Possibly her guardians, but they're undead-
corrupted versions of her priests. Zeboim wouldn't approve of undead in 
her temple. They might be a side effect of the Cataclysm, not her 
design.
5.	Stating your purpose: If you encounter any intact divine magic or 
spiritual presence, clearly state why you're here. "We seek the 
Scepter to stop those who would abuse your power for conquest."
Cyrus's role: As a cleric, he could potentially petition Zeboim directly or 
at least make proper observances. Mishakal and Zeboim aren't enemies-both 
are gods of Krynn, and Cyrus could frame this as one divine cause supporting 
another.
 
YOUR ASSESSMENT
Standing before the broken statue, you feel reasonably confident that Zeboim 
would approve of stopping the Dragon Army. The Highlord wants to 
abuse her power; you want to use it properly to defend freedom.
But the goddess is chaotic and unpredictable. Even with good intentions, 
you need to show proper respect. No arrogance, no entitlement-petition, not 
theft.
Time remaining: ~6 minutes before your window closes.
What do you do?
1.	Return to Kessa and Cyrus with full intelligence and theological 
assessment
2.	Quickly investigate the southern service entrance to confirm it's 
viable (2-3 minutes)
3.	Leave a small tribute at the statue now as a gesture before 
entering (what would you offer?)
4.	Something else?
3, then 2. What do I have of magical value that isn't immediately critical for 
mission success?
Dec 9
CHOOSING A TRIBUTE
You float before the broken statue, mentally reviewing your inventory for 
something appropriate.
Your magical items:
Currently Attuned (NOT candidates - you need these):
*	Ring of Mind Shielding (essential protection from patron)
*	Amulet of Health (keeps you alive, CON 19)
*	Trident of Warning (your primary weapon for this mission)
Equipped but not attuned:
*	Cloak of Manta Ray (absolutely critical - you're underwater)
*	Studded Leather Armor (your only armor)
*	Sending Stone (communication with Laurana/Haven)
Consumables (probably not appropriate tribute):
*	Potions (you'll likely need these)
*	Aboleth Mucus (weird, not valuable as tribute)
*	Scrolls (emergency escape items)
Items in your pack:
*	Ring of Water Walking (not attuned, party shared item)
*	Black Diamond (2,000 gp value, intended for eventual sale)
Weapons:
*	Trident of Warning (in use)
*	You likely have a backup mundane weapon?
 
THE DECISION
The Ring of Water Walking is the most logical choice:
Why it's appropriate:
*	Magical item of significant value (~1,500+ gp worth)
*	Thematically perfect - it's a water/sea-related magic item being 
offered to the goddess of the sea
*	Not currently needed (you're underwater, it does nothing here)
*	It's a party shared item, not personally attuned, so losing it won't cripple 
you
*	Shows genuine sacrifice - you're giving up something valuable, not just 
token coins
The symbolism: "We walk upon your waters by your grace, Lady of Storms. 
We return this gift to your domain and ask your blessing for our cause."
 
THE OFFERING
You swim to the broken statue's base, where the face of Zeboim lies half-
buried in silt, her stone eyes staring upward. You draw out the Ring of Water 
Walking - it gleams even in the dim light, the enchantment still active.
You place it carefully in her stone palm, clearly visible.
Then you speak-the words bubble through the water, but you mean them:
"Zeboim, Lady of Storms, Mistress of the Deeps-we come seeking 
your Scepter, not for conquest or glory, but to stop those who 
would abuse your power. The Dragon Army would use your gift to 
enslave the free peoples of Krynn. We ask your blessing to prevent 
this desecration."
You pause, then add:
"This ring is our tribute-given freely, in respect for your domain. 
May our cause prove worthy."
 
RESPONSE:
The water around the statue seems to... shift. Not violently, but noticeably. 
The current swirls around your offering, and for just a moment, you feel the 
temperature drop sharply-then warm slightly, like the sea deciding whether 
to welcome or reject you.
The ring remains where you placed it, but you sense... acknowledgment. 
Not approval or disapproval yet, but awareness. Something in this place 
knows you're here, knows what you've said, knows your intent.
The drowned ones in the plaza above don't react. Whatever just happened was 
subtle, spiritual rather than physical.
You've made your offering. Whether Zeboim will help, hinder, or remain 
neutral remains to be seen-but you've shown proper respect.
 
INVESTIGATING THE SOUTHERN SERVICE ENTRANCE
Time remaining: ~4 minutes
You move quickly to the rear of the temple, to the rotted service door with the 
kelp-shrouded opening.
You peer inside more carefully now:
The Storage Chamber:
*	About 20 feet deep, 15 feet wide
*	Multiple amphora and storage jars lining the walls-most intact, 
surprisingly
*	Shelves collapsed in places, but the space is navigable
*	Heavy silt on the floor (undisturbed for centuries)
*	A narrow corridor leads north toward the main sanctuary-maybe 4 
feet wide, decent height
*	No movement, no guardians visible
*	The corridor has a slight curve to it, preventing you from seeing all the 
way through
Checking more carefully:
*	The doorway itself is 4 feet tall/wide-easy passage
*	No wards visible (unlike the main doors)
*	The kelp provides natural concealment from outside observers
*	Scattered debris near the entrance could be moved aside quietly
One concern: The silt on the floor is thick. Moving through here will disturb 
it, creating clouds of sediment. That's unavoidable, but it's not a huge problem 
if you're careful-the current will slowly disperse it.
Assessment: This is definitely your best entry point. Concealed, unguarded, 
leads toward the interior, avoids the front door wards entirely.
 
Time check: ~2 minutes remaining
You should return to Kessa and Cyrus before they start worrying.
Heading back up:
You ascend smoothly, the Cloak making the 120-foot rise effortless. At 80 feet, 
you spot them immediately-Kessa treading water, Cyrus floating nearby 
using his Amulet's swim ability. They both turn as you approach.
Kessa's relief is obvious. "Right on time. What did you find?"
 
BRIEFING YOUR TEAM:
What do you tell them? Full layout, entry point recommendation, the offering 
to Zeboim, the drowned ones?
And what's your plan:
1.	Enter via southern service entrance (all three together, stealth

2.	Different approach?
3.	Any specific instructions for Kessa and Cyrus?
Not the ring. But the mucus is a representation of our interaction with the 
Aboleth, which would likely be an enemy to any god/goddess. I would explain

Dec 9
A BETTER TRIBUTE
You're absolutely right. You pause, reconsidering. The ring is valuable, yes, but 
impersonal. The aboleth mucus, though...
You withdraw the vial from your waterproof pouch. The thick, opalescent 
substance swirls inside-a trophy from Khû'leth the Deep One, the ancient 
aboleth whose attempted invasion you crushed utterly.
Swimming back to the broken statue, you hold the vial before Zeboim's stone 
face.
Your offering:
"Zeboim, Lady of Storms, Mistress of the Deeps-this is the essence 
of Khû'leth, an aboleth who sought to enslave coastal peoples and 
bend the sea itself to his alien will. He would have violated the 
natural order, imposed his foul tyranny on those who live by your 
waters."
You place the vial carefully in her stone palm.
"We destroyed him and his army. Five hundred sahuagin, all 
crushed in a single strike. His brain scattered, his power broken, 
his slaves freed. This mucus is proof of our victory-proof that we 
stand against those who would corrupt your domain with slavery 
and mind control."
You meet the statue's sightless gaze.
"Now the Dragon Army seeks your Scepter to enslave others, to 
abuse your power for conquest. We ask your blessing to stop them, 
as we stopped the aboleth. We fight for freedom-in all its forms, 
upon all waters."
 
RESPONSE
The water around the statue surges.
Not violently, but powerfully-a sudden current that swirls around you, 
around the vial, around the broken face of the goddess. The temperature 
plunges ice-cold for three heartbeats, then warms to almost pleasant.
The vial remains in the statue's palm, but the mucus inside seems 
to... dissolve. Not physically-you can still see it-but something about it 
changes. Becomes more translucent. Accepted.
And then you feel it: approval.
Not words, not a voice, but a sensation like the moment before a storm 
breaks-that electric tension in the air, that promise of wild power about to be 
unleashed. The sea itself seems to acknowledge you.
You have pleased Zeboim.
Your enemy was her enemy-aboleths are antithetical to the natural chaos of 
the sea, imposing rigid mental slavery where there should be freedom and wild 
power. And you offered proof of your victory, not mere gold or trinkets.
The drowned ones in the plaza above... you glance up. They've stopped 
moving. All three are perfectly still, facing away from the temple entrance, 
looking outward as if watching for external threats.
They're not attacking. They're... guarding for you now?
The path is clear.
 
RETURNING TO YOUR TEAM
You ascend swiftly, the Cloak propelling you effortlessly through the water. At 
80 feet, Kessa and Cyrus turn as you approach.
Kessa's relief is obvious. "Right on time. What did you find?"
You quickly brief them:
"The temple's more intact than expected. Three drowned ones were 
patrolling the main entrance, but I made an offering to Zeboim-
the aboleth mucus. Told her we stopped Khû'leth from enslaving 
her domain, and that we're here to stop the Dragon Army from 
abusing her Scepter the same way."
Cyrus's eyes widen. "You... petitioned the goddess directly? And 
she answered?"
"She approved. The drowned ones have stopped patrolling-they're 
facing outward now, like they're guarding the temple from external 
threats instead of guarding it from us."
Kessa grins. "So we just got divine clearance for a heist. I love it."
"There's a service entrance at the rear of the temple-unguarded, 
no wards, leads to a storage area and then toward the main 
sanctuary. That's our way in. The main doors have wards on them, 
and even with Zeboim's blessing, I'd rather not test them if we 
don't have to."
Cyrus nods thoughtfully. "A wise choice. If the goddess has granted us 
passage, we should still show proper caution and respect. We are petitioners, 
not conquerors."
Your briefing continues:
*	Temple layout (plaza, main sanctuary, inner sanctum)
*	Southern service entrance (concealed, 4-foot opening, kelp-shrouded)
*	Interior likely flooded but structurally sound
*	Magical presence strongest near main doors
*	Side structures mostly collapsed/blocked
Kessa checks her daggers. "So we go in quiet, through the back, show proper 
respect, find the Scepter, and get out. Simple."
Cyrus adjusts his holy symbol. "And if we encounter guardians inside?"
 
Good question. What's your approach?
1.	Full stealth - Avoid all contact if possible, treat this as sacred ground
2.	Prepared for combat - Cyrus can Turn Undead if needed, but prefer 
talking first
3.	Diplomatic - Announce yourselves as Zeboim's petitioners, speak to 
any guardians
4.	Something else?
And marching order for the descent and entry?
*	Johannes (Trident of Warning gives party advantage on initiative, can't 
be surprised)
*	Kessa (stealth expert, perception, trap-finding)
*	Cyrus (support, healing, divine magic)
Or different arrangement?
3 if the opposition is something that can be reasoned with, 1 if it is mindless 
or elemental.
Dec 9
FINAL PREPARATIONS
"If we encounter anything that can be reasoned with-guardians, spirits, even 
intelligent undead-we speak first," you say. "We're here with Zeboim's 
blessing, not as thieves. But if it's mindless or elemental, we stay quiet and 
avoid it entirely. No unnecessary conflict in a goddess's temple."
Cyrus nods approvingly. "A balanced approach. Wisdom and respect in equal 
measure."
Kessa shrugs. "I can work with that. Though if something does attack, I'm not 
holding back."
"Fair enough. Marching order: I'll take point with the Trident-we can't be 
surprised while I'm conscious. Kessa, stay close behind me for trap-spotting 
and stealth. Cyrus, rear guard with support and healing ready."
"Understood," Cyrus confirms.
"One more thing," you add. "The water inside will be dark-possibly 
no light at all in the inner chambers. I can see in magical darkness, 
but you two will need light sources. Cyrus, can you provide that 
without alerting everything in the temple?"
Cyrus considers. "I can cast Light on a small object-a coin, a stone-and 
cover it when stealth is needed. Or I can use my more subtle spells if 
necessary. The choice is yours."
Kessa pats her gear. "I've got a hooded lantern if we need mundane light. 
Waterproof, adjustable shutter."
 
THE DESCENT - TOGETHER
The three of you descend in formation. The water grows darker, colder, more 
oppressive with each passing moment. At 100 feet, Kessa glances at you, her 
expression serious but calm. At 120 feet, the temple emerges from the gloom.
What Kessa and Cyrus see:
Cyrus's reaction is reverent. He makes a sign of blessing as the structure 
comes into view. "Magnificent... even in ruin, you can feel the divine 
presence."
Kessa's more practical. "Those the drowned ones you mentioned?" She points 
toward the plaza.
You nod. The three undead are exactly as you left them-facing outward, still 
as statues, not patrolling. They don't react as you approach.
"They're... guarding for us?" Kessa sounds incredulous.
"Zeboim's will," Cyrus murmurs. "The goddess has granted us passage. 
Remarkable."
 
APPROACHING THE SERVICE ENTRANCE
You lead them around the southern perimeter, staying low and using debris 
for concealment-though with the drowned ones not actively patrolling, it 
feels almost unnecessary.
The kelp-shrouded service entrance appears exactly as you scouted it. You 
gesture: There. Our entry point.
Kessa moves forward, examining the opening with professional interest. She 
tests the rotted door frame, checks the kelp for resistance, peers into the dark 
interior. After a moment, she nods: Clear. No traps visible.
Cyrus casts Light on a small smooth stone, then immediately covers it with a 
dark cloth. "Ready when you are."
 
ENTERING THE TEMPLE
You slip through the opening first, Trident ready. The storage chamber is 
exactly as you remembered-amphora, collapsed shelves, thick silt on the 
floor. Your movement stirs up a small cloud of sediment, but the current 
slowly disperses it.
Kessa follows, moving with practiced grace. Her eyes adjust to the darkness-
or rather, Cyrus uncovers the light stone slightly, casting a dim blue-white 
glow across the chamber.
Cyrus enters last, his movements careful and respectful. He glances around 
the storage area, taking in the ancient vessels and forgotten supplies. "These 
were sealed before the Cataclysm. The priests knew what was coming..." His 
voice is soft, reverent.
The Storage Chamber - Detailed Look:
Now that you have light (dim but sufficient), you can see more:
*	The amphora contain preserved goods-oil, grain, wine. Still sealed after 
280 years.
*	Religious items on the shelves: censers, offering bowls, ritual 
implements
*	Everything is arranged with care, not hastily abandoned
*	A sense of preparation, not panic
*	The priests sealed this place deliberately, preserving what was sacred
The Northern Corridor:
Ahead, the narrow passage leads deeper into the temple. It curves slightly to 
the right, preventing you from seeing the full length. The walls are carved with 
reliefs-waves, fish, storms rendered in flowing stone.
Kessa moves to the corridor entrance, listening carefully. After a moment, she 
signals: No movement. No sounds.
 
PROCEEDING FORWARD
You advance into the corridor, Trident held ready. The passage is about 30 
feet long, curving gently. The carvings become more elaborate as you 
progress-you see Zeboim herself depicted multiple times, commanding 
storms, blessing ships, drowning the arrogant.
At the end of the corridor, you see an archway opening into a larger space 
beyond. Dim blue-green light filters through-not sunlight (you're too deep), 
but something else. Magical? Bioluminescent?
You approach cautiously and peer through the archway.
 
THE MAIN SANCTUARY - FIRST GLIMPSE
The chamber beyond is vast-maybe 60 feet across, with a high vaulted ceiling 
that's partially collapsed. Water flows freely through the space, and the source 
of the light becomes clear:
Glowing coral grows along the walls and pillars, pulsing with soft 
bioluminescence. It's beautiful, ethereal, casting shifting shadows across 
ancient mosaics on the floor.
The chamber layout:
*	Central altar: A raised platform in the middle, carved from dark stone. 
Empty now, but clearly the focal point
*	Pillars: Six massive columns supporting the vaulted ceiling-three still 
standing, three collapsed
*	Side alcoves: Small shrine spaces along the walls, most filled with 
debris
*	Northern doorway: Directly opposite your position, another 
archway-larger, more ornate, with intact double doors
*	Those doors are sealed: Heavy bronze, with glowing glyphs across 
their surface
*	That must be the Inner Sanctum-where the Scepter would be kept
Guardians?
Your Trident tingles with warning. There's something here.
You scan the chamber carefully-
THERE.
Floating near the central altar: a translucent, humanoid figure. Not quite 
solid, not quite ghost. It wears robes that ripple like water, and its face is 
serene but watchful.
A water spirit? A temple guardian? The ghost of a priest?
As you watch, it turns slowly-almost as if on patrol-and faces your direction. 
For a moment, you think it's spotted you.
But then it continues its rotation, circling the altar in a slow, deliberate 
pattern. Guarding. Waiting.
It hasn't noticed you yet.
Kessa and Cyrus have seen it too. Kessa's hand moves to her dagger 
instinctively. Cyrus holds up a hand: Wait.
 
What's your approach?
1.	Announce yourselves - Step into the sanctuary, speak clearly, 
identify as Zeboim's petitioners
2.	Cyrus leads - Have the cleric approach first, religious figure to 
(potentially) religious guardian
3.	Observe longer - Watch the spirit's pattern, assess if it's hostile or 
neutral
4.	Try to bypass - Move through the chamber stealthily, avoid interaction 
entirely
5.	Something else?
The spirit continues its slow patrol around the altar, unaware of your 
presence-for now.
Kessa has darkvision (half-elf); Cyrus got the Googles of Night for this very 
reason.
Dec 9
CORRECTED - LIGHT SOURCES
You're absolutely right. My apologies.
Corrected:
*	Kessa has darkvision 60 ft (half-elf) - she can see fine in the darkness
*	Cyrus has the Goggles of Night from the aboleth mission loot - 
darkvision 60 ft when worn
*	Johannes has Devil's Sight (see normally in magical darkness, 120 ft)
Cyrus didn't cast Light-he simply donned his goggles as you entered the

illumination, which maintains perfect stealth.
 
THE MAIN SANCTUARY - CORRECTED VIEW
The chamber is dark except for the glowing coral providing dim 
bioluminescence along the walls. To normal eyes, it would be nearly 
impossible to navigate. But between your Devil's Sight, Kessa's darkvision, and 
Cyrus's goggles, you all see clearly.
The translucent guardian spirit continues its slow patrol around the central 
altar, unaware of your presence in the shadowed archway.
With proper vision established:
You can see the entire sanctuary clearly:
*	Central altar (dark stone, currently empty)
*	Six pillars (three standing, three collapsed)
*	Side alcoves with debris
*	Northern doorway with sealed bronze doors (glowing glyphs)
*	The water spirit/guardian circling methodically
Kessa studies the spirit with professional assessment, her darkvision giving 
her clear sight. She signals: Alone. Patterned movement. Hasn't detected us.
Cyrus adjusts his goggles slightly, examining the guardian with his cleric's

corporeal. Perhaps a bound spirit-a temple warden left by the priests."
 
What's your approach?
1.	Announce yourselves - Step into the sanctuary, speak clearly,

2.	Cyrus leads - Have the cleric approach first, religious figure to

The spirit continues its patrol, and you remain undetected in the darkness.
I don't think Zeboim would resent conflict; fighting for one's interest is at the

Dec 9
OBSERVATION AND ASSESSMENT
You signal Kessa and Cyrus to hold position, settling in to watch the spirit's 
behavior. Zeboim is chaotic, yes-but not mindlessly violent. She respects 
strength, courage, and proper respect. If this guardian is her will made 
manifest, understanding its purpose matters.
You observe for several minutes, noting every detail:
 
THE GUARDIAN'S PATTERN
Movement:
*	Completes a full circuit around the altar every 90 seconds (remarkably 
precise for something supposedly chaotic)
*	Never strays more than 15 feet from the altar
*	Passes within 5 feet of the northern doorway (the Inner Sanctum 
entrance) on each rotation
*	Its path is perfectly consistent-not random patrol, but deliberate??
Behavior:
*	Doesn't investigate the side alcoves
*	Doesn't approach the archway where you entered
*	Never looks toward the collapsed sections
*	Focuses entirely on the altar and the sealed doorway beyond
Nature of the guardian: You study it more carefully with your warlock's 
understanding of magical entities:
It's translucent but stable-not flickering like a ghost, not shapeless like a 
water elemental. The robes flow with water-like motion, but the figure itself 
maintains consistent form. Humanoid features are visible: serene face, hands 
folded as if in prayer or meditation, no visible weapons.
Not aggressive. Not hunting. Not even particularly alert.
It's... waiting. Maintaining presence. Holding a post.
 
ARCANA/INSIGHT CHECK
You consider what you're seeing through multiple lenses:
As a Warlock (Arcana): This is bound magic-a spirit anchored to this 
place by divine command, not imprisonment. It's fulfilling a duty, not 
suffering a curse. The binding is seamless, willing, purposeful.
As someone who understands contracts (Insight): The spirit's 
behavior suggests specific instructions: Guard the altar. Protect the 
sanctum entrance. Maintain presence. But nothing about "attack all intruders" 
or "prevent access at all costs."
As someone recently blessed by Zeboim: You remember the sensation 
when you made your offering-that electric awareness, that acknowledgment. 
The drowned ones changed their behavior after Zeboim approved your 
petition. They stopped patrolling threats and started guarding outward.
This spirit hasn't changed behavior.
Why?
 
THE TEST
You lean close to Cyrus and Kessa, whispering barely audibly: "It's not hostile. 
It's waiting."
Cyrus nods slowly, studying the spirit through his goggles. "A test, perhaps? 
Zeboim approved our presence, but..."
"But she wants to see what we do with that approval," you finish. "She's 
chaotic-she values choice, freedom of action. Will we sneak past like thieves, 
or will we announce ourselves like petitioners?"
Kessa considers this. "Or will we attack because we can? Prove we're strong 
enough to take what we want?"
"No," Cyrus says quietly but firmly. "She values strength, yes-but 
also respect. The drowned ones guard for us because we showed proper 
reverence. This spirit..." He pauses. "This spirit guards the sanctum. The 
sacred heart of her temple. If we're truly petitioners, not thieves, we 
should ask permission to enter."
You watch the spirit complete another circuit. It shows no sign of aggression, 
no indication it would attack unprovoked. But it is between you and the Inner 
Sanctum doors.
The test becomes clear:
Zeboim wants to see if you'll:
1.	Sneak past (technically respectful but avoiding true interaction-
cowardly?)
2.	Attack preemptively (showing strength but unnecessary violence-
arrogant?)
3.	Announce yourselves (showing courage and respect-proper 
petitioner behavior?)
The goddess of storms values bold action and proper respect in equal 
measure. Sneaking seems... insufficient. Attacking seems disrespectful. 
Speaking seems right.
 
CYRUS'S ASSESSMENT
The cleric watches for another moment, then turns to you. "I believe it will 
allow us passage if we approach with proper respect. It guards the sanctum, 
yes-but from whom? From thieves and defilers. Not from those granted 
Zeboim's blessing."
He pauses. "But the spirit won't know we have that blessing unless we tell it. 
It's bound to its duty-it can't simply leave its post because the drowned ones 
changed behavior."
Kessa nods slowly. "So we announce ourselves. Let it know we're here with the 
goddess's permission. If it attacks anyway..." She touches her dagger. "Then 
we defend ourselves. But we give it the chance to stand aside peacefully."
 
Your decision?
1.	Step forward and announce yourselves - "We are petitioners, 
blessed by Zeboim. We seek the Scepter to prevent its desecration."
2.	Have Cyrus approach alone first - Cleric to spirit, divine authority 
meeting divine guardian
3.	Try to bypass after all - Maybe you're overthinking this; the spirit 
might simply ignore you
4.	Something else?
The spirit completes another circuit, passing near the sealed sanctum doors, 
then continuing its eternal vigil around the altar.
We announce our presence, and respect Zeboim's freedom to test our 
humility. Regardless of the spirit's reaction, even if it is hostile, we stand firm 
until it actually harms someone. I will move in front of the others, so I take the 
attack if it happens. It will get advantage because I will not react until blood is 
spilled.
Dec 9
ANNOUNCING PRESENCE
You step forward from the archway, moving past Kessa and Cyrus into the 
open sanctuary. Your trident is held low-not threatening, but ready. You 
position yourself clearly in front of your companions, making your body the 
barrier between them and any potential threat.
Kessa starts to move up beside you, but you gesture her back: Stay behind me.
She hesitates, clearly unhappy about letting you take point alone, but respects 
your decision.
Cyrus understands immediately. He nods solemnly and remains at your 
shoulder-close enough to heal, far enough to let you take the lead.
 
THE ANNOUNCEMENT
You raise your voice, letting it carry through the water-filled chamber. Your 
tone is respectful but firm-petitioner, not supplicant. Free person addressing 
another power, not beggar pleading for scraps.
"Guardian of Zeboim's temple-we announce ourselves."
The spirit stops mid-circuit. It turns slowly toward you, its translucent form 
rippling like disturbed water. The serene face regards you with ancient, patient 
eyes.
"I am Johannes Constantinius. With me are Kessa Darrow and 
Brother Cyrus of Mishakal. We come as petitioners, blessed by the 
Lady of Storms. We seek the Tempest Scepter-not for conquest or 
personal glory, but to stop those who would abuse your goddess's 
power."
The spirit drifts closer, moving with that same unhurried grace. It's now 20 
feet away, still approaching. You hold your ground.
"We destroyed Khû'leth the Deep One, an aboleth who sought to 
enslave the coastal peoples and corrupt the sea with his mind-
slavery. We offered proof of that victory to Zeboim herself. She 
acknowledged us. She granted us passage."
15 feet away now. The spirit's eyes-if they can be called eyes-study you with 
unreadable intensity.
You lower your trident completely, holding it at your side. Non-threatening. 
Vulnerable.
"We respect your duty, guardian. We respect your goddess's 
domain. We stand before you openly, offering you the same 
freedom Zeboim values: the freedom to choose. Test us if you must. 
We will not strike first."
 
THE SPIRIT'S RESPONSE
It's now 10 feet away. Close enough to attack if it wishes. You feel Cyrus tense 
behind you, ready to heal or intervene. Kessa's hand is on her dagger, but she's 
holding position.
The spirit raises one translucent arm-
You remain absolutely still. If this is an attack, so be it. You've stated your 
case. You've shown respect. The rest is Zeboim's will.
The arm extends toward you, palm open. Not a fist. Not a weapon.
It touches your chest-or rather, the water where your chest is. The contact 
sends a shock through you, cold and electric like lightning through water. Not 
painful, but probing. Searching.
CHA Save (your CHA is +3): Roll with advantage? No-you allowed this. 
You're not resisting.
Roll: 8 +3 = 11
The spirit's presence washes over you, through you, examining your intent, 
your truth, your purpose. You feel it reading you like Zeboim herself might-
looking past words to the core of who you are.
It sees:
*	Your curse, your bound service to a demon
*	Your military past, your unit's death
*	Your desperate search for freedom
*	Your fierce protection of the innocent
*	Your malicious compliance with your patron's demands
*	Your hatred of slavery in all its forms
*	Your willingness to sacrifice for others
The spirit sees all of it.
 
JUDGMENT
The cold presence withdraws. The spirit steps back, its hand lowering.
Then it speaks-not with a voice, but with words that form directly in your 
mind, carried by water and divine will:
"YOU SPEAK TRUTH. YOU FIGHT BONDAGE. YOU HONOR 
FREEDOM."
The spirit turns away from you, floating back toward the central altar. But 
instead of resuming its patrol, it positions itself to one side-deliberately 
clearing the path to the northern doorway and the sealed sanctum beyond.
"THE LADY OF STORMS HAS GRANTED YOU PASSAGE. I DO NOT 
OPPOSE HER WILL. ENTER THE SANCTUM. CLAIM THE 
SCEPTER. USE IT WISELY."
A pause, then one final statement:
"SHOW THE SAME COURAGE YOU SHOWED HERE. DO NOT 
WAVER WHEN THE STORM TESTS YOU."
The spirit becomes perfectly still-no longer guarding against you, but 
guarding for you, much like the drowned ones outside.
 
THE PATH IS CLEAR
Cyrus releases a breath he'd been holding. "Blessed Mishakal... Johannes, you 
just submitted yourself to divine judgment and passed."
Kessa moves up beside you, studying the spirit warily. "That was either the 
bravest or the stupidest thing I've ever watched. Probably both." She grins 
slightly. "But it worked."
You look at the northern doorway-the sealed bronze doors with their glowing 
glyphs. The Inner Sanctum lies beyond. The Tempest Scepter waits.
But the spirit's final words echo in your mind: "Do not waver when the storm 
tests you."
There's another test coming. Inside the sanctum. Something more than just 
retrieving an artifact.
 
Approaching the sealed doors:
The three of you move toward the northern archway. Up close, the doors are 
magnificent-bronze worked with reliefs of storms, lightning, crashing waves. 
The glyphs glow with soft blue-green light, clearly magical wards.
But now that you're close, you can read what the glyphs say. They're in an 
ancient dialect, but Cyrus translates:
"Enter with reverence. Speak your purpose. Prove your worth."
The doors aren't locked. They're waiting.
 
What do you do?
1.	Open the doors directly - You've been granted passage; proceed with 
confidence
2.	Speak your purpose aloud first - State why you're here before 
entering
3.	Have Cyrus perform a blessing/prayer - Religious observance 
before entering the sanctum
4.	Check for additional wards or traps - Kessa examines the doors 
first
5.	Something else?
The guardian spirit watches silently from the altar, patient and approving.
3, then 2, then wait until these two steps are acknowledged.
Dec 9
PRAYERS AND PURPOSE
You gesture to Cyrus. "Brother-this is a sacred place. We should honor it 
properly."
Cyrus nods, moving forward to stand before the bronze doors. He removes his 
holy symbol of Mishakal-the blue crystal infinity symbol-and holds it

CYRUS'S PRAYER
The cleric's voice is clear and sincere, carrying through the water-filled

"Zeboim, Lady of Storms, Mistress of the Deeps, Queen of 
Tempests-we stand before your sanctum with humble hearts and

He raises the symbol of Mishakal slightly.
"I am Brother Cyrus, servant of Mishakal the Healing Hand. 
Though we serve different aspects of the divine, we both honor the

A pause, then he continues:
"We ask your blessing as we enter your inner sanctum. We seek the
