He bows deeply, holding the position for several heartbeats.
"May Mishakal's compassion and your wild strength work together 
this day. May freedom triumph over bondage. May the storm break 
the chains of tyranny."
 
RESPONSE TO THE PRAYER
The water around the doors stirs-not violently, but noticeably. The current 
swirls in a tight spiral around the bronze surfaces, and the glyphs flare 
brighter for a moment before settling back to their steady glow.
The guardian spirit at the altar shifts slightly-you feel its approval, though it 
doesn't speak.
Cyrus lowers his holy symbol and steps back, nodding to you. "The goddess 
hears us. Proceed."
 
STATING YOUR PURPOSE
You move forward to stand directly before the doors, your hand resting on the 
bronze surface. The metal is cold even through the water, ancient and 
powerful.
You speak clearly, projecting your voice to fill the sanctum:
"Zeboim, we are Johannes Constantinius, Kessa Darrow, and 
Brother Cyrus. We seek the Tempest Scepter to stop the Dragon 
Army fleet staging at Flotsam. Fifteen warships prepare to sail 
against the free peoples of Ansalon, carrying invasion and 
conquest."
You press your palm flat against the door.
"Highlord Lucien of the Dragon Army seeks this very Scepter-not 
to honor your power, but to abuse it. To use your storms as 
weapons of tyranny. To bend your wild strength to his master's 
will. We would deny him this desecration."
Your voice hardens with conviction:
"We will use the Scepter to destroy his fleet, to break his invasion 
before it begins, to preserve the freedom of those who would 
otherwise fall to slavery. We will wield your power for one 
purpose-liberation-and then return it to your domain, our 
purpose fulfilled."
A final statement:
"We have fought aboleths and dragons. We have freed prisoners 
and broken chains. We stand before you not as conquerors or 
thieves, but as warriors of freedom seeking a weapon against 
tyranny. Judge us worthy or wanting-but know that we speak only 
truth."
 
THE SANCTUM'S RESPONSE
Silence for three heartbeats.
Then the glyphs on the doors blaze brilliant blue-white, so bright that 
even your Devil's Sight is momentarily dazzled. Kessa shields her eyes; Cyrus 
turns his head slightly but maintains his reverent stance.
The light pulses once, twice, three times-like a heartbeat, like waves crashing, 
like lightning striking.
Then the bronze doors swing open.
Not slowly, not ominously-but welcomingly. As if the sanctum itself is 
inviting you inside, acknowledging your stated purpose and granting access.
The guardian spirit's voice echoes in your mind once more:
"THE LADY HAS HEARD. THE LADY HAS JUDGED. ENTER, 
WARRIORS OF FREEDOM. FACE THE STORM."
 
THE INNER SANCTUM REVEALED
Beyond the doors lies a chamber that takes your breath away.
The sanctum is smaller than the main sanctuary-perhaps 40 feet across-
but perfectly preserved. The walls are covered in intricate mosaics showing 
Zeboim's greatest acts: storms that saved desperate sailors, tempests that 
destroyed tyrant fleets, the wild beauty of the unfettered sea.
The chamber's features:
Central Pedestal: At the room's heart stands a pedestal of dark stone, 
carved with spiraling patterns like whirlpools and hurricanes. Upon it rests-
The Tempest Scepter.
Even from the doorway, you can see it clearly: approximately three feet long, 
worked from what appears to be solidified storm cloud and lightning given 
physical form. Silver-grey metal shot through with crackling blue-white 
energy. The head is shaped like a thunderhead, with stylized lightning bolts 
extending downward. It practically hums with contained power.
The Water: The water in this chamber is different. It moves in a slow, 
circular pattern around the pedestal-a perpetual whirlpool, gentle but 
constant. The current pulls everything toward the center, then spirals upward 
along the walls before descending again.
The Ceiling: Unlike the collapsed main sanctuary, this ceiling is intact-
domed, covered in mother-of-pearl that catches and reflects light in shifting 
patterns. It almost looks like storm clouds moving overhead.
The Test: Standing between you and the pedestal, positioned in the circling 
current, are three figures.
Water Elementals.
Not small ones. Each is roughly eight feet tall, vaguely humanoid but clearly 
composed entirely of animated water. They don't appear hostile-they're 
simply there, moving with the circular current, maintaining their positions 
around the pedestal.
Guardians? A test? Both?
As you watch, they continue their slow rotation, never breaking formation, 
never approaching the pedestal or the doors. They're like the current itself 
given form and purpose.
The spirit's final words echo again: "Do not waver when the storm tests you."
 
ASSESSMENT
Kessa studies the elementals warily. "Three of them. Large. Between us and 
the Scepter." She glances at you. "Fighting or talking?"
Cyrus considers carefully. "They move with the current... they're part of the 
sanctum's defense, not separate from it. Perhaps..." He pauses. "Perhaps 
they'll test our strength. Zeboim values courage and power as much as 
respect."
You study the chamber, the elementals, the Scepter. The test is clear enough: 
can you reach the pedestal and claim the Scepter? Will you be strong enough? 
Brave enough? Worthy enough?
But the elementals aren't attacking. They're waiting. Like everything else in 
this temple, they're giving you the chance to act first.
 
What's your approach?
1.	Announce yourselves again - State your purpose to the elementals 
specifically
2.	Simply walk forward - Proceed confidently toward the pedestal, see 
if they react
3.	Prepare for combat - Assume they'll attack once you get close enough
4.	Study the current pattern - Look for a way to work with the 
whirlpool rather than against it
5.	Something else?
The Tempest Scepter awaits on its pedestal, humming with storm-born power. 
The water elementals circle endlessly, patient and implacable.
But even in this act, we must respect the sanctity of life. There are soldiers 
aboard these ships who are following the orders of their leaders, who may act 
out of honest loyalty to their comrades, but not out of a love of darkness or 
evil. We will seek to spare life as we can, though the lives of innocents must 
take precedence.
Dec 9
THE COMPLETE TRUTH
You pause, realizing you spoke incompletely. The elementals continue their 
patient rotation, but something in the chamber's energy feels... expectant. 
Waiting for the whole truth, not just part of it.
You step forward, speaking again to the sanctum, to Zeboim, to the test itself:
"But I must speak the complete truth-for anything less dishonors 
this sacred place."
Your voice carries across the water, sincere and resolute:
"Even in destroying this fleet, we must respect the sanctity of life. 
There are soldiers aboard those ships who follow orders given by 
their commanders, who act out of honest loyalty to their comrades 
and their homes. Not all who serve the Dragon Army do so from 
love of darkness or evil. Some are conscripts. Some are deceived. 
Some simply know no other path."
You meet the gaze of the nearest elemental-if such beings can be said to have 
gazes.
"We will use the Scepter to break their invasion, yes. But we will 
seek to spare life where we can. We will target ships, not sailors. 
We will give them the chance to surrender, to flee, to choose 
freedom over their masters' tyranny. The lives of the innocents 
they threaten must take precedence-but we will not become 
butchers ourselves."
Kessa glances at you, understanding dawning on her face. Cyrus nods slowly, 
his expression approving.
You continue:
"Zeboim values freedom-true freedom, which includes the 
freedom to make mistakes, to serve the wrong masters, to be 
redeemed. We will not abuse your power by using it to slaughter 
those who might yet choose a better path. We will use the storm to 
break chains, not to forge new ones in blood."
A final statement, spoken with absolute conviction:
"If that makes us unworthy of the Scepter, so be it. But we will not 
lie to gain your favor. This is who we are. This is how we will wield 
your power."
 
THE SANCTUM'S TRUE RESPONSE
The water in the chamber surges.
The gentle whirlpool becomes a powerful current, spinning faster, pulling 
everything toward the center with tremendous force. The three water 
elementals are caught in it, spiraling inward-
And then they dissolve.
Not destroyed-released. They flow back into the current, becoming part of 
the sanctum's waters again, their purpose fulfilled. They were never meant to 
fight you. They were meant to bear witness.
The current slows, gentles, returns to its perpetual rotation.
And the Tempest Scepter on its pedestal flares brilliant white-blue, 
lightning crackling across its surface in approval.
A presence fills the chamber-not the guardian spirit, not the elementals, but 
something vast and wild and approving. Zeboim herself, perhaps, or simply 
her will made manifest in this sacred space.
Words form in your mind, in all three of your minds simultaneously, spoken in 
the voice of storm and sea:
"YOU UNDERSTAND. POWER WITHOUT WISDOM IS TYRANNY. 
STRENGTH WITHOUT MERCY IS CRUELTY. FREEDOM 
WITHOUT RESPONSIBILITY IS CHAOS."
The presence intensifies:
"YOU WOULD WIELD MY STORM NOT FOR CONQUEST, BUT FOR 
LIBERATION. YOU WOULD SPARE EVEN YOUR ENEMIES 
WHERE YOU CAN. YOU SPEAK TRUTH EVEN WHEN IT MIGHT 
COST YOU THE PRIZE YOU SEEK."
A pause, like the stillness before thunder:
"YOU ARE WORTHY."
 
THE GIFT
The current around the pedestal parts, creating a clear path directly to the 
Scepter. The water itself seems to guide you forward, gentle pressure at your 
back propelling you toward the artifact.
You swim forward, Kessa and Cyrus following close behind. The three of you 
approach the pedestal together.
Up close, the Tempest Scepter is even more magnificent. It's not metal-it's 
solidified storm essence, lightning frozen into semi-physical form, cloud given 
weight and substance. Power radiates from it in waves, making your skin 
tingle even through the water.
You reach out slowly, respectfully-
Your hand closes around the shaft.
POWER floods through you.
Not overwhelming, not crushing-but immense. You feel the potential 
contained in this artifact: storms that could level cities, lightning that could 
shatter mountains, tempests that could sink entire fleets. The raw, untamed 
power of nature itself, focused and directed through divine will.
But you also feel control. This isn't wild magic that might escape your grasp. 
This is a tool, a weapon, a gift freely given by a goddess who trusts you to wield 
it properly.
The Scepter accepts you. You are its bearer now, its wielder, its master for as 
long as your purpose aligns with Zeboim's values.
 
THE SCEPTER'S PROPERTIES
As you hold it, knowledge flows into your mind-not words, 
but understanding:
Tempest Scepter (Artifact - requires attunement)
*	Functions as a +2 quarterstaff in melee
*	Call Lightning (at will): As the 3rd-level spell, no concentration 
required, CL 9, DC 17
*	Control Weather (1/day): As the 8th-level spell, but limited to 
storm/tempest effects
*	Storm's Fury (1/day): Summon a massive storm in a 1-mile radius-
devastating winds, lightning, torrential rain. Essentially weaponized 
weather.
*	Resistance to lightning and thunder damage
*	Water breathing (constant, for bearer and allies within 30 feet)
But there's also a responsibility:
*	The Scepter judges its wielder continuously
*	Using it for tyranny, conquest, or needless cruelty will cause it to reject 
you violently
*	Using it to defend freedom, break chains, or protect the innocent 
strengthens the bond
*	When your stated purpose is fulfilled, you must return it to Zeboim's 
domain or find a worthy successor
 
ATTUNEMENT DECISION
You're currently attuned to:
1.	Ring of Mind Shielding (essential - patron protection)
2.	Amulet of Health (CON 19, substantial HP boost)
3.	Trident of Warning (advantage on initiative, no surprise)
The Tempest Scepter requires attunement. You'll need to un-attune 
from one item.
Recommendation: Un-attune from the Trident of Warning for now. The 
Scepter is far more powerful and directly mission-critical. You can re-attune to 
the Trident after you've used the Scepter and returned it.
Do you:
1.	Attune to the Scepter now (choose which item to un-attune from)
2.	Wait until you're back on the Stormbreaker to handle 
attunement
3.	Have someone else attune to it (though it clearly chose you)
Cyrus and Kessa watch with awe and respect. Kessa whistles softly. "That's... 
that's a weapon that could change the course of the war."
Cyrus's expression is more thoughtful. "And the responsibility that comes with 
it is equally heavy. Use it well, Johannes."
The sanctum's presence has faded to a gentle awareness. The test is complete. 
The Scepter is yours.
What do you do?
I give it to Cyrus. He was the most strongly affected by the recognition that 
calling down the storm could end the lives of hundreds of Dragon Army 
soldiers. He did not see that as a victory, but as a great loss. Whatever I said 
was a direct response to his initial reaction; he is the only one who should be 
trusted to carry it. He can attune to it at his discretion.
Dec 9
THE TRUE WORTHY BEARER
You hold the Scepter for a long moment, feeling its power thrumming through 
your hands. Then you turn to Cyrus.
The cleric looks at you questioningly, but you see understanding beginning to 
dawn in his eyes.
"Brother Cyrus," you say formally, "this is not mine to wield."
You extend the Tempest Scepter toward him.
"When we first discussed this mission-destroying the Dragon 
Army fleet-you were troubled. Not by the necessity of it, but by the 
cost. You saw beyond the tactical victory to the hundreds of lives 
that would be lost. Soldiers following orders. Young men far from 
home. People who might yet choose a different path."
Cyrus starts to protest: "Johannes, the goddess chose-"
You cut him off gently but firmly:
"She tested me, yes. But what I said-the recognition that we must 
spare life where we can, that not all who serve darkness do so 
willingly, that we must balance justice with mercy-those weren't 
my thoughts alone. They were yours. You spoke them first, when 
we planned this operation. I only gave voice to what you taught 
me."
You press the Scepter into his hands.
"You are a healer, Cyrus. A servant of Mishakal. You understand 
the sanctity of life better than any of us. If anyone can wield a 
weapon of such devastating power while still honoring that 
sanctity, it's you. Not me-I'm bound to a demon and fight every 
day not to become what my curse wants me to be. Not Kessa-she's 
a killer, skilled and necessary, but she strikes first and asks 
questions later."
Kessa doesn't argue. She nods slowly, accepting the truth of it.
"You, Brother Cyrus, will use this power with wisdom. You'll call 
the storm when you must, but you'll grieve the necessity. You'll give 
them every chance to surrender. You'll remember that each life 
lost is a tragedy, not just a statistic. That's why you should bear this 
burden."
 
CYRUS'S RESPONSE
The cleric holds the Scepter, and his hands tremble slightly-not from its 
weight, but from the magnitude of what you're giving him.
"Johannes..." His voice is thick with emotion. "This is... I don't know if I'm 
worthy of-"
"That's exactly why you are," you interrupt. "Anyone who thinks 
they're unworthy of such power is precisely the person who should 
wield it. Pride and certainty are dangerous. Humility and doubt 
keep us honest."
Cyrus looks down at the Scepter, then back at you. Tears mix with the 
seawater on his face-you can see them, even here in the depths.
"You honor me beyond measure," he says quietly. "And you're right-I was 
troubled. I am troubled. The thought of calling lightning down on ships full of 
men who might be conscripts, who might have families, who might simply be 
following orders..." He closes his eyes. "It weighs on me."
"Good," you say simply. "Let it weigh on you. Let it remind you to use this 
power sparingly, carefully, only when there's no other way. That weight is 
what makes you worthy."
 
THE SANCTUM'S JUDGMENT
The presence that had faded surges back-not angry, but approving.
The water in the chamber swirls around Cyrus, around the Scepter in his 
hands. Lightning crackles along its length, but instead of the blue-white 
energy you saw, it now glows with a softer, silvery-blue light-storm tempered 
with healing, power balanced with mercy.
Words form in your minds again:
"WISDOM. THE WARRIOR RECOGNIZES HIS LIMITS. THE 
HEALER ACCEPTS THE BURDEN. BOTH UNDERSTAND: POWER 
IS NOT POSSESSION-IT IS RESPONSIBILITY."
The presence focuses on Cyrus specifically:
"CLERIC OF MISHAKAL, YOU BEAR MY STORM. WIELD IT WITH 
THE SAME CARE YOU WIELD YOUR HEALING MAGIC. 
REMEMBER: EVERY STORM MUST END. EVERY TEMPEST MUST 
GIVE WAY TO CALM. USE MY FURY TO DEFEND FREEDOM, 
THEN LET THE WATERS BE STILL AGAIN."
A final benediction:
"YOU ARE BOTH WORTHY. THE ONE WHO SEES CLEARLY. THE 
ONE WHO ACTS RIGHTLY. GO FORTH. BREAK THE CHAINS OF 
TYRANNY. SPARE WHAT YOU CAN. DESTROY WHAT YOU 
MUST."
The presence fades, leaving only the gentle current and the three of you 
standing in the sanctum.
 
AFTERMATH
Kessa breaks the silence: "Well. That was... intense." She looks between you 
and Cyrus. "You really just gave away an artifact of divine power because you 
thought someone else should have it."
You shrug. "I gave it to the person who should wield it. That's not giving it 
away-that's putting it where it belongs."
Cyrus grips the Scepter with both hands, his expression resolute despite the 
weight of responsibility. "I will honor this trust. Both yours, Johannes, and the 
goddess's. I will use this power as it should be used-to protect, to defend, to 
free. And when our purpose is fulfilled..." He looks at the Scepter thoughtfully. 
"We'll return it. Or find the next worthy bearer."
"For now," you say practically, "we have Phase 1 complete. The 
Scepter is ours-yours. Phase 2 is rescuing Lady Sharane's 
daughter from the Dragon Army flagship. Then Phase 3: dealing 
with Highlord Lucien and his fleet."
Kessa nods, back to business. "Right. One impossible task down, two to go. 
Let's get back to the Stormbreaker and plan the next move."
 
ATTUNEMENT NOTE
Cyrus will need to attune to the Tempest Scepter during a short rest. He's 
currently attuned to:
1.	Pearl of Power (1st level spell slot recovery)
2.	Amulet of the Depths (swim speed, water breathing, cold resist, speak 
with dead)
3.	Goggles of Night (darkvision 60 ft)
He'll likely un-attune from the Goggles since the Scepter provides water 
breathing for him and nearby allies (30 ft radius), making underwater 
operations easier for everyone.
 
EXITING THE TEMPLE
The three of you turn to leave the sanctum. The bronze doors remain open, 
welcoming. The guardian spirit in the main sanctuary nods as you pass-a 
gesture of respect between equals.
The drowned ones in the plaza outside continue their outward guard, 
protecting rather than threatening.
You ascend through the clear water, the temple falling away beneath you. At 
80 feet, you can see the hull of the Stormbreaker above. At 60 feet, the 
sunlight strengthens. At 40 feet, you break into full daylight.
You surface beside the ship. Captain Andra is at the rail immediately, eyes 
wide.
"You're back! And you have-" She sees the Scepter in Cyrus's hands and her 
expression shifts to awe. "By the gods. You actually did it."
Crew members help you aboard. As you stand dripping on the deck, Cyrus still 
holding the Tempest Scepter, the Stormbreaker's sailors back away slightly-
not in fear, but in reverence. They recognize divine power when they see it.
Captain Andra approaches carefully. "Commander Constantinius. Brother 
Cyrus. What are your orders?"
 
What do you do?
1.	Proceed immediately to Phase 2 - Sail to Flotsam, begin 
reconnaissance for Elara's rescue
2.	Short rest aboard ship - Let Cyrus attune to the Scepter, recover 
resources, plan carefully
3.	Report to Admiral Kethren first - Inform Ak-Thyln command of 
your success
4.	Something else?
The sun is still high-early afternoon. You have time, but the Dragon Army 
fleet deploys in 10-12 days. Every hour counts.
Actually, with what we do, the Googles are mission-critical. The Pearl is nice, 
but it's only a 1st level spell.
Dec 9
ATTUNEMENT DECISION
You're absolutely right. Cyrus considers his options as the crew gives him 
space on the deck:
Currently attuned:
1.	Pearl of Power - Recover one 1st-level spell slot per day (useful but 
limited)
2.	Amulet of the Depths - Swim speed, water breathing, cold resistance, 
Speak with Dead 1/day (extremely valuable)
3.	Goggles of Night - Darkvision 60 ft (mission-critical for operations)
The Tempest Scepter provides water breathing for bearer and allies within 
30 feet, which overlaps with the Amulet. However, the Amulet also provides 
swim speed, cold resistance, and Speak with Dead-all valuable.
The Pearl, while nice, only recovers a single 1st-level slot. Compared to the 
divine artifact in his hands, it's clearly the least essential.
Cyrus nods to himself. "I'll un-attune from the Pearl. A single first-level spell 
slot is helpful, but not worth losing access to this." He holds up the Tempest 
Scepter. "We can always sell or gift the Pearl to someone who needs it more."
Decision made: Cyrus will attune to the Tempest Scepter and un-attune 
from the Pearl of Power during the next short rest.
 
ABOARD THE STORMBREAKER
Captain Andra awaits your orders, her crew maintaining respectful distance 
from the divine artifact.
The Stormbreaker rocks gently at anchor, the sun still high in the early 
afternoon sky. You've successfully completed Phase 1-arguably the most 
uncertain part of the operation. You have the weapon that can destroy the 
Dragon Army fleet.
Now comes Phase 2: Rescuing Elara, Lady Sharane's daughter, from the 
Dragon Army flagship in Flotsam harbor.
Current status:
*	Timeline: 10-12 days until Dragon Army fleet deploys
*	Location: Sunken Temple of Zeboim, ~40 miles from Flotsam
*	Party condition: Full HP, most spell slots available (you used no 
resources in the temple)
*	Mission progress: Phase 1 complete, Phase 2 and 3 remain
Options:
1. Proceed immediately to Flotsam
*	Sail directly to the port city
*	Begin reconnaissance for Elara's rescue
*	No rest, maintain momentum
*	Travel time: ~6-8 hours depending on winds
2. Short rest aboard ship first
*	Let Cyrus attune to the Scepter (1 hour)
*	Recover any resources, plan Phase 2 in detail
*	Sail to Flotsam afterward
*	Still arrive tonight or early tomorrow
3. Report to Admiral Kethren in Ak-Thyln
*	Inform command of your success
*	Get any updated intelligence on Flotsam/Dragon Army
*	Significant detour (adds 1-2 days)
*	Probably unnecessary
4. Anchor here and plan extensively
*	Full long rest if needed
*	Detailed planning session for Phase 2
*	Approach Flotsam fully prepared
*	Most cautious option
 
What's your call?
I'd recommend Option 2 - take a short rest to let Cyrus attune and discuss 
Phase 2 strategy, then sail to Flotsam. You'll arrive tonight under cover of 
darkness, perfect for reconnaissance. You don't need to report back to Ak-
Thyln yet-you have the Scepter and a mission to complete.
What do you want to do?
We keep the Pearl. The expectation is that our possession of the Scepter is 
temporary. Once it is returned, it would make sense to re-attune to the Pearl. 
Actually, let's do 1. Why wait when the ship can be travelling while we rest, 
etc.?
Dec 9
SETTING SAIL FOR FLOTSAM
You're right-no reason to waste time anchored when you can rest while 
traveling.
"Captain Andra," you call out. "Set course for Flotsam. We'll rest and plan en 
route."
She nods crisply. "Aye, Commander. We'll make good time with the current 
winds. Should reach Flotsam harbor by nightfall, maybe earlier." She turns to 
her crew. "Weigh anchor! Prepare to make sail! Helmsman, set course 
northeast by east!"
The Stormbreaker comes alive with activity. Sailors scramble up the rigging, 
canvas unfurls, and within minutes the ship is cutting through the waves 
toward Flotsam.
 
SHORT REST EN ROUTE
Captain Andra provides you with her cabin for privacy-a courtesy for the 
operation's command element. The three of you settle in: Cyrus sits cross-
legged with the Tempest Scepter across his lap, beginning the attunement 
process. Kessa sprawls in a chair, finally relaxing after the tension of the 
temple. You lean against the bulkhead, feeling the ship's steady rhythm.
Cyrus's Attunement (1 hour):
The cleric breathes slowly, deeply, his hands resting on the Scepter. You watch 
as the artifact's energy begins to resonate with him-lightning flickering along 
its length in time with his heartbeat, storm essence recognizing and accepting 
its new bearer.
His holy symbol of Mishakal glows faintly in response, divine energies 
intertwining: healing and tempest, mercy and fury, calm and storm. Not 
opposing forces, but complementary ones.
After an hour, Cyrus opens his eyes. They briefly flash with storm-light before 
returning to normal.
"It's done," he says quietly. "I can feel it-the power, the responsibility, the 
goddess's trust." He looks at the Scepter with something like reverence. "This 
is... humbling."
Attunement complete:
*	Cyrus: Pearl of Power, Amulet of the Depths, Tempest Scepter
*	Pearl remains for re-attunement after the Scepter is returned
 
PLANNING PHASE 2: ELARA'S RESCUE
With attunement complete and the ship making steady progress toward 
Flotsam, you spread out what intelligence you have.
What you know about the situation:
The Target: Elara
*	Daughter of Lady Sharane (resistance ally/supporter in Flotsam region)
*	Captured by Dragon Army ~2 weeks ago
*	Held aboard the flagship Tiamat's Wrath as leverage/hostage
*	Age unknown, condition unknown, exact location on ship unknown
The Location: Flotsam Harbor
*	Major port city, currently under Dragon Army control (occupied, not 
fully garrisoned)
*	Harbor contains the Dragon Army fleet: 15 warships including the 
flagship
*	Tiamat's Wrath is the command vessel-largest, most heavily guarded
*	Fleet is preparing to deploy in 10-12 days
The Opposition: Highlord Lucien
*	Commands the fleet and occupation forces
*	High-ranking Dragon Army officer (Highlord = major commander)
*	Powerful combatant (exact capabilities unknown)
*	Based aboard Tiamat's Wrath
*	Likely has elite guards, officers, mages
Haven Intelligence Network:
*	Contact in Flotsam: "The Fishwife" (tavern owner, resistance 
sympathizer)
*	Can provide local intelligence, safe house, current disposition
*	Network has been monitoring Dragon Army movements
Your Assets:
*	Stormbreaker and Captain Andra's crew (naval support)
*	Tempest Scepter (ultimate weapon for Phase 3)
*	Your party's skills: stealth, combat, magic
*	Element of surprise (Dragon Army doesn't know you're coming)
 
STRATEGIC DISCUSSION
Kessa leans forward, studying the rough map of Flotsam harbor that Captain 
Andra provided. "Okay, so we need to get Elara off a heavily guarded flagship 
in an occupied harbor without alerting the entire Dragon Army fleet. Simple."
Her tone is dry, but you can see her mind working-she's already thinking 
through approaches.
Cyrus strokes his beard thoughtfully. "The key question is: do we attempt 
stealth, or do we use the Scepter as leverage?"
"What do you mean?" you ask.
"Well," Cyrus gestures with the Scepter, "we could sneak aboard, find Elara, 
extract her quietly. Classic infiltration. But we could 
also announce ourselves-show Lucien we have the weapon he covets, offer a 
trade: Elara for safe passage. Or threaten to destroy his fleet if he doesn't 
release her."
Kessa shakes her head. "That second option gives him time to prepare, to set 
traps, to use Elara as a shield. And it tells him we have the Scepter, which 
might make Phase 3 harder."
"True," Cyrus concedes. "But stealth has its own risks. If we're caught aboard 
the flagship, we're trapped in the heart of enemy forces with no easy escape."
 
APPROACH OPTIONS
Option A: Full Stealth Infiltration
*	Reconnaissance first via "The Fishwife" contact
*	Nighttime approach (you have Devil's Sight, Kessa has darkvision, Cyrus 
has Goggles)
*	Board Tiamat's Wrath covertly
*	Locate Elara, extract her, escape before alarm raised
*	Pros: Maintains surprise for Phase 3, clean operation if successful
*	Cons: High risk if discovered, unknown ship layout, Elara's location 
uncertain
Option B: Negotiation/Intimidation
*	Approach openly with Scepter
*	Demand Elara's release, threaten fleet destruction
*	Force Lucien to choose between his hostage and his mission
*	Pros: Direct, forces enemy response, might avoid combat entirely
*	Cons: Reveals Scepter possession, gives enemy time to prepare, might 
trigger hostage execution
Option C: Distraction + Extraction
*	Create major diversion elsewhere in harbor (fire, explosion, false attack)
*	Dragon Army responds to threat
*	Infiltrate flagship while defenses are weakened/distracted
*	Pros: Reduces guards on flagship, creates confusion
*	Cons: Requires precise timing, might harm innocents, still requires 
successful infiltration
Option D: Intelligence First
*	Make contact with "The Fishwife" immediately upon arrival
*	Gather detailed information before committing to approach
*	Adapt plan based on current situation
*	Pros: Most informed decision, flexible response
*	Cons: Takes time, relies on local assets
Option E: Something else?
 
Kessa waits for your input. "You're the tactical mind here, Johannes. What's 
your read?"
Cyrus adds: "And remember-we also need to consider Phase 3. How we 
extract Elara may impact our ability to destroy the fleet afterward. If we reveal 
the Scepter now, they'll be watching for its use later."
The Stormbreaker cuts through the waves, carrying you steadily toward 
Flotsam. You have maybe 4-5 hours before you arrive-time to plan, but not 
unlimited time.
What's your approach?
Let's see if we can find someone intimately familiar with the design of Tiamat's 
Wrath, or similar ships, who can help us understand exactly where we might 
expect to find Elara, and so we can plan how best to enter the ship and exit it 
without alarm.
Dec 9
SEEKING EXPERT KNOWLEDGE
"Before we commit to any approach," you say, "we need better intelligence. 
Specifically, we need someone who knows the layout of Tiamat's Wrath-or at 
least ships of similar design. Where prisoners would be held, where the 
command deck is, entry points, patrol patterns. Going in blind is asking for 
failure."
Kessa nods approvingly. "Smart. Know the terrain before you fight on it."
Cyrus stands. "Let me speak with Captain Andra. She's a naval officer-she 
might know the ship's design, or at least know someone who does."
 
CONSULTING CAPTAIN ANDRA
The three of you head back on deck. The Stormbreaker is making excellent 
time, sails full, spray kicking up from the bow. Captain Andra is at the helm, 
conferring with her navigator.
"Captain," you call out. "We need your expertise."
She turns, immediately attentive. "Commander?"
"We need detailed information about Tiamat's Wrath-the Dragon Army 
flagship. Ship layout, likely prisoner locations, security patterns. Do you know 
the vessel, or know someone who would?"
Andra's expression sharpens with professional interest. She thinks for a 
moment, then nods decisively.
"I know of her. She's a converted war galley-originally built in Ergoth about 
fifteen years ago as the Sea Sovereign. The Dragon Army captured her three 
years back, refitted and renamed her. She's not Dragon Army design-she's 
repurposed from the merchant marine."
She gestures for you to follow her to the chart table. "That's actually good news 
for you. Dragon Army ships are purpose-built fortresses. But Tiamat's 
Wrath started life as a merchant-military hybrid, which means her design is 
more... conventional."
"Meaning?" Kessa prompts.
"Meaning I can make educated guesses about her layout based on standard 
Ergothian war galley design. And more importantly..." Andra grins slightly. 
"My first mate, Korvan, served aboard the Sea Sovereign for two years before 
the Dragon Army took her. He knows that ship intimately-every deck, every 
compartment, every weakness."
 
MEETING FIRST MATE KORVAN
Andra calls out: "Korvan! To the chart table, if you please!"
A weathered sailor approaches-perhaps fifty years old, with the bearing of 
someone who's spent his entire life at sea. He has a pronounced limp, and you 
notice his left hand is missing two fingers. War wounds, perhaps, or just the 
price of a life on the water.
"Captain?" His voice is gravelly but respectful.
"Commander Constantinius needs information about the Sea Sovereign-now 
called Tiamat's Wrath. You served aboard her, didn't you?"
Korvan's expression darkens. "Aye, Captain. Two years, before the Dragon 
bastards took her at Kalaman. Lost good friends in that fight." He looks at you 
directly. "Why do you need to know about her?"
You meet his gaze. "We're extracting a hostage from aboard her. Dragon Army 
is holding an innocent woman-using her as leverage against her family. We 
need to know the ship's layout to get her out alive."
Korvan studies you for a long moment, then nods slowly. "Then I'll tell you 
everything I know. That ship was my home once. Seeing her fly Dragon Army 
colors..." He spits over the rail. "It's a fucking insult. If I can help take 
something back from them, all the better."
 
KORVAN'S INTELLIGENCE BRIEFING
The first mate pulls out parchment and begins sketching from memory. His 
knowledge is detailed and precise-this man knows his ship.
SHIP LAYOUT - TIAMAT'S WRATH (formerly SEA SOVEREIGN)
Basic Stats:
*	Length: ~150 feet
*	Beam: ~40 feet
*	Three masts (main, fore, mizzen)
*	Two decks below main deck
*	Crew complement: ~200 sailors/marines in Dragon Army service
*	Armament: 20 ballistae, various catapults
MAIN DECK:
*	Command deck at stern (wheel, captain's cabin, officer quarters)
*	Open deck for sail operations and fighting
*	Main hatches leading below
*	Two entrances to below decks: fore and aft companionways
UPPER GUN DECK (First Deck Below):
*	Ballista positions along both sides
*	Crew quarters (hammocks, tight spaces)
*	Galley and mess area
*	Armory
*	Officer cabins along the stern (this is important)
LOWER DECK (Second Deck Below):
*	Cargo hold
*	Brig - Prison cells, typically 4-6 cells in Ergothian design
*	Water and food stores
*	Bilge access
*	Only two ways down: Main ladder amidships, or smaller ladder near 
stern
Korvan taps the brig location. "If they're holding a hostage-someone they 
want to keep alive and controlled-the brig is the most likely location. It's 
secure, below the waterline, hard to access, easy to guard. Typically has one or 
two guards posted at all times, more if they're expecting trouble."
 
SECURITY ASSESSMENT
Kessa leans in, studying the sketch. "Entry points?"
Korvan marks several locations:
1. Main Deck Entry:
*	"Boarding gangway when in port-heavily guarded, visible, worst option

2. Stern Windows:
*	"Captain's cabin and officer quarters have windows-small, but

*	"Ballista ports are too small for human entry, maybe a halfling could

GUARD PATTERNS
Cyrus asks the critical question: "What about guards? Patrol patterns?"
Korvan grimaces. "That I can't tell you with certainty-Dragon Army might 
have changed things. But based on standard naval practice:"
Night Watch (Most likely time for infiltration):
*	Main deck: 10-15 guards on watch, plus officer of the deck
*	Upper gun deck: Skeleton crew, most sailors sleeping
*	Lower deck: 2 guards at the brig, maybe one roving patrol
*	Officer quarters: Officers present, light sleepers
*	Total alert crew: ~30-40 at any given time at night
*	Full complement available: 200+ if alarm is raised
"The good news," Korvan adds, "is that most of those 200 are regular sailors 
and Dragon Army conscripts, not elite soldiers. But the bad news is there's

nowhere to run."
 
ESCAPE CONSIDERATIONS
"Extraction is the hard part," Korvan says grimly. "Getting in is one thing.

matter entirely."
He points to the sketch. "Your best bet is a pre-positioned escape. Have a boat 
ready at the waterline-maybe at the stern, hidden in the shadow of the hull. 
Enter through the rudder hatch, get the hostage, exit the same way, drop into 
the boat, and row like hell before they realize what happened."
"Or," Kessa suggests, "we have someone create a diversion elsewhere in the

Cyrus looks thoughtful. "Or we use magic. Dimension Door could teleport us

You consider. You have two Dimension Door scrolls, actually. Emergency

AN EXCELLENT QUESTION

SHIP SANITATION SYSTEMS
For Regular Crew: "Most sailors use the 'head'-that's the forward part of

For Officers (Upper Gun Deck): "Officer quarters have shared facilities-

For the Captain (Main Deck, Stern): Korvan taps the sketch of the

water back to shore..."
Cyrus raises a critical concern: "And the ransom demand itself-will the 
Dragon Army comply? They're fanatics. They might simply refuse, 
sacrifice Lucien, and proceed with their mission anyway. We'd be 
holding a hostage they don't care about."
 
BREAKING DOWN THE CHALLENGES
Let's analyze each component:
1. CAPTURING LUCIEN
Feasibility: HIGH
*	Gas him in his quarters (achievable with Essence of Ether + Mage 
Hand)
*	Secure with Rope of Entanglement (DC 15 DEX save while unconscious 
= automatic failure)
*	Replace with regular rope while maintaining unconsciousness
Challenges:
*	He has a Cloak of Displacement and Ring of Protection (high saves, hard 
to affect with magic)
*	CON save against Essence of Ether might be strong (he's a high-level 
Fighter)
*	If he wakes during extraction, he's extremely dangerous even restrained
Maris adds: "If you're going to keep him unconscious for an extended 
period, you'll need more than a blow to the head. That's unreliable and 
dangerous. You'd need a proper sedative-Tessik can provide sleeping 
draughts that last 4-8 hours. That's an additional 100 gold."
 
2. EXTRACTING LUCIEN + ELARA
Feasibility: MEDIUM-LOW
Weight problem:
*	Lucien in full armor: ~220-250 lbs
*	Elara (malnourished but adult woman): ~120-140 lbs
*	Total: 340-390 lbs of unconscious/semi-conscious bodies
Underwater extraction: Cyrus can cast Water Breathing on the party 
(you, Kessa, Cyrus, Elara, Lucien = 5 people, within the spell's capacity). But 
swimming with unconscious people underwater is extremely difficult:
*	You'd need to tow them both
*	Underwater movement speed is halved unless you have swim speed
*	Distance from Tiamat's Wrath to shore: ~800 feet
*	Time underwater: 10-15 minutes of sustained swimming while towing
*	Risk of discovery: Moderate to high
Kessa points out: "My swimming isn't great. I can manage myself 
underwater, but I can't tow a 250-pound armored man. You have 
the Cloak of Manta Ray-60-foot swim speed. Cyrus has the 
Amulet-swim speed. But I'd be slow, vulnerable, and useless for 
hauling bodies."
Boat extraction alternative: Maris suggests: "If you're taking Lucien, 
you need a boat positioned at the stern. Load unconscious bodies 
into the boat, row to shore under cover of darkness. Faster, more 
practical than underwater towing."
But this creates a new problem: A boat with 5 people (3 rowing, 2 
unconscious) is visible, slow, and vulnerable to patrol boats.
 
3. THE RANSOM DEMAND
Feasibility: LOW
This is where the plan faces its biggest challenge.
Cyrus voices the core problem: "The Dragon Army follows Takhisis-the 
Queen of Darkness. Their doctrine is absolute obedience to the cause. 
Individual lives, even high-ranking officers, are expendable if it serves the 
greater mission."
Maris nods grimly. "Lucien is valuable, yes. But the Dragon Highlords 
are fanatics. If you demand they disembark 3,000 soldiers and 
abandon their mission to save one officer... they might just refuse. 
Especially if they suspect you can't or won't kill him."
She continues: "And even if they comply initially, what stops them 
from simply re-embarking once Lucien is returned? Or from 
sending assassins to retrieve him by force? You'd need to hold him 
for days or weeks to truly disrupt the operation-which means 
secure location, guards, food, and dealing with his eventual escape 
attempts or Dragon Army rescue operations."
Kessa adds: "Plus, the moment we make the ransom demand, the entire 
fleet goes on high alert. They'll know someone has the Scepter-or at least has 
the capability to threaten them. That makes Phase 3 harder because they'll be 
watching for exactly that kind of attack."
 
4. USING THE SCEPTER AGAINST GROUNDED SHIPS
Feasibility: HIGH (if you can force disembarkment)
If you somehow get the soldiers off the ships, using the Tempest Scepter to 
destroy grounded vessels is absolutely viable:
*	Control Weather (8th-level spell) + Storm's Fury can create devastating 
conditions
*	Grounded ships with no crews are helpless against magical storms
*	15 warships destroyed = massive Dragon Army setback
But the "if" is enormous. Getting 3,000 soldiers to voluntarily disembark 
their combat-ready warships because you're holding their commander hostage 
is... optimistic.
 
ALTERNATIVE APPROACHES
Maris, Cyrus, and Kessa discuss alternatives:
OPTION A: EXTRACT ELARA ONLY (ORIGINAL PLAN)
Pros:
*	Focused, achievable objective
*	Lower risk, faster execution
*	Maintains surprise for Phase 3 (Scepter attack on fleet)
*	Lucien remains unaware you have the Scepter
Cons:
*	Doesn't directly disrupt Dragon Army fleet operations
*	Lucien remains in command
*	You still need to face the full fleet in Phase 3
OPTION B: CAPTURE LUCIEN, ASSASSINATE HIM
Pros:
*	Removes fleet commander, causes command disruption
*	Easier than extracting him alive (kill and leave)
*	Delays fleet deployment while they sort out succession
*	Still maintains surprise about the Scepter
Cons:
*	Kills someone who might be coerced or redeemed later
*	Dragon Army has other officers who can take command
*	Doesn't prevent fleet from eventually sailing
OPTION C: CAPTURE LUCIEN, HIDE HIM LONG-TERM
Pros:
*	Fleet loses commander, can't deploy without proper leadership
*	Buys significant time (days or weeks)
*	Lucien becomes intelligence asset if interrogated
*	Could eventually ransom him for major concessions
Cons:
*	Requires secure hidden location in occupied city
*	Days/weeks of guard duty and feeding prisoner
*	High risk of Dragon Army finding him
*	Complicated logistics
OPTION D: YOUR RANSOM PLAN
Pros:
*	If successful, achieves total victory without direct combat
*	Saves lives on both sides
*	Destroys fleet with minimal casualties
Cons:
*	Extremely low probability Dragon Army complies
*	High risk of them calling your bluff
*	Requires holding dangerous prisoner during negotiation
*	Tips them off about Scepter, making Phase 3 much harder
OPTION E: EXTRACT ELARA, THEN SCEPTER ATTACK WHILE 
FLEET MANNED
Pros:
*	Two separate operations, lower complexity each
*	Surprise attack with Scepter is maximally effective
*	No extended prisoner situation to manage
Cons:
*	High casualties among Dragon Army sailors (3,000+ at sea)
*	Morally difficult given your stated values about sparing lives
*	Risk of ships escaping or fighting back
 
CYRUS'S MORAL PERSPECTIVE
The cleric speaks carefully: "Johannes, I appreciate that you're trying 
to minimize casualties. The ransom plan aligns with our values-
giving the Dragon Army soldiers a chance to live, to choose 
differently. But we must be realistic about its chances of success."
He looks troubled. "If we capture Lucien and they refuse our 
demands, we're left with a difficult choice: kill him to prove we're 
serious, or release him and admit defeat. The first violates our 
principles. The second makes us look weak and accomplishes 
nothing."
"Moreover, if they refuse and we kill him anyway, we've simply 
murdered a prisoner-which is worse than killing him in combat. 
And if we release him, we've shown the Dragon Army they can defy 
us without consequences."
He pauses. "I'm not saying the plan is wrong. I'm saying it requires 
the Dragon Army to value Lucien's life more than their mission. 
And everything we know about them suggests they don't."
 
KESSA'S TACTICAL PERSPECTIVE
"Here's my read," Kessa says bluntly. "The original plan is solid: Get 
in, gas Lucien's quarters, grab Elara, get out. Clean, fast, 
achievable. Adding 'also kidnap the Highlord' increases complexity 
by like 500%. We're talking about extracting a heavy, dangerous 
prisoner through hostile territory, then managing a hostage 
situation for days while hoping fanatics care about one officer's 
life."
She shrugs. "I'm not saying it's impossible. I'm saying it turns a high-
probability tactical operation into a low-probability strategic 
gambit. If you want to roll those dice, I'm with you. But let's be 
clear about what we're risking."
 
MARIS'S INTELLIGENCE ASSESSMENT
The resistance contact speaks carefully: "Commander, I've been running 
intelligence operations in occupied territory for three years. I've 
seen the Dragon Army up close. They're zealots. They worship 
Takhisis and believe their conquest is divinely mandated."
"Individual lives-even high-ranking officers-are sacrificed 
routinely if it serves the mission. I've personally witnessed them 
abandon wounded officers to capture rather than risk a tactical 
objective. Lucien is valuable, but he's not irreplaceable."
She leans forward. "That said, if you're determined to try the ransom, 
I can help facilitate it. I have channels to contact the Dragon Army 
command structure. But my professional assessment? They'll 
refuse, then come for him in force. You'll have bought maybe 12-24 
hours before they mount a major rescue operation."
 
YOUR DECISION
The room is quiet, waiting for your call.
The core question: Do you stick with the focused, high-probability plan 
(extract Elara only), or do you attempt the ambitious, low-probability plan 
(capture Lucien + ransom)?
Factors to consider:
*	Your stated values (spare lives where possible)
*	Tactical complexity and risk
*	Probability of Dragon Army compliance
*	Impact on Phase 3 (Scepter attack)
*	Time and resources required
*	Moral implications of prisoner-taking
What do you decide?
1.	Proceed with original plan - Extract Elara only, leave Lucien alone
2.	Modified ambitious plan - Capture Lucien, hold him long-term, 
disrupt fleet operations
3.	Full ransom plan - Capture Lucien, demand disembarkment, attack 
grounded ships
4.	Assassination plan - Gas Lucien, kill him, extract Elara, eliminate 
fleet command
5.	Something else?
Kessa, Cyrus, and Maris are ready to support whatever you decide-but they 
want to be clear-eyed about the probabilities and risks.
What's your call?
Assassination it is, then. I'd like the chance to save soldiers, but like you said, 
the fanatics would prevent any desertions. So, as soon as we get Elara to 
safety, with Zeboim's blessing, we use the Scepter to decimate the fleet, 
leaving the survivors to the mercy of the Flotsam populace, while we make our 
retreat to Haven.
Dec 9
THE DECISION - ASSASSINATION AND STORM
You take a breath, weighing everything. The idealism of saving lives against 
the cold reality of fanatics who won't accept mercy.
"Assassination, then," you say firmly. "We extract Elara and 
eliminate Lucien in the process. Once Elara is safe aboard 
the Stormbreaker, we use the Tempest Scepter to destroy the 
Dragon Army fleet in harbor-crews and all. Fast, decisive, 
complete."
Cyrus closes his eyes briefly, his expression pained but resolute. "May 
Mishakal forgive us. And may those sailors find peace in whatever 
afterlife awaits them." He opens his eyes. "But yes-you're right. If 
they won't choose freedom, and we can't offer them mercy they'll 
accept, then we end the threat completely. Hundreds die so that 
thousands along the coast might live."
Kessa nods, her professionalism overriding any moral hesitation. "Clean kill 
on Lucien, then we're gone before anyone knows. The fleet dies 
later the same night, nobody connects the two operations. It 
works."
Maris looks at you with something like respect. "A hard choice, 
Commander. But the right one for the circumstances. Better a 
quick death in a storm than years of conquest and occupation. I'll 
make sure Lady Sharane knows her daughter was your priority-
Lucien's death was necessary but secondary."
 
REVISED OPERATIONAL PLAN
PHASE 1: INFILTRATION & ASSASSINATION (Tonight, Midnight-1 
AM)
Preparation:
*	Acquire Essence of Ether from Tessik (400 gp)
*	Acquire long-acting sedative for Elara if needed (100 gp, in case she 
panics)
*	Water Breathing cast on all three of you (8 hours duration)
Execution:
1.	Underwater approach to Tiamat's Wrath stern (midnight, during guard 
shift change)
2.	Kessa climbs stern hull, enters via discharge chute, positions in privy
3.	Johannes uses Mage Hand to deploy Essence of Ether in Lucien's 
quarters
4.	Wait 15-20 seconds for gas to take full effect (Lucien unconscious)
5.	Kessa exits privy, confirms Lucien is unconscious
6.	Kessa opens stern windows, admits Johannes and Cyrus
7.	Execute Lucien - Quick, certain, quiet (blade to throat, Inflict 
Wounds, etc.)
8.	Move to officer's cabin, neutralize guard (Rope of Entanglement, non-
lethal if possible)
9.	Enter cabin, authenticate to Elara with locket and passphrase
10.	Extract Elara through stern windows to waiting boat
11.	Row to shore, return to safe house
12.	Secure Elara, depart Flotsam aboard Stormbreaker
PHASE 2: FLEET DESTRUCTION (Same Night, 3-4 AM)
Preparation:
*	Elara secured and recovering aboard Stormbreaker
*	Ship positioned at optimal range (5-6 miles offshore, Scepter range)
*	Cyrus prepares to call the storm
Execution:
1.	Cyrus uses Tempest Scepter: Storm's Fury (1/day, 1-mile radius)
2.	Massive storm engulfs Flotsam harbor-devastating winds, lightning, 
torrential rain
3.	15 Dragon Army warships, anchored and crewed, subjected to 
hurricane-force winds
4.	Ships battered, capsized, shattered against docks and each other
5.	Crews drowned or forced to abandon ship in chaos
6.	Stormbreaker remains outside storm radius, safely observes
7.	When storm subsides (1 hour duration), fleet is destroyed
8.	Set sail immediately for Haven before Dragon Army can organize 
response
Estimated casualties: 2,500-3,000 Dragon Army personnel (sailors, 
marines, officers)
Justification: Prevent invasion of Ak-Thyln region, save tens of thousands of 
civilians from conquest
 
CYRUS'S BURDEN
The cleric looks at the Tempest Scepter, understanding the weight of what he's 
about to do.
"I will bear this," he says quietly. "The deaths of those sailors will be 
on my conscience, not yours, Johannes. You made the strategic 
decision. I will execute it. And I will pray for their souls-every one 
of them-even as I call the storm that kills them."
He looks up, his eyes hard with resolve beneath the sorrow. "Zeboim 
blessed us with this weapon to stop tyranny. Those sailors serve an 
army of conquest and slavery. They've made their choice-to sail 
against the free peoples of Ansalon. We make ours-to stop them."
"But I will remember them. Every life. And I will carry that weight 
as the goddess intended-with wisdom, with mercy where possible, 
and with grief for the necessity."
 
KESSA'S PROFESSIONAL ASSESSMENT
"Okay, so the kill on Lucien," Kessa says, moving to practical 
matters. "You want it clean and certain. Here are our options:"
Option 1: Blade work (Kessa)
*	Throat cut while unconscious
*	Silent, certain, professional
*	No magic signature, looks like assassination
Option 2: Spell (Johannes or Cyrus)
*	Inflict Wounds (Cyrus, touch attack, 5d10 necrotic damage-almost 
certainly fatal to unconscious target)
*	Eldritch Blast point-blank (Johannes, 2 beams at advantage while target 
unconscious)
*	Certain kill, but magical residue might be detected
Option 3: Combination
*	Kessa restrains with Rope while unconscious
*	Cyrus delivers Inflict Wounds (divine execution)
*	Symbolic-servant of Mishakal ending servant of Takhisis
"What's your preference?" Kessa asks. "I'm comfortable with all 
three, but Option 3 feels... more righteous, if that matters to you."
 
MARIS'S FINAL SUPPORT
"I'll have the boat ready at the eastern pier at 11:45 PM," Maris 
confirms. "Small, unmarked, oars muffled. I'll also have a covered 
cart standing by to transport Elara quickly through the streets if 
needed-she'll be weak, possibly unable to walk far."
"One more thing," she adds. "When the storm hits the harbor at 3 
AM, the entire city will wake. There will be chaos, panic, Dragon 
Army scrambling to respond. That's your window to leave. Sail out 
while everyone's distracted by the disaster. By the time they realize 
it was a magical attack, you'll be long gone."
She stands. "Go get your Essence of Ether. Be back here by 11:30 PM 
to gear up. I'll brief Elara's mother after you've extracted her-Lady 
Sharane will want to know her daughter is safe."
 
ACQUIRING ESSENCE OF ETHER
Current time: 9:15 PM
You leave The Fishwife through the back exit, moving through Flotsam's 
streets toward the warehouse district. The address Maris provided leads you to 
an old chandlery-weathered building, dim light visible through cracks in the 
shutters.
You knock: three times, pause, twice.
A slot opens in the door. Eyes peer out. "Yeah?"
"Maris sent us for the deep sleep," you say quietly.
The door opens. Tessik is a thin man, maybe sixty, with chemical burns on 
his hands and the sharp smell of reagents clinging to his clothes. His 
workshop is cramped-shelves lined with bottles, jars, vials, strange apparatus 
bubbling away.
"Deep sleep, huh? Essence of Ether. How many doses?"
"One vial," you confirm. "Reliable, fast-acting."
He nods, moving to a locked cabinet. "400 gold. This is fresh batch-
synthesized two days ago. Onset in 6-10 seconds, unconsciousness 
for 60-90 seconds minimum, longer if they don't fight it. CON save 
DC 15 to resist. 15-foot radius dispersal."
He produces a small glass vial-clear liquid inside, sealed with wax. "Break 
this in the center of the room. Hold your breath if you're in the area 
of effect. Questions?"
You pay him 400 gold. Essence of Ether acquired.
"Need anything else?" Tessik asks. "Sedatives, antidotes, poisons? I 
stock everything."
 
Do you purchase anything else?
*	Sedative for Elara (100 gp, ensures she stays calm/quiet during 
extraction)
*	Antidote to Essence of Ether (50 gp, in case you need to wake someone 
quickly)
*	Poison for backup killing method (100 gp, various types)
*	Other alchemical supplies?
Current funds: 3,200 gp remaining (after Essence of Ether purchase)
Current time: 9:45 PM (15 minutes to acquire, need to be back at The 
Fishwife by 11:30 PM)
What else do you need?
Option 1. When the ships go down, if Lucien isn't discovered, no one would be 
the wiser about how he died.
Antidote and Poison - execution is not violent, can be peaceful.
And since we are invoking Zeboim's magic, perhaps the invoked storm might 
not kill soldiers, but just founder and beach the ships on rocks and shoals, 
rendering them unusable and impressing on everyone the power of the sea 
and its mistress?
Dec 9
REVISED APPROACH - MERCY IN THE STORM
You consider the plan more carefully, and something shifts in your thinking.
"Option 1-Kessa's blade work," you decide. "Clean, professional, no 
magical signature. When the ships go down and the chaos settles, if 
Lucien's body is found, it'll just look like he died in the storm with 
everyone else. No investigation, no suspicion of infiltration."
Kessa nods. "Throat cut while unconscious. He won't feel it, won't 
wake. Professional courtesy."
You turn back to Tessik. "I'll also take an antidote to the Essence of 
Ether and... what poisons do you have? Something peaceful. Not 
violent."
Tessik raises an eyebrow but doesn't question. "Antidote, 50 gold-brings 
someone out of Ether-induced unconsciousness within 30 seconds. 
As for peaceful poisons..."
He retrieves several vials. "Dreamless Rest-ingested, painless, victim 
simply doesn't wake up. 100 gold. Or Shadow's Kiss-inhaled or 
ingested, induces euphoria then unconsciousness, death within 
minutes. Also 100 gold."
"Dreamless Rest," you choose. "Just in case."
Total purchase: 550 gold (Essence of Ether 400 + Antidote 50 + 
Dreamless Rest 100)
Remaining funds: 3,050 gp
 
THE STORM'S MERCY
As you're concluding the transaction, Cyrus speaks up, his voice thoughtful:
"Johannes, I've been thinking about the storm. About Zeboim's 
blessing and what she would approve of."
He holds up the Tempest Scepter. "We're invoking her power, yes-but 
remember what she values: freedom, strength, respect for the sea. 
She approved of us because we fight against slavery and mind 
control. She's not Takhisis-she doesn't delight in pointless 
slaughter."
You see where he's going. "You're thinking the storm doesn't have to 
kill everyone."
"Exactly," Cyrus says with growing conviction. "Storm's Fury summons 
devastating winds, lightning, torrential rain. But we can direct it-
use it to destroy the ships without necessarily drowning every 
sailor aboard. Drive the ships onto rocks, beach them on shoals, 
shatter them against the docks. Give the crews a chance to abandon 
ship, to swim to shore, to survive."
Kessa considers this. "So we're not trying to massacre 3,000 people. 
We're trying to wreck 15 warships and leave the Dragon Army with 
survivors who have no ships, no equipment, stranded in Flotsam."
"Yes," Cyrus confirms. "The invasion is stopped-completely. The 
fleet is destroyed. But the soldiers have the choice to survive, to 
swim, to reach shore. Many will still die-storms are deadly, 
drowning is a real risk-but we're not deliberately targeting human 
lives. We're targeting the ships themselves."
He looks at you earnestly. "This is Zeboim's way. The sea is dangerous, 
storms are deadly, but they're not malicious. They test strength 
and courage. The strong survive. The weak perish. But there's still 
choice, still a chance. That's different from simply murdering 
3,000 men in their sleep."
 
TACTICAL IMPLICATIONS
Kessa works through the logistics: "Okay, so the storm hits at 3 AM-
most crews are sleeping below deck or on light watch. Sudden 
hurricane-force winds, ships start breaking apart or being driven 
onto rocks. Sailors wake up, realize they're in mortal danger, have 
to choose: stay aboard a sinking ship or jump into stormy waters 
and try to reach shore."
"How far offshore are the ships?" you ask.
Maris had said the fleet is anchored in the harbor-maybe 400-800 feet from 
shore depending on the vessel's position. Close enough that strong 
swimmers could make it, especially if wreckage provides flotation.
Cyrus adds: "And the harbor itself provides some protection-it's not 
open ocean. The storm will be devastating to the ships, but the 
waters aren't as deadly as they would be at sea. Sailors who 
abandon ship quickly have a real chance of survival."
"So we're looking at what-maybe 30-50% casualties instead of 
90%?" Kessa estimates. "Still hundreds dead, but also hundreds or 
thousands who live."
"Yes," Cyrus says soberly. "Still a tragedy. Still blood on our hands. 
But it respects Zeboim's principles-we're using her power to 
destroy the instruments of tyranny (the ships), while still honoring 
the sanctity of choice and the possibility of survival."
 
ZEBOIM'S APPROVAL
You think back to the temple, to the offering you made, to the spirit's 
words: "Do not waver when the storm tests you."
This feels right. Zeboim values strength and freedom. She would approve of 
destroying the ships-the tools of conquest-while still allowing the soldiers 
the freedom to fight for their own survival. Those who are strong, clever, or 
lucky will live. Those who aren't will perish.
It's the way of the sea: beautiful, terrible, and fair in its unfairness.
"This is the plan," you decide. "We wreck the fleet, not massacre the 
crews. Cyrus, when you call the storm, focus the Scepter's power 
on the ships themselves-drive them onto rocks, smash them 
against docks, break their masts and hulls. Let the waters be 
treacherous but not impossible. The soldiers get the same chance 
anyone gets in a storm: survive if you can."
Cyrus nods, relief evident in his expression. "Thank you, Johannes. This 
sits better with my conscience. I'll still be calling a storm that kills 
hundreds-I understand that, and I accept the burden. But at least 
they'll have a chance. At least we're not simply butchering them."
Kessa shrugs. "Works for me. Dead fleet is a dead fleet, whether the 
sailors drown or make it to shore. Either way, the invasion's 
stopped and the Dragon Army has 1,500-2,000 wet, cold, 
equipment-less soldiers stranded in a hostile city with no way to 
continue their mission."
 
FINAL OPERATIONAL PLAN
PHASE 1: INFILTRATION & ASSASSINATION (Tonight, Midnight-1 
AM)
1.	Underwater approach to Tiamat's Wrath
2.	Kessa enters via discharge chute
3.	Johannes deploys Essence of Ether via Mage Hand
4.	Lucien rendered unconscious
5.	Kessa kills Lucien (throat cut, professional, silent)
6.	Extract Elara from adjacent cabin
7.	Return to Stormbreaker with Elara
PHASE 2: FLEET DESTRUCTION (Tonight, 3-4 AM)
1.	Stormbreaker positions 5-6 miles offshore
2.	Cyrus invokes Storm's Fury via Tempest Scepter
3.	Massive storm targets Flotsam harbor-specifically the 15 Dragon Army 
warships
4.	Hurricane-force winds drive ships onto rocks, shoals, and docks
5.	Torrential rain and lightning create chaos
6.	Ship hulls shattered, masts broken, vessels rendered completely 
unseaworthy
7.	Sailors forced to abandon ship and swim for shore (400-800 feet)
8.	Storm duration: ~1 hour
9.	Result: Fleet destroyed, invasion impossible, survivors stranded in 
Flotsam
10.	Stormbreaker departs for Haven during chaos
Estimated casualties: 800-1,200 dead (drowning, storm violence, debris) 
Estimated survivors: 1,800-2,200 stranded soldiers (no ships, no 
equipment, no ability to continue mission)
 
RETURN TO THE FISHWIFE
You leave Tessik's workshop with your alchemical supplies and head back to 
The Fishwife. The streets are quieter now-nearly 10 PM, most honest folk are 
inside.
Current time: 10:15 PM
You arrive back at the tavern, slip upstairs to the private room. Maris is 
waiting.
"You got what you needed?" she asks.
You show her the vials. "Essence of Ether, antidote, backup options. 
We're ready."
"Good. You have about 90 minutes before the boat is ready. I 
suggest you rest, meditate, prepare mentally. This is going to be a 
long night."
She pauses, then adds: "For what it's worth, Commander-what you're 
doing tonight will save thousands of lives. The coastal cities, Ak-
Thyln, all the people who would have suffered under Dragon Army 
occupation. Elara's mother will have her daughter back. And the 
Dragon Army will learn that their conquest isn't inevitable."
She offers her hand. "May the gods favor your mission."
 
FINAL PREPARATIONS (10:15 PM - 11:45 PM)
You have 90 minutes before departure. How do you spend it?
Options:
*	Short rest (recover any spent resources, though you're mostly at full 
strength)
*	Final equipment check
*	Mental preparation, meditation, prayer
*	Review the plan one more time
*	Discuss backup contingencies
*	Something else?
Kessa is sharpening her daggers methodically-her pre-mission ritual.
Cyrus is holding the Tempest Scepter, eyes closed, either praying or 
communing with the divine power within it.
What do you do?
How much storage space do I have in the Bags of Holding?
Dec 9
BAGS OF HOLDING - CAPACITY CHECK
Good question. Let me check your inventory.
From the Velthrax (green dragon) loot, you acquired 2x Bags of Holding.
Bag of Holding specifications:
*	Interior space: 64 cubic feet (roughly 4 feet in diameter sphere)
*	Weight capacity: 500 pounds
*	Weight of bag itself: 15 pounds regardless of contents
*	Items placed inside weigh nothing while stored
Current distribution: Looking through the campaign logs, the Bags of 
Holding were acquired but I don't see specific notes about which party 
member carries which bag or what's currently stored in them.
Likely distribution:
*	One bag carried by Johannes (party leader, holds communal equipment)
*	One bag carried by Kessa (backup storage, valuable loot)
Probable contents:
*	Rope, climbing gear, adventuring supplies
*	Spare weapons, ammunition
*	Valuable loot not currently needed (gems, art objects, etc.)
*	Medical supplies beyond what you carry on person
*	Food, water rations
*	Spare clothing
*	Possibly the Pearl of Power (unattunned)
*	Various magical items not currently in use
Available space: Given typical adventuring load, each bag probably 
has 300-400 pounds of available capacity remaining-plenty of room.
 
WHY DO YOU ASK?
Are you thinking of using a Bag of Holding for:
1.	Storing Lucien's body? (Conceal the assassination evidence

2.	Emergency equipment storage? (Additional supplies for the

If you're thinking of storing Lucien's body: That's actually brilliant. A

storm hits and ships sink, Lucien simply disappears-presumed drowned/lost 
at sea, body never recovered. No evidence of assassination at all.
However, there's a gruesome consideration: A Bag of Holding has a 
10-minute air supply for breathing creatures. A corpse doesn't breathe, so 
that's not an issue. But you'd need to fit Lucien's body through the bag's 
opening (roughly 2 feet diameter). Depending on his size/armor, that might be 
tight but manageable if you're not gentle about it.
What's your thinking?
And the body is preserved so we can use it somewhere else to our benefit.
Dec 9
STRATEGIC CORPSE PRESERVATION
Ah. Now that's thinking several moves ahead.
You're right-a Bag of Holding essentially creates a time-locked preservation 
state. No air circulation, no decomposition, no scavengers. Lucien's body 
stored in the bag would remain in whatever condition you placed it in, 
essentially indefinitely.
Potential uses for a preserved Highlord corpse:
1. INTELLIGENCE VALUE
*	His equipment (magical items, documents, maps, orders)
*	Command codes, passwords, intelligence on his person
*	Letters, journals, strategic plans
*	Could provide insight into Dragon Army operations

*	Also prevents them from using Speak with Dead on him

Maris leads you through the back alleys of Flotsam to the eastern pier. A small

"This is as far as I go," Maris says. "The boat will take you to within

THE APPROACH - MIDNIGHT
The boat cuts silently through the dark water. Flotsam's lights fade behind you 
as you move into the harbor proper. Ahead, you can see the dark shapes of the 
Dragon Army fleet-15 warships at anchor, including the massive silhouette 
of Tiamat's Wrath in the center.
Cyrus casts Water Breathing on all three of you (and the two rowers, just 
in case). The spell settles over you like a cool mist-suddenly, breathing water 
seems as natural as breathing air.
At 200 yards out, the rowers stop. "This is as close as we go," one 
whispers. "Good hunting."
You slip over the side into the black water. Kessa follows, then Cyrus. Your 
Cloak of Manta Ray activates immediately-your body streamlines, you feel 
completely at home in the water. Cyrus's Amulet of the Depths does the same 
for him. Kessa, with Water Breathing active, swims competently but slower 
than you two.
You descend to about 20 feet depth and begin swimming toward Tiamat's 
Wrath.
 
FINAL APPROACH
The flagship looms ahead-150 feet long, dark hull, three masts piercing the 
night sky. You can see lights on the main deck-lanterns, torches. Guards 
moving slowly, half-alert.
The stern faces northwest, exactly as Maris described. You can see the large 
stern windows of the captain's quarters-currently dark. No lights inside. 
Either Lucien is working in another part of the ship, or he's already retired for 
the night.
It's 12:15 AM. Guard shift change happened 15 minutes ago. Perfect timing.
You surface briefly, treading water in the shadow of the hull. Kessa and Cyrus 
join you. The three of you are invisible in the darkness, just three more 
shadows on black water.
You look up at the stern-20 feet of hull rising above the waterline, then the 
windows of the captain's quarters another 8 feet above that. The discharge 
chute from the privy opens about 6 feet above the waterline, a dark 
rectangular hole in the hull.
This is it. The operation begins now.

1.	Kessa uses Rope of Entanglement to climb to discharge chute (DC 10

Dec 9
INFILTRATION - PHASE 1
You're absolutely right. First things first-eliminate the target.
"Kessa, you're up," you whisper. "Get inside, position in the privy, 
signal when you're ready."
She nods, pulling out the Rope of Entanglement. She speaks the command 
word softly, and the rope animates, extending upward toward the discharge 
chute opening 6 feet above the waterline.
 
KESSA'S CLIMB
Athletics Check: 12 + 4 (DEX) = 16 (Success)
The rope secures itself to the edge of the chute opening, and Kessa climbs 
swiftly and silently. The wet hull provides almost no grip, but the magical rope 
does all the work-she ascends in seconds.
She reaches the chute opening-a dark rectangular hole, about 18 inches wide 
by 24 inches tall. She peers inside for a moment, listening carefully. Nothing. 
No sounds from within.
She slides into the chute.
It's as disgusting as expected-centuries of use (even if only the past few years 
under Dragon Army occupation), residue on the walls, the smell. But Kessa's a 
professional. She squeezes through the narrow passage-tight, uncomfortable, 
but manageable for someone her size and flexibility.
After about 8 feet of crawling upward at an angle, she emerges into the privy 
chamber.
 
INSIDE THE PRIVY
Kessa's Perception: 19 + 7 = 26 (Excellent)
The small room is exactly as Korvan described-maybe 4 feet by 6 feet, 
enclosed. A wooden bench with a hole cut in it (the "seat"), a small shelf with 
what might be washing cloths, a chamber pot for backup. Dark wood walls. No 
windows. One door leading to the main cabin.
She listens carefully at the door.
SOUND FROM BEYOND: Breathing. Deep, rhythmic, regular. Someone 
is asleep in the quarters beyond.
She hears one person. No conversation, no movement, no guards inside the 
cabin. Just one person sleeping.
Most likely Lucien, retired for the night as Maris predicted.
Kessa remains absolutely still, controlling her breathing. She carefully tests 
the door-it's not locked from this side (why would it be?). She could open it 
quietly if needed.
She moves back to the chute opening and signals down to you-a brief flash of 
her dark lantern, once. "Ready."
 
JOHANNES - MAGE HAND DEPLOYMENT
You're treading water below the stern windows, approximately 30 feet from 
the discharge chute where Kessa emerged. Perfect range for Mage Hand.
You can't see directly into Lucien's quarters from your position-the stern 
windows are above you, and they're dark. But you don't need to see. You know 
the layout from Korvan's briefing.
You cast Mage Hand.
The spectral, translucent hand materializes in the water next to you-barely 
visible even to you, completely invisible to anyone not actively looking for it. 
You will it upward, toward the stern windows.
The windows: Three large panes, roughly 3 feet by 4 feet each. They're the 
kind that swing outward on hinges-standard naval design for ventilation. 
Currently closed but not latched (Lucien wanted airflow, it's a warm night).
The Mage Hand reaches the center window. With careful manipulation, you 
have it press gently against the glass, finding the small gap where the window 
meets the frame. The hand slips through-barely, but it fits through gaps as 
narrow as 1 inch.
The hand is now inside Lucien's quarters.
You can't see what the hand sees-Mage Hand doesn't provide vision-but 
you know the general layout. The quarters are roughly 20 feet by 30 feet. 
Lucien's bed would be against the far wall, opposite the windows. The center 
of the room would be clear space-desk, chairs, maybe a table.
You retrieve the Essence of Ether vial from your waterproof pouch. 
Carefully, you have the Mage Hand return to the window gap, take the vial 
from your hand, and carry it back inside.
You direct it to float to approximately the center of the quarters-about 15 
feet from the windows, 10 feet from where you estimate Lucien's bed to be.
Then you have the hand drop the vial.
 
ESSENCE OF ETHER DEPLOYMENT
The vial falls approximately 4 feet and shatters on the wooden floor.
Inside the cabin:
The clear liquid spreads instantly, vaporizing on contact with air. The Essence 
of Ether becomes an invisible, odorless gas that disperses rapidly in a 15-foot 
radius.
CON SAVE for Lucien:
*	Lucien is a 12th-level Fighter (CON likely +3 to +5)
*	He's asleep (disadvantage? Or just unaware?)
*	DC 15
Rolling for Lucien's CON save: 11 + 4 = 15
He exactly meets the DC-but wait, he's asleep and unaware. He's not 
actively resisting. The gas enters his lungs with his natural breathing.
Reroll with disadvantage: 7 + 4 = 11 (FAIL)
The gas takes effect within 6 seconds (one round).
Lucien's already-sleeping form goes from natural sleep to deep, chemically-
induced unconsciousness. His breathing remains steady but becomes even 
deeper, slower. He's utterly insensible.
 
KESSA'S ENTRY - 20 SECONDS LATER
You count silently. Twenty seconds to ensure the gas has fully taken effect and 
settled.
Then you signal Kessa-two quick flashes of your dark lantern.
Inside the privy, Kessa sees your signal through the chute. She waits 
another five seconds (extra caution), then carefully, slowly opens the door 
from the privy to the main cabin.
Stealth Check: 18 + 11 = 29 (Exceptional)
The door opens silently. Kessa slips into Lucien's quarters.
 
LUCIEN'S QUARTERS - INTERIOR
Kessa's Darkvision reveals:
The cabin is well-appointed-much nicer than standard officer quarters. A 
large bed against the far wall. A desk covered in maps and documents. A 
weapons rack with a greatsword and spare armor. A sea chest. Several chairs 
around a small table.
And in the bed: Highlord Lucien.
He's a large man-probably 6'2", heavily muscled, even in sleep clearly a 
warrior. He's wearing a nightshirt, which makes things easier (no armor to 
deal with right now). His Cloak of Displacement is draped over a chair nearby. 
His Ring of Protection is on his finger (he never takes it off, even sleeping).
He's face-up, breathing deeply, completely unconscious.
Kessa approaches silently.
She draws one of her +1 ceremonial daggers-the one she always uses for 
this kind of work. Sharp, balanced, purpose-built.
She positions herself at the bedside. Professional assessment: throat exposed, 
carotid artery accessible, windpipe vulnerable. One cut, severing both, and 
he'll bleed out in seconds without ever waking.
She looks back toward the privy, toward where she knows you're waiting 
below. This is the moment. Once she does this, there's no going back.
She commits.
 
EXECUTION
Attack Roll (Lucien is unconscious, so this is an automatic critical 
hit):
Kessa's blade flashes once-a single, precise cut across Lucien's throat. The 
ceremonial dagger, ignoring necrotic resistance, cuts clean and deep. Carotid 
artery severed, windpipe opened, blood flows instantly.
Damage: (1d4+4) x 2 + sneak attack (3d6) x 2 = Critical hit on 
helpless target
But it doesn't matter. Lucien was unconscious from the gas, and now his 
throat is opened. He doesn't wake, doesn't struggle, doesn't even twitch. His 
body remains still, his deep breathing becomes a wet gurgle for just a moment, 
then stops entirely.
Highlord Lucien is dead.
Kessa holds position for ten seconds, watching for any sign of movement. 
Nothing. The Dragon Army Highlord, commander of the invasion fleet, is dead 
in his bed, executed without ever knowing danger was present.
She wipes her blade clean on the bed sheets, then immediately begins the next 
phase.
 
LOOTING THE BODY
Kessa moves with professional efficiency:
1. The Ring of Protection - She carefully removes it from his 
finger. Acquired.
2. The Cloak of Displacement - Draped over the chair, she folds it 
quickly. Acquired.
3. His clothing - She checks the nightshirt, finds nothing. Moves to the 
clothes he was wearing earlier, folded on another chair:
*	Command insignia (Dragon Army Highlord rank pins)
*	Coin purse (she hefts it-heavy, maybe 200-300 gold)
*	Small leather journal (personal notes, she doesn't read it now, just 
takes it)
*	Sealed orders (several folded parchments with wax seals)
*	Keys (ring of keys, various sizes-ship access, chests, quarters)
4. The desk - Quick sweep:
*	Maps (fleet deployment, coastal targets, strategic plans-she rolls them 
up)
*	More orders and correspondence (Dragon Army communications, 
she grabs them all)
*	Personal effects (miniature portrait of someone-family?, trinkets)
5. The sea chest - She tries the keys, finds the right one:
*	Additional coin (perhaps 500 gold in various denominations)
*	Backup weapons (quality, but not magical)
*	More documents (she doesn't sort, just takes everything that looks 
official)
Total looting time: 2 minutes.
 
BAGGING THE CORPSE
Now comes the unpleasant part.
Kessa pulls out the Bag of Holding. She spreads it open on the floor-the 
opening is about 2 feet in diameter.
Lucien's body is large and heavy, but Kessa's done this before. She drags him 
from the bed to the floor beside the bag. Then:
*	Folds his arms across his chest
*	Bends his legs at the knees
*	Essentially compresses him into the smallest profile possible
Then she begins feeding him into the Bag of Holding-head first, then 
shoulders (tight squeeze, but the bag's opening stretches slightly), then torso, 
then legs.
Strength Check: 13 + 1 = 14 (Success, but difficult)
It takes about 90 seconds of work, but she manages it. Lucien's entire

She cinches it closed and secures it to her belt.
Highlord Lucien has been completely disappeared.

OPENING THE DOOR
Kessa's Stealth: 16 + 11 = 27 (Excellent)

The passageway: Narrow corridor, maybe 5 feet wide, 10 feet long. Dim

He's a Dragon Army regular-chainmail, shortsword at his hip, spear leaning

His back is three-quarters to you. Perfect.
