ROPE OF ENTANGLEMENT - ACTIVATION
Kessa speaks the command word firmly but quietly: "Ensnare."
The magical rope animates instantly, shooting forward like a living serpent. It

Attack Roll: 14 + 7 (Kessa's DEX for magical item) = 21 (Hit)
The rope wraps around the guard's torso, arms, and legs in a tight, constrictive 
coil before he can react.
Guard's DEX Save: 9 + 2 = 11 (FAIL vs DC 15)
The guard is Restrained-completely. His arms are pinned to his sides, his 
legs bound together, the rope constricting with magical strength. He opens his

SILENCING THE GUARD
Kessa is already moving. She crosses the 10 feet in a heartbeat (movement +

escape.
Athletics Check (contested): Kessa 15 + 1 = 16 vs Guard's Strength 
12 + 1 = 13 (Success)
The guard's attempted shout becomes a muffled grunt against her palm. His

*	Tears a strip from his own shirt and gags him firmly (can't speak, can

*	Commands the Rope of Entanglement to release him

Inside Elara's cabin:
The room is small-maybe 10 feet by 12 feet. A narrow bed, a single chair, a

And on the bed, sitting up suddenly at the sound of the door opening: Elara.
She's in her mid-twenties, dark hair disheveled, wearing a simple dress that's

She sees three armed strangers entering her locked cabin and her first instinct

"Your mother remembers the storms you weathered together," you

Elara's hand goes to her mouth. Her eyes fill with tears. "That's... that's my

"This is real," you confirm. "But we have maybe ten minutes before

ABOARD THE EXTRACTION BOAT
Elara is wrapped in the blanket, clutching her grandmother's locket, tears 
streaming down her face. "Is this real? Am I really free?"
Cyrus sits beside her, his voice gentle. "You're free. We're taking you to 
safety. Your mother will be so relieved."
Elara looks at the three of you-really looks, for the first time since the chaos 
of the extraction. "Who are you? I mean... I know you're resistance, 
but... you came for me. Just me. Why?"
Kessa answers simply: "Because you were a prisoner. Because your 
mother asked for help. Because it was the right thing to do."
"And because," you add, "the Dragon Army doesn't get to hold 
innocent people hostage. Not while we can do something about it."
Elara nods, fresh tears coming. "Thank you. All of you. I thought... I 
thought I'd be there until they had no more use for me. Or worse."
She pauses, then asks quietly: "Highlord Lucien. You said he was 
'gone.' Is he... did you kill him?"
 
How do you answer?
1.	Be direct: "Yes. He's dead. He won't hurt anyone else."
2.	Be vague: "He's not a threat anymore. That's all that matters."
3.	Defer: "Let's get you safe first. We can discuss everything later."
4.	Let Cyrus answer (as the cleric, he might frame it better)
5.	Something else?
The rowboat continues cutting through the dark water. The Stormbreaker is

Dec 9
THE TRUTH
You meet Elara's eyes directly, your voice steady and honest.
"Yes. He's dead. He won't hurt anyone else."
Elara absorbs this for a long moment. Her expression cycles through shock, 
relief, guilt, and finally something like grim acceptance.
"Good," she says quietly. "Is that terrible? That I'm glad he's dead?"
Cyrus shakes his head gently. "No, child. He held you prisoner, used 
you as leverage against your mother, threatened your life. It's 
natural to feel relief that your captor is gone."
"He wasn't... directly cruel to me," Elara says, her voice distant. "Not 
physically. But he made it clear-every day-that my life depended 
on my mother's cooperation. That if she didn't provide what the 
Dragon Army needed, I would suffer for it. The threat was always 
there, hanging over everything."
She pulls the blanket tighter around herself. "He would come to my cabin 
sometimes. Just stand there, watching me. Reminding me that he 
controlled whether I lived or died. That was worse than any 
beating. The constant fear, the powerlessness..."
Kessa's expression hardens. "Men like that-men who use power over 
the helpless-they don't deserve mercy. You're free because he's 
dead. Don't feel guilty about that."
Elara nods slowly. "How did you...?" She trails off, then decides she doesn't 
need the details. "Never mind. I don't need to know. Just... thank you. 
For doing what had to be done."
 
REACHING THE STORMBREAKER
The rowboat pulls alongside the Stormbreaker. Captain Andra is at the rail, 
clearly relieved to see you.
"Commander! You're back. And you have her?" She sees Elara 
wrapped in the blanket. "By the gods, you actually pulled it off."
Rope ladders drop down. Sailors help Elara aboard first-she's weak and 
needs assistance, but she makes it. Kessa follows, then Cyrus, then you. The 
two rowers stay in their small boat, ready to return to shore.
"Payment," you say, handing one of the rowers a pouch of gold (50 gold 
pieces-generous for their risk). "Tell Maris the mission was a complete 
success. Elara is safe. Tell Lady Sharane her daughter will be 
coming home."
The rower nods, stowing the gold. "Safe sailing, Commander. Give the 
Dragon Army hell."
They row back toward Flotsam's lights, disappearing into the darkness.
 
ABOARD THE STORMBREAKER - 1:00 AM
Captain Andra directs sailors to help Elara below deck. "Get her warm, fed, 
and rested. Medical check if she needs it."
Elara looks back at you before she's led away. "Thank you. All of you. I'll 
never forget this."
Then she's gone, being cared for by the Stormbreaker's crew.
Andra turns to you, her expression serious. "Phase 1 complete. Now-
Phase 2. The fleet."
You glance toward Flotsam harbor-the lights, the dark shapes of fifteen 
Dragon Army warships at anchor. 3,000 soldiers sleeping aboard, unaware of 
what's coming.
Cyrus stands at the rail, the Tempest Scepter in his hands, staring at the 
distant fleet. His expression is resolute but heavy with the weight of what he's 
about to do.
"How long until we're in position?" you ask Captain Andra.
"We're already offshore about 4 miles," she says. "For the Scepter's 
range, we need to be within about 5-6 miles of the target. We can 
move to optimal position-say, 5 miles out-within 30 minutes. 
That puts us at 1:30 AM."
She pauses. "You want to hit them at 3 AM, you said? During the 
deepest part of the night watch, when most are asleep?"
You nod. "Maximum impact, minimum warning."

Dec 9
BRIEFING CAPTAIN ANDRA
You head to the captain's cabin with Kessa and Cyrus. Captain Andra pours 
four glasses of rum-a naval tradition after successful operations-and 
gestures for you to sit.
"Report, Commander. I saw you extract the girl successfully. What 
else happened aboard Tiamat's Wrath?"
You lay out the operation step by step:
"We infiltrated via the stern-Kessa through the discharge chute, 
Cyrus and I through the windows. Used alchemical gas to render 
Highlord Lucien unconscious in his quarters. Then we eliminated 
him."
Andra's eyebrows rise. "You killed a Dragon Army Highlord? While 
extracting the hostage?"
"Opportunity presented itself," Kessa says matter-of-factly. "He was 
alone, vulnerable, and his death removes a major threat. We took 
it."
"More than that," you continue, pulling out the Bag of Holding. "We have 
his body. And everything he was carrying."
You spread Lucien's possessions on the table:
*	Maps showing fleet deployment and coastal invasion targets
*	Sealed orders with Dragon Army command seals
*	Personal journal with notes on strategy and command structure
*	Command insignia and keys
*	The magical items (Cloak of Displacement, Ring of Protection)
*	Coin purse with ~800 gold
Andra examines the maps carefully, her tactical mind immediately recognizing 
their value. "These are detailed invasion plans. Ak-Thyln is the 
primary target, but there are secondary objectives here-Kalaman, 
Tarsis, half a dozen coastal cities. This is... this is a comprehensive 
conquest strategy."
She looks up at you. "And you have his corpse? Why?"
Cyrus explains: "Intelligence exploitation. We can use Speak with 
Dead to interrogate him-extract information about Dragon Army 
command structure, prisoner locations, strategic weaknesses. 
Then potentially use the body for disinformation operations later."
"Also," you add, "when the storm hits and the fleet is destroyed, 
Lucien's body won't be found in the wreckage. The Dragon Army 
will assume he drowned, was lost at sea. No investigation, no 
suspicion of infiltration. Just another casualty of the storm."
Andra sits back, impressed despite herself. "Commander, that's... that's 
extraordinarily thorough. You didn't just complete the mission-
you turned it into a major intelligence coup and removed a key 
enemy commander in the process."
She raises her glass. "To professional excellence. And to Elara's 
freedom."
You all drink.
 
THE STORM DISCUSSION
The rum finished, the mood shifts. Andra's expression becomes more somber.
"Now-the storm. You're planning to use the Tempest Scepter to 
destroy the entire Dragon Army fleet. Fifteen warships, roughly 
3,000 personnel aboard."
Cyrus nods slowly, the weight already visible in his eyes. "Yes. At 3 AM, 
when most are sleeping. We'll call a massive storm-hurricane 
winds, lightning, torrential rain. Drive the ships onto rocks, shatter 
their hulls, break their masts. Make them completely 
unseaworthy."
"And the crews?" Andra asks directly.
"We're not trying to maximize casualties," you clarify. "The storm 
targets the ships themselves. Sailors will have the opportunity to 
abandon ship, swim to shore. The harbor is close-400 to 800 feet 
from most anchor positions. Strong swimmers, quick thinkers, 
lucky ones-they'll survive."
Cyrus adds quietly: "But many won't. Storm conditions are deadly. 
Drowning, debris, panic, exhaustion. We're estimating 800 to 
1,200 dead. Perhaps more."
Andra is silent for a moment, then nods grimly. "War is never clean, 
Commander. Those sailors serve an army of conquest. They're 
sailing to invade Ak-Thyln, to subjugate free cities, to bring tyranny 
to the coast. You're stopping that. The blood is on the Dragon 
Army's hands-they chose this path."
She looks at Cyrus specifically. "Brother, you're carrying a heavy 
burden tonight. But remember-every sailor who dies in that storm 
is a soldier who won't be landing on Ak-Thyln's beaches, burning 
homes, enslaving families. You're trading hundreds of enemy lives 
for thousands of innocent ones. That's not murder. That's war."
Cyrus nods slowly, but you can see it doesn't make the weight any lighter.
 
CYRUS'S PREPARATION - SPIRITUAL 
READINESS
After the briefing, Cyrus excuses himself. "I need time alone. To pray. To 
prepare."
You find him an hour later on the forward deck, sitting cross-legged with the 
Tempest Scepter across his lap. The artifact pulses with faint blue-white light, 
responding to his presence.
He's not praying audibly-just sitting in silence, eyes closed, one hand on the 
Scepter, the other on his holy symbol of Mishakal.
You approach quietly. "Brother. How are you holding up?"
Cyrus opens his eyes. They're clear but sad. "I'm ready. Or as ready as I'll 
ever be."
He looks at the Scepter. "I've been communing with the divine-both 
Mishakal and Zeboim. Asking for wisdom, for strength, for 
forgiveness if what I'm about to do is wrong."
"And?" you ask gently.
"Mishakal reminds me that healing sometimes requires cutting 
away disease. That protecting the innocent sometimes means 
standing against those who threaten them-even unto death. She 
doesn't rejoice in violence, but she understands necessity."
He pauses. "Zeboim... Zeboim approves. She sees this as righteous-
using her storms to destroy tools of conquest, to test the strength of 
those caught in the tempest. She values freedom above all else. The 
Dragon Army sails to enslave-that's anathema to her."
Cyrus looks up at you. "I'm not at peace with what I'm about to do, 
Johannes. I won't be. I'll carry the weight of every soul that drowns 
tonight. But I accept the burden because the alternative-allowing 
that fleet to sail, to invade, to conquer-is worse."
He stands, gripping the Scepter firmly. "I will call the storm. I will 
shatter those ships. I will give the sailors every chance I can to 
survive-but I won't hold back the power needed to ensure the fleet 
is destroyed. And when it's done, I will pray for every soul lost, 
enemy and innocent alike."
"Then I'll mourn with you," you say. "And I'll help you carry that 
weight. You're not alone in this, Brother."
Cyrus clasps your shoulder. "Thank you, my friend. Now-let's finish 
this."
 
POSITIONING THE STORMBREAKER - 2:30 AM
Captain Andra has been slowly moving the Stormbreaker into optimal 
position. You're now approximately 5 miles offshore from Flotsam harbor-
far enough to be safe from the storm's effects, close enough for the Scepter's 
magic to reach.
From the deck, you can see Flotsam's lights in the distance-the city still 
sleeping, unaware of what's coming. The fifteen Dragon Army warships are 
dark shapes in the harbor, lanterns marking their positions. Occasional patrol 
boats move between them, small lights bobbing on the black water.
It's 2:45 AM.
Andra approaches. "We're in position, Commander. Stable 
anchorage, good visibility of the target zone. Whenever Brother 
Cyrus is ready."
The crew has been briefed-they know a storm is coming, they know it's 
magical, they know to stay well clear of the affected area. Some are nervous. 
Others are grimly satisfied-many of these sailors lost friends or family to 
Dragon Army raids.
 
FINAL PREPARATIONS - 2:45 AM TO 3:00 AM
You have fifteen minutes before the planned strike time.
Cyrus stands at the bow, the Tempest Scepter held in both hands. The 
artifact is glowing more brightly now-responding to his intent, to the divine 
power flowing through him, to Zeboim's blessing.
Kessa stands nearby, watching Flotsam. Her expression is unreadable-
professional, focused, but there's something in her eyes. Regret? Acceptance? 
Both?
You stand with them, looking at the distant fleet. In fifteen minutes, those 
ships will be wreckage. In an hour, hundreds will be dead.
It's a terrible calculus. But it's the right one.
 
Do you:

2.	Say something to Cyrus (final words of support before he calls the 
storm)
3.	Say something to Kessa (check in on your companion)
4.	Pray yourself (to whatever gods might listen)
5.	Something else?
The minutes tick by. The sea is calm. The night is quiet.
Soon, it will be neither.

Dec 9
THE WAIT - 2:45 AM TO 3:00 AM
You stand in silence at the bow with Cyrus and Kessa, watching the distant 
lights of Flotsam. The sea is calm, the wind gentle. The Stormbreaker rocks 
softly at anchor.
Cyrus holds the Tempest Scepter, eyes closed, breathing steadily. Preparing 
himself mentally and spiritually for what comes next.
Kessa stands with arms crossed, her professional mask firmly in place, but you 
can see the tension in her shoulders. She's killed many people-but never 
hundreds at once, never from a distance like this.
You simply wait. There's nothing more to say. The decision is made. The time 
approaches.
2:50 AM. Ten minutes.
2:55 AM. Five minutes.
Captain Andra quietly orders her crew to secure anything loose on deck. The 
sailors move efficiently, professionally. They trust their captain. They trust 
you.
2:58 AM. Two minutes.
Cyrus opens his eyes. He looks at the Scepter in his hands, then at the distant 
harbor, then at you.
"It's time," he says quietly.
You nod.
 
CYRUS CALLS THE STORM - 3:00 AM
Cyrus raises the Tempest Scepter high, pointing it toward Flotsam harbor. He 
speaks-not loudly, but with absolute conviction:
"Zeboim, Lady of Storms, Mistress of the Deeps-I invoke your 
power. Grant me your tempest. Let the winds howl. Let the 
lightning strike. Let the sea rise against those who would enslave 
the free peoples of Ansalon."
"Shatter the ships of tyranny. Give their sailors the same choice 
you give all who face your storms-survive through strength, or 
perish in the deep. Let this be righteous fury, not mindless 
slaughter. Let this be your will made manifest."
He brings the Scepter down in a sharp arc, pointing directly at the distant 
fleet.
"STORM'S FURY!"
 
THE STORM BEGINS
The Tempest Scepter blazes with blinding blue-white light. Lightning arcs 
from its tip, shooting across five miles of open water toward Flotsam harbor. 
The bolt doesn't strike the ships directly-instead, it explodes in the sky above 
the fleet, spreading like a web of electrical fury across the entire harbor.
Then the storm begins.
 
WIND
The wind hits first-not gradually building, but instantly. Zero to hurricane 
force in seconds. The calm night air becomes a screaming gale, 100+ mph 
winds hammering Flotsam harbor from every direction simultaneously.
The Dragon Army warships, peacefully at anchor moments before, are 
suddenly battered by impossible winds. Masts creak, then groan, then begin to 
snap. Sails that were furled tear loose and shred instantly. Anchor chains 
strain against the sudden force.
Men on deck watch are blown off their feet, some swept overboard 
immediately. Lanterns extinguish or crash, spreading fire. Alarm bells begin 
ringing-chaotic, panicked.
 
RAIN
The rain comes next-not drops, but sheets. Torrential, blinding, impossible 
amounts of water falling from the sky. Visibility drops to near zero. The harbor 
becomes a churning mess of wind-driven rain and spray.
Below decks, sleeping sailors wake to the sound of apocalyptic weather. Water 
begins pouring through any opening-hatches, gun ports, damaged sections. 
The ships are being drenched, weighted down, pushed and pulled by forces 
beyond anything natural.
 
LIGHTNING
Then the lightning. Bolt after bolt, striking masts, rails, water. The harbor is 
illuminated in strobing flashes-blue-white light revealing scenes of chaos and 
terror. Sailors scrambling on deck, trying to secure lines or abandon ship. 
Officers shouting orders that can't be heard over the wind.
One lightning bolt strikes the main mast of a warship-you can see it even 
from five miles away-and the entire mast explodes in splinters, crashing 
down onto the deck below, crushing anyone underneath.
 
THE SEA RISES
And finally, the sea itself responds to Zeboim's fury. Waves that should not 
exist in a harbor-ten feet, fifteen feet, twenty feet high-crash into the 
anchored ships. The vessels are driven against each other, hulls grinding, 
smashing, splintering.
Ships begin to drag anchor, pushed by wind and wave toward the shore, 
toward rocks, toward the docks. Some collide with each other-massive 
wooden hulls crashing together with the sound of thunder.
The first ship to founder is one of the smaller warships on the eastern edge of 
the fleet. A wave catches it broadside, the wind catches the broken rigging, and 
it simply capsizes. One moment it's struggling to stay upright, the next it's 
rolling over, men screaming as they're thrown into the churning water.
 
THE HARBOR IN CHAOS
From your position five miles away on the Stormbreaker, you can see the 
storm's terrible majesty. A circular area roughly one mile in diameter, 
centered on the Dragon Army fleet, is being subjected to the full fury of a 
hurricane compressed into a single hour.
Lightning flashes constantly. 
Wind screams. 
Rain blinds. 
Waves smash.
Ships are being driven onto the docks, onto rocks, onto each other. You see 
masts falling, hulls breaking, sails tearing. Men jumping into the water, trying 
to swim for shore through impossible conditions.
The Stormbreaker itself is affected peripherally-the wind is strong 
here, the waves higher than normal, rain beginning to fall-but nothing like 
the apocalyptic conditions in the harbor. Captain Andra has already ordered 
all hands to secure positions, and the ship rides the rough water confidently.
 
CYRUS WATCHES
The cleric stands at the bow, the Tempest Scepter still glowing in his hands, 
channeling divine power into the storm. His face is wet-rain or tears, you 
can't tell. His lips move in prayer, though you can't hear the words over the 
wind.
He's maintaining the storm, guiding it, ensuring it focuses on the ships rather 
than spreading to devastate the entire city. This is controlled fury, not blind 
destruction.
But it's still fury. And it's still killing people.
 
THE FLEET'S DESTRUCTION - FIRST 15 
MINUTES
3:00-3:15 AM:
Five ships have already capsized or broken apart completely. Their 
crews are in the water-some swimming desperately for shore (400-800 feet 
through storm conditions), some clinging to wreckage, some simply 
disappearing beneath the waves.
Three more ships have been driven onto rocks or the docks, their 
hulls shattered, taking on water rapidly. Men pour from below decks, 
abandoning ship in organized or panicked fashion depending on their officers.
The remaining seven ships are still afloat but heavily damaged-
masts broken, sails destroyed, hulls leaking, listing badly. They're being 
pushed inexorably toward shore or rocks by the wind and waves.
You can see patrol boats capsizing-the small craft have no chance in these 
conditions. The men aboard are thrown into the maelstrom.
On shore, Flotsam itself is in chaos. The city has woken to the sound of the 
storm. People pour into the streets, staring at the harbor in horror. Some 
brave souls (or foolish ones) are running toward the docks, trying to help 
sailors who make it to shore.
The Dragon Army garrison is mobilizing-you can see torches and 
lanterns moving in organized groups. But what can they do? Fight a storm? 
They're helpless, watching their fleet die.
 
KESSA SPEAKS
Over the wind, Kessa shouts: "It's working! The fleet is being 
destroyed!"
But her voice lacks triumph. She's watching men die, and even for a 
professional killer, this is different. This is wholesale destruction.
 
Do you:
1.	Continue watching in silence (bear witness to what you've 
unleashed)
2.	Check on Cyrus (see how he's holding up under the burden)
3.	Say something to Kessa (acknowledge the weight of this moment)
4.	Go below deck (you don't need to watch this)
5.	Something else?
The storm continues. The screaming wind. The crashing waves. The dying 
fleet.
Time remaining: 45 minutes of Storm's Fury.
2
Dec 9
CHECKING ON CYRUS
You move closer to Cyrus, fighting against the wind that's reached even 
the Stormbreaker. The cleric stands rigid at the bow, both hands gripping the 
Tempest Scepter, his entire body trembling with the effort of channeling 
divine power.
"Cyrus," you call over the wind. "Brother, are you alright?"
He doesn't respond immediately. His eyes are fixed on the harbor, on the 
destruction, on the flashes of lightning revealing scenes of chaos and death. 
Tears are streaming down his face, mixing with the rain and spray.
"I can feel them," he says hoarsely. "Every life that ends. Every soul 
that passes. Mishakal grants me awareness-not specifics, just... 
the weight. The numbers."
His grip tightens on the Scepter. "Seventy-three so far. Seventy-three 
men have drowned or been crushed. Most of them never woke up-
trapped below deck when their ships capsized. They died in their 
sleep, drowned in the dark."
He closes his eyes briefly. "Is that mercy or cruelty? That they never 
knew what killed them?"
 
THE STORM CONTINUES
Another massive wave crashes into a warship, and even from five miles away 
you can hear the terrible sound of wood splintering. The ship's hull cracks 
open, and it begins to sink rapidly.
Men pour from the hatches-some making it into the water, some trapped as 
the ship goes down.
Cyrus's body jerks slightly. "Eighty-one. Eighty-nine. Ninety-four."
He's counting. He's feeling each death as it happens.
"Cyrus, you don't have to-" you start, but he shakes his head.
"Yes, I do. If I'm going to kill them, I will WITNESS them. Every 
single one. I will know what this costs. I will carry their weight."
His voice cracks. "One hundred and twelve. One hundred and twenty-
three."
 
SURVIVORS REACHING SHORE
But it's not all death. Through the storm, you can see figures making it to 
shore-sailors who abandoned ship early, strong swimmers, lucky ones who 
found wreckage to cling to. They crawl onto the docks or the beach, collapsing, 
coughing up water, alive.
"Some are surviving," you point out. "Look-there, and there. 
They're making it."
Cyrus nods, his expression desperate for any comfort. "Yes. Yes, I can feel 
that too. Perhaps... perhaps three hundred have reached shore 
already. Maybe more. They're exhausted, injured, but alive."
Another ship breaks apart, its back snapping under the combined force of 
wind and wave.
"One hundred and forty-seven. One hundred and fifty-nine."
 
THE BURDEN OF DIVINE AWARENESS
You realize what's happening. Cyrus isn't just wielding Zeboim's power-he's 
experiencing it through Mishakal's lens. The storm goddess grants 
destruction; the healing goddess grants awareness. He's caught between two 
divine perspectives: the righteous fury and the tragic cost.
"Cyrus," you say firmly, gripping his shoulder. "You're not alone in this. 
I ordered this strike. I made this decision. The weight is mine as 
much as yours."
"No," Cyrus says, his voice strained but resolute. "You made the strategic 
decision. I'm executing it. I'm the one channeling the power that's 
killing them. This is MY burden to carry. And I accept it. I just... I 
need to feel it. To honor it. To remember."
He looks at you, rain and tears streaming down his face. "Promise me 
something, Johannes. Promise me that when we return to Haven, 
we'll tell Laurana exactly what this cost. Not just 'we destroyed the 
fleet.' The real number. Every life. So they know what was paid to 
stop this invasion."
"I promise," you say immediately.
"And promise me," he continues, his voice breaking, "that we'll do 
everything in our power to make sure those 3,000 deaths meant 
something. That they saved thousands more. That this wasn't just... 
senseless slaughter."
"I promise, Brother. On my honor. Their deaths will matter."
 
THE TURNING POINT - 3:30 AM
By now, the harbor is a scene of utter devastation:
Twelve of fifteen ships are completely destroyed-capsized, broken, or 
sunk. The water is choked with debris, wreckage, bodies.
The remaining three ships are clearly doomed-they're being driven 
inexorably toward the rocky shore, hulls breached, taking on massive amounts 
of water. Their crews are abandoning ship en masse, jumping into the storm-
tossed water and swimming desperately for land.
The shore is lined with survivors-hundreds of soaked, exhausted 
Dragon Army sailors who made it. Flotsam citizens are helping pull them from 
the water, despite the Dragon Army being an occupying force. Common 
humanity overrides politics in the face of disaster.
The Dragon Army garrison has given up trying to organize a military 
response and is instead focused on rescue-boats going out (carefully, in the 
edges of the storm), ropes being thrown, medics treating the survivors.
Cyrus's counting has become almost mechanical: "Four hundred and 
eighteen. Four hundred and thirty-two. Four hundred and fifty-
six."
But he also adds, desperately: "Eight hundred on shore. Maybe nine 
hundred. Nearly half have survived."
 
THE STORM'S END - 3:45 AM
As the storm approaches its one-hour duration, Cyrus speaks one final prayer:
"Mishakal, goddess of healing, receive these souls. They were 
soldiers of tyranny, but they were also sons, brothers, fathers. 
Grant them peace."
"Zeboim, Lady of Storms, your fury has been righteous. The fleet is 
broken. Let your waters now be still."
The Tempest Scepter's glow begins to fade. The storm doesn't stop instantly-
that would be unnatural-but it begins to diminish rapidly. The wind drops 
from hurricane force to merely strong. The rain lessens. The waves calm.
By 4:00 AM, the storm is gone. The harbor is eerily quiet except for the sounds 
of wreckage settling, survivors calling out, and rescue efforts continuing.
 
THE AFTERMATH
Dawn is still hours away, but the damage is clear:
The Dragon Army fleet: Completely destroyed. All fifteen warships are 
wrecked beyond any possibility of repair. Twelve are sunk or capsized. Three 
are beached and broken.
Casualties (Cyrus's final count):
*	Dead: 547 sailors and marines
*	Survived: Approximately 2,450
*	Missing/uncertain: Small number, likely drowned but not 
confirmed
The invasion of Ak-Thyln is impossible. The Dragon Army has lost its entire 
naval capability in this region. Thousands of soldiers are stranded in Flotsam 
with no ships, no equipment, and no way to continue their mission.
 
CYRUS COLLAPSES
The moment the storm fully ends and the Scepter's glow extinguishes 
completely, Cyrus's legs give out. You catch him before he hits the deck.
He's not unconscious-just utterly spent. Physically, mentally, spiritually 
exhausted.
"Five hundred and forty-seven," he whispers. "I felt every one. Every 
single one."
Then he looks up at you, his eyes red and haunted but also... resolved.
"But we saved Ak-Thyln. We saved the coastal cities. We stopped 
the invasion. It was worth it. It had to be worth it."
He's not asking for confirmation. He's telling himself. Trying to believe it.
"It was worth it, Brother," you say firmly. "And their sacrifice will be 
remembered."
Kessa appears, helping you support Cyrus. "Let's get him below. He needs 
rest."
Captain Andra approaches, her expression grim but 
respectful. "Commander, the mission is complete. The Dragon Army 
fleet is destroyed. Do you want to remain here, or shall we set 
course for Haven?"
 
What do you do?
1.	Depart immediately for Haven (before Dragon Army organizes, 
while chaos still reigns)
2.	Remain offshore briefly (observe the aftermath, gather any final 
intelligence)
3.	Send a message to Flotsam (to Lady Sharane, to "The Fishwife," 
confirming Elara is safe)
4.	Something else?
The mission is complete. The fleet is destroyed. Elara is safe. Lucien is dead.
But the cost weighs heavy on all of you.
1
Dec 9
DEPARTURE FOR HAVEN - 4:15 AM
"Set course for Haven immediately," you order Captain Andra. "Best 
possible speed. We need to be far from here before the Dragon 
Army sorts itself out."
Andra nods crisply. "Aye, Commander. We'll be underway within 
minutes."
She turns to her crew, barking orders. "Weigh anchor! Unfurl all sails! 
Helmsman, set course southwest by south-Haven, maximum 
speed! Move!"
The Stormbreaker comes alive with purposeful activity. Sailors scramble up 
the rigging, canvas drops and catches the wind, the anchor chain rattles up. 
Within five minutes, the ship is cutting through the water, putting distance 
between you and Flotsam.
 
BELOW DECK - CYRUS'S CABIN
You and Kessa help Cyrus below. He can walk, but barely-his legs are 
unsteady, his entire body trembling with exhaustion. You ease him onto his 
bunk.
"Rest, Brother," you say quietly. "You've done what needed to be 
done. Sleep now."
Cyrus nods weakly. "Five hundred and forty-seven," he murmurs 
again. "I need to remember the number. For the report. For 
Laurana. For... for myself."
His eyes are already closing. The combination of magical exertion, spiritual 
burden, and emotional exhaustion has drained him completely.
Within moments, he's asleep-not peaceful sleep, but the deep, dreamless 
sleep of someone pushed past their limits.
Kessa pulls a blanket over him. "He's going to carry this for the rest of 
his life," she says quietly.
"We all will," you reply. "But he carried the heaviest part. He felt 
every death."
"That's... that's a terrible gift," Kessa says. "To be aware like that. I 
kill people, but I don't FEEL it the way he did. I don't know if I 
could."
You look at the Tempest Scepter, now resting beside Cyrus's bunk, its glow 
completely extinguished. It looks like an ordinary staff now-no hint of the 
devastating power it just unleashed.
"Come on," you say. "Let's check on Elara, then get some rest 
ourselves. It's been a long night."
 
ELARA'S CABIN
You find Elara in a small passenger cabin, wrapped in blankets, a bowl of soup 
(mostly eaten) on the table beside her. She's awake, staring at the ceiling.
"Elara," you say gently, knocking on the open door. "How are you 
feeling?"
She sits up slowly. "Better. Warmer. Fed. Safe, for the first time in 
two weeks." She pauses. "I heard... something. Earlier. Like thunder, 
but sustained. And the ship was rocking more than normal. What 
happened?"
You exchange glances with Kessa. How much to tell her?
"The Dragon Army fleet," you say simply. "It no longer exists. A 
storm destroyed it."
Elara's eyes widen. "All of it? All fifteen ships?"
"All of it."
She processes this for a long moment. "And the sailors? The soldiers?"
"Many survived," Kessa says. "Maybe half. The rest..." She doesn't 
finish.
Elara closes her eyes. "So many deaths. Because of me."
"No," you say firmly. "Not because of you. Because the Dragon Army 
chose conquest. Because they held you hostage. Because they were 
sailing to invade and enslave thousands. What happened tonight 
saved far more lives than it cost."
"But it still cost lives," Elara whispers.
"Yes. And we'll carry that weight. But it was the right choice."
Elara nods slowly, not fully convinced but accepting it. "When will we 
reach Haven?"
"Three days, maybe four," Kessa estimates. "Depending on wind and 
weather. You'll be reunited with your mother soon."
Elara's expression softens at that. "I can't wait to see her. To hold her. 
To tell her I'm safe." She touches the silver locket at her neck. "Thank 
you. For everything. For saving me. For... for doing what you had to 
do."
"Rest," you tell her. "You're safe now. That's all that matters."
 
ON DECK - DAWN APPROACHES
You return to the deck as the first hints of dawn touch the eastern horizon. 
The Stormbreaker is making excellent speed, already 15-20 miles from 
Flotsam. Behind you, the sky above the city is still dark with residual storm 
clouds, slowly dissipating.
Captain Andra joins you at the rail. "We're clear, Commander. No 
pursuit-the Dragon Army has no ships left to pursue with. We're 
safe."
You nod, watching the sunrise.
"One hell of a night," Andra says quietly. "I've seen naval battles 
before. Fought in a few. But I've never seen anything like what 
Brother Cyrus did. That was... gods, that was divine wrath made 
manifest."
"He paid for it," you say. "In a way I don't think any of us can fully 
understand."
"But it worked," Andra says pragmatically. "The Dragon Army's 
invasion capability in this region is gone. Ak-Thyln is safe. The 
coastal cities are safe. And we have a Dragon Army Highlord's 
corpse, his intelligence, and a rescued hostage. By any measure, 
this operation was a complete success."
She's right. Tactically, strategically-it was a perfect operation.
But it doesn't feel like victory. It feels like necessity. Like survival. Like the 
grim reality of war.
 
THE VOYAGE HOME
The sun rises fully, illuminating the Stormbreaker as it sails southwest toward 
Haven. The sea is calm now, almost peaceful. Hard to believe that just hours 
ago, a divine storm was tearing ships apart.
Mission status:
*	Elara: Rescued, safe, recovering
*	Lucien: Dead, body and intelligence secured
*	Dragon Army fleet: Completely destroyed (15/15 ships wrecked)
*	Casualties: 547 dead, ~2,450 survived but stranded
*	Invasion: Prevented-Ak-Thyln and coastal cities saved
Party status:
*	Johannes: Exhausted but unharmed
*	Kessa: Weary, contemplative
*	Cyrus: Physically and spiritually drained, sleeping, will need time to 
recover
Assets acquired:
*	Cloak of Displacement (magical)
*	Ring of Protection (magical)
*	Lucien's strategic documents and maps
*	Command insignia and journal
*	~800 gold
*	Invaluable intelligence for Haven
 
THREE DAYS LATER - APPROACHING HAVEN
The voyage is uneventful. The Stormbreaker makes good time, the weather 
favors you, and no Dragon Army assets intercept (how could they?).
Cyrus gradually recovers. He emerges from his cabin after the first day, 
moving slowly, looking haunted but functional. He spends hours in prayer, 
speaking to both Mishakal and Zeboim, seeking peace with what he did. The 
number "five hundred and forty-seven" is burned into his memory-he 
mentions it often.
Elara grows stronger. With food, rest, and safety, she begins to look more 
like herself. She spends time on deck, watching the sea, clutching her 
grandmother's locket. She asks about her mother constantly-How is she? 
Does she know I'm safe? When will I see her?
Kessa remains steady. The professional mask never fully comes down, but 
you catch her staring at the horizon sometimes, lost in thought. She killed 
Lucien personally, witnessed the storm's destruction-even for someone 
trained to kill, this operation was intense.
You process everything. The decisions made, the lives saved, the lives lost. 
The weight of command. The reality that you ordered an attack that killed 547 
people-even if it saved thousands more.
On the third evening, as Haven comes into view on the horizon, Cyrus joins 
you at the rail.
"I've been thinking," he says quietly. "About Lucien's corpse. About 
the interrogation we can conduct with Speak with Dead."
"And?"
"I don't think I should be the one to question him," Cyrus admits. "I 
killed 547 of his men. I'm... not objective. Laurana should handle it, 
or someone from intelligence. Someone who can ask the right 
questions without emotion clouding judgment."
"Agreed," you say. "We bring the corpse to Laurana, along with all 
the documents and intelligence. Let Haven's professionals extract 
everything useful. That's not our role."
Cyrus nods with visible relief. "Good. I've done enough this week."
 
ARRIVAL AT HAVEN - EVENING, DAY 4
The Stormbreaker enters Haven's hidden dock as the sun sets. Word has 
already spread-scouts spotted you approaching, runners were sent ahead.
Commander Laurana Brightblade is waiting at the dock, along with a 
small group of officers and healers.
As you disembark, Laurana's eyes scan your group quickly: You, looking 
weary but intact. Kessa, professional as always. Cyrus, moving 
slowly, looking like he's aged ten years. And Elara, wrapped in a 
cloak, nervous but whole.
"Commander Constantinius," Laurana says formally. "Report."
"Mission successful, Commander," you reply. "Elara has been 
extracted and is unharmed. The Dragon Army fleet at Flotsam has 
been completely destroyed-all fifteen warships rendered 
unseaworthy. The invasion of Ak-Thyln has been prevented. 
Additionally, we eliminated Highlord Lucien and secured his body 
along with extensive intelligence materials."
Laurana's eyes widen slightly-the only visible sign of her surprise. "You... 
all of that? In one operation?"
"Yes, ma'am."
She looks at your group with something like awe. "That's... extraordinary. 
Come. We'll debrief fully, but first-" She gestures to the healers. "Get 
medical attention, food, rest. You've earned it."
Then she approaches Elara directly, her voice softening. "Lady Elara. Your 
mother has been beside herself with worry. She's in Haven, 
waiting. Would you like to see her?"
Elara's face transforms-hope, joy, tears. "Yes. Please. I need to see her."
Laurana smiles genuinely. "Come with me."
As Elara is led away toward an emotional reunion, Laurana turns back to 
you. "We'll debrief tomorrow morning. For now-rest. You've done 
exceptional work."
She pauses, then adds quietly: "And I'm sorry for whatever it cost you."
 
EPILOGUE - THE NEXT MORNING
The formal debriefing takes place in Haven's command center. You, Kessa, 
and Cyrus present the full operational report:
*	Infiltration of Tiamat's Wrath
*	Assassination of Highlord Lucien
*	Extraction of Elara
*	Destruction of the Dragon Army fleet via Tempest Scepter
*	Casualty estimates: 547 enemy dead, ~2,450 survived but stranded
Laurana listens carefully, taking notes, asking clarifying questions. When you 
present Lucien's corpse (still in the Bag of Holding), his equipment, and the 
intelligence documents, her tactical staff practically vibrates with excitement.
"This is a intelligence goldmine," one officer says, examining the 
maps. "Fleet dispositions, invasion timelines, command structure-
we can use this."
When Cyrus reports the casualty numbers-specifically that he was divinely 
aware of each death-Laurana's expression becomes somber.
"Brother Cyrus," she says gently. "What you did saved thousands of 
lives. Ak-Thyln, Kalaman, Tarsis-all those cities that would have 
fallen to Dragon Army invasion. The coastal peoples owe you a debt 
they'll never know they have."
"Five hundred and forty-seven," Cyrus says quietly. "That's the price."
"Yes," Laurana acknowledges. "And it's a price we'll honor. Every 
report, every record will include that number. We won't forget 
what it cost."

ELARA AND LADY SHARANE

with tears in her eyes.
"You brought my daughter home," she says, her voice breaking. "I don't 
have words. I don't have enough gold. I could never repay what 
you've done."
"We don't need repayment," you say simply. "Your daughter is free. 
That's enough."
Elara adds quietly: "They killed the man who held me captive. They 
destroyed the fleet that would have enslaved thousands. And they 
gave me a chance to live again. I'll never forget that."
Lady Sharane insists on providing a substantial reward: 2,000 gold 
pieces (split three ways: ~665 gp each), plus a standing offer of merchant 
contacts, intelligence network access, and future support.

The fight goes on.

OOC - Direction Discussion
I'm so glad you're enjoying it! And I completely understand both requests. Let 
me address them:
 
1. Fun, Lighter Adventure
Absolutely yes. We've been doing heavy, dark, morally complex missions for a 
while now. The party needs (and deserves) something lighter-a palate 
cleanser that's still engaging but doesn't carry the weight of hundreds of 
deaths and moral calculus.
Some ideas for lighter adventures:
*	Tournament/Competition Arc: Haven hosts games/contests 
(archery, magical duels, tactical challenges). Friendly rivalry, showcase 
skills, win prizes, meet interesting NPCs, no life-or-death stakes.
*	Festival/Celebration: A liberated town throws a festival. The party 
participates in festivities, solves a minor mystery (stolen prize pig?), 
helps with entertainment, maybe light combat against bandits trying to 
ruin things.
*	Treasure Hunt: Old map found, leads to forgotten cache. Classic 
dungeon delve with traps, puzzles, monsters-but no moral weight, just 
adventure for adventure's sake.
*	Diplomatic Mission Gone Silly: Escort duty or negotiation that goes 
comedically sideways. No betrayals or darkness, just chaos and 
problem-solving.
*	Help a Village: Small-scale problem (monster in the woods, cursed 
well, rivalry between families) that's important to locals but low-stakes 
for the party.
Which appeals to you? Or something else entirely?
 
2. Cyrus's Redemption Arc
You're absolutely right. Cyrus is in a dark, heavy place right now-carrying 547 
deaths on his conscience, questioning whether he's still worthy of Mishakal's 
grace, wondering if he's crossed a line he can't uncross.
That cannot be where his story stays.
Here's what I'm thinking for his redemption arc:
The Setup: Cyrus has saved thousands by killing hundreds. He did the right 
thing strategically, but it's tearing him apart spiritually. He needs to 
be shown-not just told-that his actions had meaning, that he's still worthy, 
that he can still heal and help.
Potential Redemption Path Ideas:
Option A: "The Lives You Saved"
*	Cyrus meets survivors from Ak-Thyln (the city that would have been 
invaded)
*	Families, children, elderly-people who are alive because the fleet never 
came
*	They don't know about the storm; they just know they're safe
*	Personal, tangible evidence that his sacrifice mattered
*	Maybe a child gives him a flower or drawing, completely innocent, 
unknowing
*	Emotional impact: "These people live because of what you did"
Option B: "Mishakal's Reassurance"
*	Divine vision or direct communication from Mishakal
*	She acknowledges his pain but affirms his righteousness
*	"You are still my servant. You are still worthy. Healing sometimes 
requires difficult choices."
*	Maybe she shows him an alternate timeline where he didn't call the 
storm-Ak-Thyln burning, thousands enslaved
*	Emotional impact: Divine validation that he's not damned
Option C: "The Unexpected Mercy"
*	Cyrus encounters one of the Dragon Army sailors who survived the 
storm
*	The sailor was a conscript, forced into service, grateful to be alive and 
free
*	Says something like "That storm saved me. I was going to desert but 
they'd have killed my family. Now I'm 'lost at sea' and I can go home."
*	Emotional impact: Not everyone who survived is angry; some were 
freed by the chaos
Option D: "The Greater Healing"
*	Cyrus performs a major act of healing that only he could do
*	Saves a life (or many lives) in a way that reaffirms his identity as healer 
first, warrior second
*	Maybe uses the same divine power that counted deaths to now count 
lives saved
*	Emotional impact: "You are still who you were. You can still heal."
Option E: Combination/Something Else
*	Mix elements from above or create something entirely different
 
My Recommendation:
Short term (next session): Light adventure that gives the party (especially 
Cyrus) a break from heavy moral weight. Tournament, festival, treasure 
hunt-something fun.
Medium term (following session): Cyrus's redemption arc. My 
preference is Option A or C-something human-scale and tangible. Having 
Cyrus meet the people he saved (or a soldier he "freed") feels more grounded 
and powerful than divine reassurance.
Long term: Continue the main campaign plot (Dragon Army, Johannes's 
patron quest, etc.) but with conscious inclusion of lighter moments and 
character development.

HAVEN - THREE DAYS AFTER DEBRIEFING
You've had time to rest, recover, and process the Flotsam operation. 
The Stormbreaker departed two days ago, Captain Andra taking her crew back 
to Ak-Thyln with news of the successful mission and thanks from Commander 
Laurana.
Elara and Lady Sharane left yesterday-returning to their estate with a 
resistance escort. Elara hugged each of you before leaving, her grandmother's 
locket gleaming at her throat. She's still processing everything, but she's alive 
and free.
Cyrus has been spending most of his time in Haven's small temple, praying 
extensively. He's functional-eating, sleeping, participating in daily life-but 
there's a heaviness to him that wasn't there before. He smiles less. He's 
quieter. The number "547" still haunts him.
Kessa has been keeping busy with training and equipment maintenance. She's 
attentive to Cyrus's state but doesn't push-she understands that some 
burdens take time.
You've been reviewing the intelligence from Lucien's documents, meeting with 
Laurana's staff, and managing the aftermath of the operation. The strategic 
impact is enormous-the Dragon Army's regional naval capability is gone, 
their invasion timeline disrupted, their command structure scrambled by 
Lucien's death.
 
UNEXPECTED VISITOR
It's mid-afternoon when a runner finds you in Haven's common 
area. "Commander Constantinius? There's a dwarf at the main gate 
asking for you specifically. Says his name is Thordin Ironhelm. 
Says you'll want to hear what he has to say."
The name doesn't ring any bells. You've met dwarves before, but no one 
named Thordin.
"Did he say what he wants?"
"No, sir. Just that it's 'a matter of professional interest to skilled 
operatives.' Those were his exact words."
Curious. You gather Kessa and Cyrus and head to the gate.
 
THORDIN IRONHELM
The dwarf waiting at Haven's entrance is impressive even by dwarven 
standards.
Thordin Ironhelm stands about 4'8", built like a brick wall, with a 
magnificent braided beard shot through with silver. He wears well-made 
traveling clothes, carries a warhammer at his belt, and has the bearing of 
someone who's seen serious action. His eyes are sharp, intelligent, assessing.
When he sees you approach, he nods respectfully. "Commander 
Constantinius? Kessa Darrow? Brother Cyrus? Good. Wasn't sure 
the descriptions I was given were accurate, but you match."
His voice is gravelly, confident. This is not a dwarf who wastes time with 
pleasantries.
"I'm Thordin Ironhelm, master delver and expedition leader. I'm 
here because I have a job that requires people with very specific 
skills: tactical thinking, combat proficiency, willingness to work in 
dangerous conditions, and-most importantly-discretion."
He looks at each of you in turn. "I've been asking around Haven for a 
skilled team. Your names came up more than once. Apparently 
you've done some impressive work recently."
Kessa's eyes narrow slightly. "What kind of job?"
Thordin grins. "The profitable kind. And before you ask-no, it's not 
resistance business. This is personal. Private. And it pays 
extremely well for relatively little risk compared to, say, infiltrating 
Dragon Army flagships or storming fortresses."
He clearly knows more about your recent activities than you'd expect a 
random dwarf to know.
"Interested?"
 
THE PROPOSITION
You invite Thordin into Haven's guest area-a private room where you can talk 
without being overheard.
Once seated, Thordin gets straight to business:
"I'm a professional delver. I explore old ruins, forgotten tombs, 
collapsed mines-places most people won't go. I find valuable 
things, I sell them, I make a good living. It's dangerous work, but 
I'm good at it."
He pulls out a worn map and spreads it on the table.
"Three weeks ago, I was contracted by a collector in Palanthas to 
locate a specific artifact: the Helm of Kharas. It's a dwarven relic from 
before the Cataclysm-ceremonial armor worn by Kharas, one of our greatest 
heroes. Historical value, religious significance, worth a fortune to the right 
buyer."**
He taps a location on the map-mountainous terrain, maybe 80 miles 
northeast of Haven.
"I tracked it to here: the ruins of Thoradin's Hall, an abandoned 
dwarven outpost that collapsed during the Cataclysm. The Helm is there. I'm 
certain of it. Problem is..."**
He pauses, choosing his words carefully.
"I need help getting it out. The place is structurally unstable, 
partially flooded, and inhabited by things that don't appreciate 
visitors. I'm good, but I'm not suicidal. I need a team."
Cyrus asks: "Why us specifically? There are other skilled fighters in 
Haven."
Thordin nods. "Fair question. Three reasons: First, you're skilled but 
not well-known outside resistance circles. This needs to stay 
quiet-my client doesn't want word spreading that the Helm is on 
the market. Second, you're not local dwarves who might have... 
complicated feelings about looting dwarven ruins. Third, you've 
proven you can handle high-risk operations and keep your mouths 
shut."
He leans forward. "Here's my offer: You help me retrieve the Helm 
from Thoradin's Hall. In exchange, you get 30% of the payment I 
receive from my client-that's 3,000 gold pieces, split however you 
want. Plus, anything else we find in the ruins is yours to keep. I 
only want the Helm."
"Timeline: Three to five days total. One day travel there, one to 
three days in the ruins depending on complications, one day back. 
Relatively low political stakes-no Dragon Army, no mass 
casualties, just professional dungeon delving."
He sits back. "So. Interested?"
 
ASSESSMENT
Kessa looks at you, eyebrow raised. This is clearly your call.
Cyrus seems... cautiously interested. A straightforward treasure recovery 
mission with no moral complexity might be exactly what he needs right now.
The money is substantial. 3,000 gold split three ways is 1,000 each-a 
significant payday for less than a week's work.
And Thordin seems legitimate. Gruff, professional, knows his business.
But there are always complications with "simple" jobs.
 
What do you do?
1.	Accept the job - Sounds like exactly what the party needs right now
2.	Ask more questions - What specific dangers? What else is in the 
ruins? Why the secrecy?
3.	Decline politely - Not interested in mercenary work
4.	Negotiate terms - Want more money, different split, or other 
conditions
5.	Something else?
Thordin waits patiently for your answer, his hands folded on the table.
Any thoughts, guys?
Dec 9
PARTY DISCUSSION
You turn to Kessa and Cyrus. "What do you two think?"
Kessa speaks first, her tone analytical: "It's straightforward work. No 
politics, no armies, no moral calculus about who deserves to die. 
We go in, navigate whatever dangers are there, grab the artifact, 
get paid. Clean."
She looks at Thordin directly. "My questions: What kind of 'things that 
don't appreciate visitors' are we talking about? Monsters? Traps? 
Rival delvers? And what makes the structure unstable enough that 
you need backup but not so unstable that we're risking burial?"
Thordin nods approvingly at the questions. "Smart. The 'things' are 
primarily darkmantles and what I believe is a grick colony in the 
lower levels. Cave predators, territorial but not organized. Traps 
exist but they're three centuries old-most are degraded, 
predictable. No rival delvers that I know of, but it's possible."
"As for structural stability: the place won't collapse randomly. But 
there are flooded sections, weakened supports, areas where heavy 
combat or explosive magic could cause problems. I need people 
who can handle threats efficiently without bringing the ceiling 
down."
 
Cyrus has been quiet, listening carefully. Now he speaks, his voice thoughtful:
"Johannes, I'll be honest-I think this is exactly what I need right 
now."
He looks at Thordin, then back to you. "A straightforward challenge. 
Solve problems, overcome obstacles, help someone accomplish a 
legitimate goal. No one dies except monsters that were going to kill 
us anyway. No weighing innocent lives against strategic necessity."
His expression is almost... hopeful? Like he's grasping for something normal, 
something that feels like adventuring instead of war.
"I'm not running from what I did in Flotsam," he clarifies. "But I 
need... I need to remember that I'm more than just the person who 
called that storm. I need to use my skills for something that doesn't 
end with me counting corpses."
He looks directly at you. "If you think it's worth doing, I'm in. If you 
have concerns, I'll listen. But... I want this."
 
Kessa adds: "Plus, 1,000 gold each is nothing to sneeze at. We've 
been taking resistance missions that pay in gratitude and strategic 
value. Having actual coin for equipment, supplies, or just... 
having-that's useful."
She leans back. "I don't see major red flags. Thordin's story checks 
out. The job is dangerous but manageable. The pay is fair. And 
honestly? Some old-fashioned dungeon crawling sounds pretty 
good right now."
 
Thordin watches the exchange with interest but doesn't pressure. He's letting 
you discuss it naturally.
What's your call, Johannes?
We can leave now...
Dec 9
DEPARTURE - IMMEDIATE
"We can leave now," you say decisively. "We're equipped, rested, and 
ready. No point waiting around."
Thordin grins broadly. "Now that's what I like to hear. Professional 
and efficient." He stands, rolling up the map. "We can resupply in 
Gateway if we need anything specific, but if you're already geared 
up, we'll make better time pushing straight through."
Kessa nods approvingly. "I'll grab my pack and weapons. Five 
minutes."
Cyrus stands as well, and for the first time in days, there's energy in his 
movement. "I'll let Laurana know we're taking a short contract. She 
should know we're leaving Haven."
 
BRIEF WITH LAURANA
You find Commander Laurana in the command center, reviewing reports. 
When you explain the situation-Thordin's offer, the dwarven relic recovery, 
three to five days-she listens carefully.
"A dungeon delve for a dwarven artifact," she says, a slight smile 
touching her lips. "Honestly, Commander, that sounds almost... 
refreshing. You've earned some time doing straightforward 
adventuring work."
She glances at Cyrus, noting the cautious hope in his expression, and her tone 
softens. "Brother Cyrus, this will be good for you. Sometimes the 
best medicine is remembering what you're capable of beyond the 
battlefield."
To you, she adds: "Keep your Sending Stone active. If an emergency 
arises, I'll contact you. Otherwise, take your time. Haven isn't going 
anywhere, and the Dragon Army is still licking its wounds from 
Flotsam. You've bought us breathing room."
"We'll be back in less than a week," you confirm.
"Safe travels. And try to have some fun-you've earned it."
 
DEPARTURE FROM HAVEN - AFTERNOON
Within thirty minutes, you're packed and ready. The party assembles at 
Haven's gate:
Johannes:

THE JOURNEY NORTHEAST - DAY 1
The four of you set out on foot, heading northeast from Haven into 
increasingly mountainous terrain. The weather is clear, the trail is decent, and 
Thordin sets a steady pace.
As you walk, Thordin shares more details:
"Thoradin's Hall was built about 400 years ago as a forward 
outpost-combination waystation, mining operation, and defensive 
position. It was never huge-maybe 200 dwarves at peak 
occupancy. When the Cataclysm hit, the mountain shifted. Half the 
complex collapsed, the rest was abandoned."
"Why was the Helm there?" Cyrus asks.
"Kharas himself never set foot in Thoradin's Hall," Thordin 
explains. "But his Helm was given as a ceremonial gift to the 
outpost's commander-Thoradin, obviously-about fifty years 
before the Cataclysm. It's been sitting in the ruins ever since, 
assumed lost."
"How did you track it down?" Kessa asks.
Thordin taps his temple. "Research. Old records, survivor testimonies, 
connecting dots. Took me three months of digging through 
archives in Thorbardin. But I'm certain it's there-in the 
commander's vault, in what's now the deepest accessible level of 
the ruins."
 
EVENING CAMP - FIRST NIGHT
You make camp in a sheltered valley as the sun sets. Thordin proves to be an 
efficient camp-maker-he has the fire going and a decent stew cooking within 
minutes.
As you eat, the dwarf studies the three of you.
"So," he says conversationally, "I heard rumors about Flotsam. 
Something about a freak storm destroying the entire Dragon Army 
fleet. Fifteen ships, all wrecked in one night."
He looks at Cyrus specifically, though his tone remains casual. "Must've 
been some storm."
Cyrus stiffens slightly, but Thordin continues before anyone can respond:
"I'm not asking for details. Your business is your business. But I 
will say this: whoever managed that-however they managed it-
saved a lot of lives. Ak-Thyln, Kalaman, half the coastal cities. 
Those people will never know how close they came to Dragon Army 
occupation."
He raises his mug. "To the unknown heroes who stop invasions. May 
their burdens be light and their sleep peaceful."
It's clearly directed at Cyrus, but framed in a way that requires no confession, 
no discussion. Just acknowledgment.
Cyrus hesitates, then raises his own mug, his voice quiet: "May their 
sacrifices matter."
You all drink.
 
APPROACHING THORADIN'S HALL - LATE 
MORNING, DAY 2
By mid-morning of the second day, you reach the site.
Thoradin's Hall is built into the mountainside-or what's left of it. The 
entrance is a massive carved archway, now partially collapsed, with dwarven 
runes along the frame. Beyond, you can see darkness, broken stone, and the 
remnants of what was once an impressive structure.
The area around the entrance is overgrown with mountain scrub. There are 
old campsites-other delvers, adventurers, scavengers over the centuries-but 
nothing recent. The place has an abandoned, forgotten feel.
Thordin pulls out climbing gear and starts distributing rope. "Right. From 
here, it gets technical. The main entrance is stable enough, but 
once we're inside, we'll be navigating collapsed passages, flooded 
chambers, and vertical shafts. Stay together, watch your footing, 
and listen when I tell you something's dangerous."
He looks at each of you seriously. "This isn't a combat mission. This is 
exploration, problem-solving, and careful movement. Speed is less 
important than not dying. Clear?"
Everyone nods.
"Good. Let's go get that Helm."
 
ENTERING THORADIN'S HALL
You light lanterns (and Cyrus dons his Goggles of Night for darkvision), and 
the four of you step through the ancient entrance into the darkness beyond.
The air inside is cool, damp, and stale. Your footsteps echo. The architecture is 
distinctly dwarven-solid, geometric, built to last. But time and catastrophe 
have taken their toll. Rubble blocks passages, water drips from cracks, and 
everything is coated in dust and moss.
Thordin leads with confidence, marking passages with chalk, checking 
structural integrity before proceeding.
"The commander's vault is three levels down," he explains. "We'll 
need to navigate the main hall, descend through the old barracks 
level, bypass the flooded mining section, and reach the 
administrative level where the vault is located. Should take most of 
the day if we're careful."
Kessa is scouting ahead slightly, checking for traps or unstable ground. "I see 
tracks here-something's been moving through recently. Clawed, 
four-legged, medium-sized."
Thordin nods. "Darkmantles, probably. They nest in places like this. 
Not aggressive unless provoked, but they'll defend territory. We 
might have to fight."
You grip your Trident of Warning, feeling its magic alert you to potential 
danger ahead.
The adventure has begun.
 
What's your approach as you proceed deeper?
1.	Thordin leads, you follow his expertise (trust the professional 
delver)
2.	Kessa scouts ahead aggressively (find threats before they find you)
3.	Proceed as a tight group (maximum defensive formation)
4.	Something else?
The darkness stretches ahead, and somewhere deep below, the Helm of 
Kharas waits.

THORDIN'S ASSESSMENT
You whisper to Thordin: "Is it safer to take them out now, or would 
fighting draw more unwelcome attention?"
Thordin studies the darkmantles carefully, his experienced eye evaluating the 
situation.
"Good question. Here's my read: Darkmantles are territorial but 
not pack hunters-they don't call for help. If we kill these three, 
we're done with them. They won't alert anything else."
He pauses, considering. "The danger is the NOISE of fighting. A quick, 
quiet kill is fine. But if there's a lot of crashing around, spell 
explosions, creatures shrieking as they die... that could wake up the 
grick colony deeper down. And trust me, you don't want to deal 
with gricks unless you have to."
Kessa whispers: "I can drop one silently with my bow before it knows

Thordin nods. "Aye. Fast and quiet. Don't let them get into the air

Cyrus adds quietly: "I can use Sacred Flame if needed-it's radiant 
damage, not explosive. Relatively quiet. Or I can heal if someone 
gets grabbed."
 
Tactical assessment:
PROS of killing them now:
*	Clear the path, no threat on return journey
*	Prevents ambush if we retreat this way
*	Darkmantles won't alert other creatures
CONS of killing them:
*	Combat noise might attract gricks from deeper levels
*	Risk of one escaping and causing problems later
*	Uses some resources (spell slots, ammunition)
PROS of sneaking past:
*	No combat noise at all
*	Saves resources for deeper threats
*	Faster progress
CONS of sneaking past:
*	They'll still be here when we return (potential ambush on exit)
*	Risk of failed stealth check triggering combat anyway
*	Leaves hostile creatures at our back
 
Thordin adds one more thought: "My experience? Kill them now if you

ELDRITCH BLAST - NOISE ASSESSMENT
Good question. Let's think about this:
Eldritch Blast mechanically has no verbal or somatic components (it's just a 
cantrip you can cast at will), but narratively it's a beam of crackling eldritch 
energy.
Thordin's assessment:
"Eldritch magic? Depends on how you cast it. If it's a quiet beam-
like a focused lance of energy-that's fine. If it CRACKS like 
lightning or BOOMS when it hits, that's loud."
He looks at you. "How does yours manifest? Some warlocks I've seen 
shoot silent shadow beams. Others blast with thunder-crack force. 
What's yours like?"
 
This is actually your call, Johannes. How have you been 
manifesting your Eldritch Blast?
Given your patron is a demon and you're a Fiend warlock, it probably has 
some hellish or dark quality to it. But the sound level is flexible.
Possible manifestations:
1.	Silent/Quiet: Dark purple-black beam that impacts with a dull thud 
(like being punched)
2.	Moderate: Crackling dark energy with a hiss/sizzle sound on impact
3.	Loud: Booming infernal blast with explosive impact
For purposes of this situation, I'd say:
*	Options 1-2 are "quiet enough" - won't alert distant creatures
*	Option 3 is "loud" - would risk attracting gricks
What's your Eldritch Blast like?
1.	The descriptions in the past have usually include that kind of vibe.

GRICKS - CREATURE KNOWLEDGE
Gricks are aberrations-worm-like predators that hunt in underground 
environments.
What you know (general knowledge):
Appearance:
*	8 feet long, serpentine body
*	Rubbery, stone-gray skin
*	Tentacled mouth with a sharp beak at the center
*	Move like snakes but can rear up to strike
Behavior:
*	Pack hunters, ambush predators
*	Detect prey through vibration and scent
*	Territorial, defend their hunting grounds aggressively
*	Not particularly intelligent but cunning hunters
Combat capabilities:
*	Tentacle attacks (reach, can grapple)
*	Beak bite (nasty damage if they get hold of you)
*	Stone Camouflage - blend into rocky environments, hard to spot 
when still
*	Damage Resistance - Their rubbery hide is resistant to non-magical 
physical damage (swords, arrows, etc. do half damage unless magical)
Weaknesses:
*	Vulnerable to magic (spells work normally)
*	Magical weapons bypass their resistance
*	Fire and radiant damage are particularly effective
*	Not very smart-can be outmaneuvered tactically
 
YOUR PARTY'S ADVANTAGES:
*	Johannes: Eldritch Blast (magical force damage, full effectiveness) +

*	Thordin: Likely has magical warhammer or knows to use magic

TACTICAL PLAN REVIEW
You lay out the plan to the group:
"I'll swim through first with the Cloak and one end of Kessa's Rope 
of Entanglement. When I reach the far side, I'll take off the Cloak 
and send it back on the rope. Each person uses the Cloak to swim 
through one at a time-those who've crossed establish a defensive 
position while we transfer the others. Kessa goes last since she's 
controlling the rope."
 
TEAM ASSESSMENT
Kessa nods immediately. "Smart. The Rope can extend up to 30 
feet and I can command it to pull or guide. So I send it through with 
you, you secure the far end, then I command it to return with the 
Cloak. Each person clips the Cloak on, I command the rope to guide 
them through, they unclip and send it back. Efficient."
Cyrus considers. "Defensive positioning on the far side makes 
sense-we don't want everyone emerging into an ambush. And 
staggering the crossings means if something attacks, we're not all 
trapped in the water at once."
Thordin strokes his beard thoughtfully. "It's solid. My only concern 
is the transfer time. Each person needs to don the Cloak, swim 
through, remove it, send it back-that's maybe two minutes per 
person? So eight to ten minutes total for all four of us?"
He glances back the way you came. "That's not too long. But it does give 
the gricks time to notice what we're doing. If they're smart, they 
might try to attack during the transfer when we're split."
Kessa shrugs. "Then those of us on the far side defend while the 
transfer completes. Better than everyone swimming through blind 
and hoping for the best."
 
ALTERNATIVE CONSIDERATION
Cyrus offers: "I could ritual cast Water Breathing on all of us. 
Takes ten minutes, but then we all swim through together as a 
coordinated unit. No splitting the party, no vulnerable transfer 
window."
The trade-off:
*	Your plan: Faster initial start (2 minutes to get first person through), 
but 8-10 minutes total, party split during transfer
*	Water Breathing ritual: 10 minutes of waiting before anyone goes, 
but then everyone crosses together in ~30 seconds
Thordin's tactical assessment: "Both work. Your way is faster to get 
eyes on the far side-you'll know what we're dealing with in two 
minutes instead of ten. The ritual is safer overall but gives the 
gricks more time to prepare and makes us sitting ducks for ten 
minutes while we cast."
He looks at you. "Your call, Commander. You're the one who's proven 
you can handle high-risk operations."
 
ADDITIONAL DETAIL - THE FLOODED PASSAGE
Thordin shows you where the passage enters the water. "It's about twelve 
feet deep here, and the ceiling is just a foot or two above the water 
surface. Once you're in, you're fully submerged. The passage runs 
straight for about forty feet, then angles up-the far side emerges 
into a chamber that should be dry."
"Should be dry?" Kessa asks.
"It was dry when I scouted this three months ago. But water levels 
can change. Worst case, the far chamber is also flooded, but I 
doubt it-the administrative level was built higher, deliberately 
above flood risk."
 
So your options:
OPTION A: Your Cloak Transfer Plan
*	Johannes scouts ahead now (2 minutes)
*	Establish beachhead on far side
*	Transfer others one at a time (8-10 minutes total)
*	Pros: Fast initial intel, defensive positioning, flexible response
*	Cons: Party split during transfer, vulnerable window
OPTION B: Water Breathing Ritual First
*	Wait 10 minutes while Cyrus casts
*	Everyone swims through together (30 seconds)
*	Pros: Party stays together, coordinated assault capability, no transfer 
vulnerability
*	Cons: 10 minutes stationary, gricks have more prep time, no advance 
intel
OPTION C: Hybrid
*	Johannes scouts NOW with Cloak (2 minutes)
*	While you're gone, Cyrus starts ritual (10 minutes)
*	By the time you return with intel, ritual is done
*	Everyone swims through together based on your scout report
*	Pros: Get intel AND coordinated crossing
*	Cons: If you encounter trouble during scout, party can't help for 10+ 
minutes
 
What's your decision?
C

Visibility underwater is poor-maybe 20 feet with your Devil's Sight, but the
