AFTERMATH - UNDERWATER CHAMBER
You float in the murky water, breathing easily thanks to the Cloak, surrounded 
by settling ichor and sediment. Both gricks are dead. The ambush that would 
have caught your companions has been completely neutralized.
Combat Summary:
*	Duration: ~12 seconds (2 rounds)
*	Damage taken: 10 HP (66/76 remaining)
*	Resources used: Hex (still active, can be moved), 4 Eldritch Blast 
beams (cantrip), 1 melee attack
*	Result: Complete tactical success
Your Trident of Warning's magic pulses once-confirming no additional 
immediate threats nearby.
 
SCOUTING THE FAR CHAMBER
With the threats eliminated, you swim forward through the passage, ascending 
the angled section where Grick #2 had been positioned.
You break the surface.
The Administrative Level - Dry Chamber:
The passage emerges into a chamber that is indeed mostly dry, just as Thordin 
predicted. Water fills the lower 3-4 feet, but above that is open air-stale, 
damp, but breathable.
What you see:
The chamber is roughly 40 feet across, with a vaulted ceiling about 
20 feet high. Carved pillars support the roof. The architecture is distinctly 
administrative-desks (long since rotted), filing cabinets (rusted and fallen), 
what might have been a reception area.
Three doorways lead out:
*	Left: A corridor heading deeper into the administrative section (dark, 
unknown)
*	Center: Larger double doors, partially ajar, with dwarven runes above 
them reading "COMMANDER'S VAULT" (your destination!)
*	Right: Another corridor, collapsed about 20 feet in (blocked)
Additional observations:
Bioluminescent fungi grows along the walls and ceiling, providing dim 
blue-green light. It's beautiful in an eerie way-enough to see by, even without 
your Devil's Sight.
No immediate threats. The chamber appears empty. No gricks, no other 
creatures visible.
Signs of age: Everything is ancient, decayed, untouched for centuries. The 
water line on the walls shows the flooding is stable-it's been at this level for a 
very long time.
The Commander's Vault doors: Heavy bronze, weathered but intact. 
They're slightly open-maybe a foot gap. You can't see inside from your 
current position.
 
DECISION POINT
You've completed your scout. The intelligence is valuable:
Confirmed:
*	Two gricks were waiting in ambush (now dead)
*	The passage is clear
*	The far chamber is accessible and mostly dry
*	The Commander's Vault is here and appears accessible
*	No other immediate threats visible
Time check: You've been gone about 6-7 minutes. Cyrus has maybe 3-4 
minutes left on his Water Breathing ritual.
Your options:
1.	Return to the party now - Report findings, bring everyone through 
together once ritual completes (safest, coordinated approach)
2.	Wait here for 3-4 minutes - Let Cyrus finish the ritual, then guide 
them through when they arrive (maintains forward position)
3.	Investigate the Vault while waiting - You're here, the doors are 
open, you could peek inside (risky-what if there's a trap or guardian?)
4.	Check the left corridor quickly - Make sure there are no additional 
threats before bringing the party through (thorough but uses time)
5.	Something else?
The fungi-lit chamber is quiet except for the gentle lap of water against stone. 
The Vault doors stand slightly ajar, waiting.
What do you do?
1
Dec 10
RETURN TO THE PARTY
You've got the intel you came for. No need to push your luck solo-better to 
bring the team through and tackle the Vault together.
You take one last look around the chamber, committing the layout to memory: 
three exits, the Vault doors in the center, fungi providing light, water line 
stable at 3-4 feet.
Then you descend back into the flooded passage.
 
THE SWIM BACK
Swimming back through the passage is quick and uneventful. The two dead 
gricks drift in the current, ichor still clouding the water slightly, but they pose 
no threat now.
You cover the 40 feet in seconds, ascending the 12-foot rise, and break the 
surface at the entrance where you left your companions.
 
REUNION - REPORT
"Johannes!" Kessa calls out as you emerge, relief evident in her 
voice. "You're back. Everything alright?"
Cyrus is still seated cross-legged, hands folded, eyes closed-deep in the final 
stages of the ritual. His voice continues in a steady, rhythmic chant. Divine 
magic pulses faintly in the air around him.
Thordin offers you a hand up onto the dry stone ledge. "What did you 
find?"
You pull yourself out of the water, dripping. "Two gricks waiting in 
ambush-one in an alcove halfway through, one at the far end. I 
eliminated both. Passage is clear now."
Kessa's eyebrows raise. "You took out two gricks solo?"
"Surprise helped. First one never knew I was there. Second one got 
a hit in but went down fast." You touch your shoulder where the tentacles 
wrapped-it's bruised but not serious. "Ten damage, nothing critical."
Thordin grins broadly. "Well done! That saves us a nasty fight in 
confined space. What about the far side?"
"Exactly as you described-dry chamber, about three to four feet of 
standing water, but breathable air above. Three exits: left corridor 
into the administrative section, center is the Commander's Vault 
with doors partially open, right corridor is collapsed and blocked."
You describe the layout in detail-the fungi lighting, the apparent lack of 
additional threats, the bronze vault doors.
"No other gricks visible?" Thordin asks carefully.
"None that I could see. But there are other passages leading 
deeper. I didn't explore those-figured we should go together."
Thordin nods approvingly. "Smart. Never split the party more than 
necessary."
 
WATER BREATHING RITUAL COMPLETES
Cyrus opens his eyes and releases a long breath. The divine magic that had 
been building around him for the past ten minutes settles into place.
"The spell is ready," he announces, standing and stretching. "I can grant 
water breathing to all four of us for the next eight hours."
He moves to each of you in turn, touching shoulders and speaking brief 
prayers. You feel the magic settle over you-a cool, fluid sensation, like the 
water itself is welcoming you.
Water Breathing active on entire party (8 hours duration).
Cyrus looks at you. "You said you cleared the ambush? Well done. 
How are you feeling? Need healing?"
"I'm fine," you assure him. "Just some bruising. Save your magic for 
real emergencies."
 
CROSSING AS A GROUP
With Water Breathing active, the crossing becomes trivial:
"Stay together," you instruct as the group prepares to enter the 
water. "Follow my lead. The passage is straight for forty feet, then 
angles up. The two dead gricks are in there-don't be startled. We'll 
surface in the administrative chamber."
Everyone nods, checking weapons and equipment one last time.
Thordin: Warhammer ready, pack secured, moving with the confidence of 
someone who's done this before.
Kessa: Hand crossbow loaded, daggers accessible, moving with professional 
efficiency.
Cyrus: Holy symbol around his neck, goggles on for darkvision, looking 
focused and ready.
You lead the way into the dark water.
 
THE PASSAGE - GROUP CROSSING
The four of you descend and swim through together. With everyone able to 
breathe water freely, there's no panic, no rushing. It's almost peaceful-like 
exploring rather than infiltrating.
Kessa notes the dead gricks as you pass, giving you an impressed look. 
The evidence of your work is clear-massive holes punched through their 
bodies, ichor still settling.
Thordin examines the alcove ambush position, nodding in 
professional respect. "Good eyes, spotting that. Would've been nasty if 
we'd swum past without noticing."
The swim takes less than a minute. You ascend the angled passage and break 
the surface into the fungi-lit administrative chamber.
 
THE ADMINISTRATIVE LEVEL - FULL PARTY 
ARRIVAL
Everyone pulls themselves up onto the higher stone ledges above the water 
line (the chamber has about 3-4 feet of water covering the floor, but the desks 
and raised platforms are dry enough to stand on).
Thordin looks around with satisfaction, water dripping from his 
beard. "Just as I remember it. Well, a bit more decayed, but the 
bones are the same."
He points to the center doors-the Commander's Vault. "That's our target. 
The Helm of Kharas should be inside, probably in a display case or 
secure chest."
Kessa is already scanning for threats, her crossbow ready, eyes moving 
systematically across the chamber. "Left corridor-anything down there 
we need to worry about?"
"Didn't scout it," you admit. "Could be more gricks, could be clear. 
The Vault seemed like priority."
Cyrus moves to the Vault doors, examining them carefully. "These runes... 
they're protective wards. Very old, but still active. See the faint 
glow?"
He's right-there's a barely perceptible shimmer around the door frame. 
Magic that's endured three centuries.
Thordin nods. "Aye. The Commander wouldn't leave his treasures 
unguarded. The wards are probably keyed to dwarven blood or 
specific command words. But with time and patience, we can work 
around them."
He looks at the group. "Question is: do we secure the chamber first-
check that left corridor, make sure nothing's going to ambush us 
from behind-or do we go straight for the Vault?"
 
What's your priority?
1.	Clear the left corridor first (secure your position, eliminate threats 
before focusing on the Vault)
2.	Go straight to the Vault (that's why you're here, deal with threats if 
they emerge)
3.	Split up (some guard, some work on Vault-efficient but risky)
4.	Set watch while examining Vault (compromise-Kessa and 
Thordin on overwatch, you and Cyrus tackle the door)
5.	Something else?
The fungi-lit chamber waits, quiet except for the gentle lap of water. The Vault 
doors stand slightly ajar, promising treasure-and possibly danger.

Dec 10
SECURING THE PERIMETER
"We clear the corridor first," you decide firmly. "Last thing we need is 
gricks or something worse coming up behind us while we're 
focused on the Vault. We do this properly-secure the area, then 
retrieve the Helm."
Thordin nods approvingly. "Professional. I like it. Better to spend ten 
minutes clearing threats than ten seconds dying to an ambush."
Cyrus hefts his mace. "Agreed. Let's make sure we're alone down 
here."
Kessa is already moving toward the left corridor, crossbow raised. "I'll take 
point. Standard sweep formation?"
"Standard sweep," you confirm. "Kessa front, I'm right behind her, 
Cyrus and Thordin cover our flanks and rear. Call out anything 
suspicious."
 
THE LEFT CORRIDOR - INVESTIGATION
The corridor extends into darkness-your various vision enhancements 
(Devil's Sight, Goggles of Night, dwarven darkvision for Thordin) make 
navigation easy despite the lack of light.
The passage is carved stone, about 8 feet wide, 10 feet tall. Water 
covers the floor to about ankle-depth here (the administrative level slopes 
slightly). Side doors branch off-offices, storage rooms, perhaps living 
quarters for senior staff.
Kessa moves carefully, checking every doorway, every shadow.
Perception checks (group):
*	Johannes: 15 + 3 = 18
*	Kessa: Natural 20 + 7 = 27 (Exceptional)
*	Cyrus: 13 + 4 = 17
*	Thordin: 16 + 5 = 21
 
WHAT KESSA DISCOVERS
"Hold," Kessa whispers sharply, raising her fist. Everyone freezes.
She points to a doorway about 30 feet ahead on the right. "Movement. 
Something large. Breathing-I can hear it."
You listen carefully. She's right-there's a wet, rhythmic sound. Something 
alive. Something big.
Thordin whispers: "How big?"
Kessa considers. "Bigger than the gricks. Maybe... eight feet? Ten?"
Your Trident of Warning begins to tingle-not urgent alarm, but definite 
warning. Danger ahead.
 
TACTICAL APPROACH
The creature (whatever it is) is in a side room, apparently unaware of your 
presence. The door is partially open-maybe 2 feet gap.
Options:
1.	Ambush from doorway (position team, strike fast when you have 
surprise)
2.	Kessa scouts alone (she's stealthiest, can get eyes on target before 
committing)
3.	Announce presence (call out, give it a chance to respond-might not

4.	Bypass entirely (close/bar the door, deal with Vault, handle this on 
the way out)
5.	Something else?
Thordin whispers: "Could be a grick alpha-larger, tougher version. 
Could be something else that moved in after the Cataclysm. Your 
call, Commander."
Kessa adds quietly: "Whatever it is, it's between us and a clear exit. I 
vote we deal with it now."
What's your approach?

AMBUSH SETUP
"We hit it hard and fast," you whisper. "Ambush from the doorway. 
Kessa, can you see inside without alerting it?"
Kessa nods, already moving silently toward the partially open door. She 
positions herself at the edge, peering through the gap with professional care.
After a moment, she signals back with hand signs:
One creature. Large. Grick-like but bigger. Coiled. Sleeping or resting.
Thordin whispers: "Grick alpha. Tougher hide, more hit points, 
nastier bite. But if it's resting, we've got the advantage."
"Positions," you whisper. "Kessa, open the door on my mark and 
take the first shot. I'll hit it with Hex and Eldritch Blast. Cyrus, 
Sacred Flame. Thordin, be ready to charge if it survives the 
opening salvo."
Everyone nods, moving into position with practiced efficiency.
Kessa: At the door, hand on the handle, crossbow ready in the other 
hand. Johannes: Behind her, clear line of sight once the door 
opens. Cyrus: To the side, holy symbol ready. Thordin: Warhammer 
gripped, prepared to rush in.
You take a breath, focus on the door, prepare your Hex.
"Three... two... one... MARK."
 
SURPRISE ROUND - GRICK ALPHA AMBUSH
Kessa kicks the door fully open with a bang, her crossbow already raised.
Inside the room-a grick alpha. It's massive compared to the regular gricks, 
easily 12 feet long, thick as a barrel, coiled in the center of what was once an 
administrative office. It was indeed resting, but the door crash wakes it 
instantly.
Its tentacled head whips around, eyes (or sensory organs) focusing on the 
doorway-
Too late.
 
KESSA'S ATTACK (Surprise Round)
Hand Crossbow + Sneak Attack:
*	Attack roll: 18 + 7 = 25 (Hit, target surprised)
*	Damage: 1d6+4 + 3d6 (sneak attack) = 5 + 4 + 14 = 23 damage
The bolt punches into the grick alpha's body with a meaty thunk. The creature 
shrieks-a deep, resonant sound that echoes through the corridors.
 
JOHANNES'S ATTACK (Surprise Round)
You cast Hex on the creature as it rears up, dark energy coiling around it. 
Then you unleash Eldritch Blast.
Two beams (target surprised):
First beam:
*	Attack roll: 14 + 7 = 21 (Hit, auto-crit)
*	Damage: (1d10+4)×2 + 1d6 (Hex) = (7+4)×2 + 3 = 22 + 3 = 25 
damage
Second beam:
*	Attack roll: 16 + 7 = 23 (Hit, auto-crit)
*	Damage: (1d10+4)×2 + 1d6 (Hex) = (9+4)×2 + 4 = 26 + 4 = 30 
damage
Total: 55 damage
The twin beams of crackling energy HISS-CRACK through the doorway, 
slamming into the grick alpha's body. Massive holes tear through its rubbery 
hide, ichor spraying across the walls.
The creature roars in pain and fury, but it's still standing-these things 
are tough.
 
CYRUS'S ATTACK (Surprise Round)
"BURN!" Cyrus shouts, thrusting his holy symbol forward.
Sacred Flame (DEX save DC 15):
*	Grick Alpha DEX save: 6 + 1 = 7 (FAIL)
*	Damage: 2d8 radiant = 15 damage
Holy fire descends from above, engulfing the wounded grick alpha. Its hide 
blackens and blisters under the radiant assault.
Total damage in surprise round: 23 + 55 + 15 = 93 damage
The grick alpha is heavily wounded, ichor pouring from multiple wounds, 
burned by holy fire, but it's not dead yet. It thrashes violently, tentacles 
lashing, preparing to fight back.
 
INITIATIVE - ROUND 1
Roll Initiative:

The grick alpha is desperate, wounded, and furious. But you're all faster.

The creature is badly wounded but still dangerous. Its tentacles are extending

FINISHING BLOW - ELDRITCH BLAST
No need to get fancy. The creature is heavily wounded, and you have the range

You raise your hand and unleash another barrage of eldritch energy.
Eldritch Blast (2 beams at Hexed Grick Alpha):
First beam:
*	Attack roll: 12 + 7 = 19 (Hit)
*	Damage: 1d10+4 (EB) + 1d6 (Hex) = 8 + 4 + 5 = 17 damage
Second beam:
*	Attack roll: 15 + 7 = 22 (Hit)

Total: 29 damage
The twin beams CRACK-HISS through the doorway, punching into the grick

second strikes where body meets tentacled head.
The massive creature shudders violently, tentacles spasming, then-
It collapses.
The grick alpha crashes to the stone floor with a heavy THUD, ichor pooling 
rapidly around it. Its tentacles twitch once, twice, then go still.
Grick Alpha: DEAD
 
AFTERMATH - SECURING THE CORRIDOR
Silence falls over the corridor, broken only by the drip of water and your 
breathing.
Thordin steps forward cautiously, warhammer ready, and prods the corpse 
with his boot. It doesn't move.
"Dead," he confirms. "That was a grick alpha alright. Nasty piece of 
work. They're usually the colony leaders-tougher, meaner, 
smarter than the regular ones."
He looks at the group with genuine respect. "You lot took it down in one 
round of actual combat. That's... impressive. Very impressive."
Kessa is already reloading her crossbow. "Good ambush. Caught it 
completely off-guard." She looks at you. "Your opening strike 
basically crippled it before it could respond."
Cyrus examines the room briefly. "This was some kind of record-
keeping office. The alpha probably moved in because it's a large, 
secure space." He checks the corners and alcoves. "Looks clear 
otherwise."
 
CONTINUING THE SWEEP
You proceed down the corridor, checking the remaining rooms systematically:
Rooms found:
*	Storage chamber: Empty, some rotted furniture, nothing of interest
*	Office: Similar to the alpha's lair, abandoned for centuries
*	Small armory: Rusted weapons, corroded armor, nothing salvageable
*	Quarters: Personal rooms for administrators, long since decayed
The corridor ends at a collapsed section about 60 feet from where you 
started. Stone has caved in, completely blocking further passage. There's no 
way through without major excavation.
"Dead end," Kessa confirms. "Nothing else down here."
Thordin nods. "Good. That means the entire administrative level is 
secure except for the Vault itself. No more threats at our backs."
 
COMBAT SUMMARY - CORRIDOR SWEEP
Encounters eliminated:
*	2 gricks (underwater passage, solo)
*	1 grick alpha (administrative corridor, group)
Party status:
*	Johannes: 66/76 HP (10 damage from earlier grick)
*	Kessa: Full HP
*	Cyrus: Full HP
*	Thordin: Full HP
Resources used:
*	Hex (still active, can be moved or dismissed)
*	Multiple Eldritch Blasts (cantrips, unlimited)
*	1 Sacred Flame (cantrip, unlimited)
*	1 crossbow bolt (Kessa)
*	Water Breathing (ongoing, 7+ hours remaining)
Tactical assessment: Perfect execution on both fronts. Area secured with 
minimal resource expenditure.
 
RETURNING TO THE VAULT
The four of you return to the main chamber where the Commander's Vault 
awaits. The bronze doors stand slightly ajar, the ancient protective wards still 
shimmering faintly in your various vision modes.
Thordin approaches the doors carefully, examining them with a professional 
eye.
"Right. Now for the tricky part." He traces the runes with his finger, not 
quite touching. "These wards are designed to prevent forced entry. If 
we just push the doors open or try to break in, they'll trigger-
probably a shock, maybe an alarm, possibly something worse."
He strokes his beard thoughtfully. "The wards are old, though. Three 
centuries old. They're still active, but weakened. With the right 
approach, we might be able to bypass or disable them."
Cyrus steps forward. "I might be able to dispel the magic, or at least 
suppress it temporarily. Divine magic versus arcane wards-it's not 
guaranteed, but it's possible."
Kessa adds: "Or I could try to pick the lock mechanism directly, if 
there is one. Sometimes the physical lock is separate from the 
magical protections."
Thordin considers both options. "The dispel is safer but might fail. 
The lockpicking is riskier-if you trigger the wards, we all feel it. 
But if it works, we're in clean."
He looks at you. "Your call, Commander. You've led us this far 
without a misstep."
 
How do you want to handle the Vault doors?
1.	Cyrus attempts to Dispel Magic (ritual cast if needed, takes 10 
minutes but safer)
2.	Kessa picks the lock (faster but riskier if wards trigger)
3.	Thordin tries a dwarven command word (he knows some 
traditional phrases, might work)
4.	Examine the doors more thoroughly first (take your time, gather 
more info before deciding)
5.	Brute force (just push through and accept the consequences-not 
recommended)
6.	Something else?
The Vault doors wait, three centuries of protection still active, the Helm of 
Kharas presumably just beyond.
What's your approach?
4, then 3, then 1, then 2
Dec 10
METHODICAL APPROACH - VAULT DOORS
"We do this carefully," you say. "No rushing. We examine the doors 
thoroughly first, then try solutions in order of risk. Thordin's 
dwarven command words first since he knows the culture, then 
Cyrus's Dispel Magic, then Kessa's lockpicking if needed."
Everyone nods-it's a sensible, methodical approach.
"Let's start with a full examination. Everyone, look for anything 
unusual."
 
PHASE 1: THOROUGH EXAMINATION
The four of you spread out around the doors, examining them from every 
angle.
Investigation/Perception Checks:
*	Johannes: 16 + 3 = 19
*	Kessa: 18 + 7 = 25 (Excellent)
*	Cyrus (Arcana for magical elements): 17 + 4 = 21
*	Thordin (History/dwarven knowledge): Natural 20 + 5 
= 25 (Exceptional)
 
WHAT YOU DISCOVER:
Thordin (critical success) finds the key details:
"Ah! Here!" he exclaims, pointing to a section of runes near the door 
handle. "I know this pattern. This is a ward of lineage-it's keyed to 
dwarven blood, specifically to the Thoradin clan. But look here..."** He traces 
another set of runes. "There's an override phrase. A formal request 
protocol."
He grins. "The Commander wasn't just trying to keep thieves out-he 
was trying to keep unauthorized DWARVES out. This is military 
security, not tomb protection. There's a proper way to request 
entry."
 
Kessa's observations:
"The physical lock is integrated with the magical wards," she notes, 
examining the mechanism. "You can't pick one without triggering the 
other. But the good news is the lock itself is simple-it's the wards 
doing the heavy lifting, not complex tumblers."
She points to stress cracks around the door frame. "The doors have been 
slightly forced open at some point-see the gap? Someone or 
something pushed them partially open, but the wards stopped 
them from going further. That's why they're ajar now."
 
Cyrus's magical analysis:
"The wards are evocation-based," he explains. "Designed to deliver a 
shock-probably lightning or force damage-to anyone trying to 
force entry. The good news is they're significantly weakened after 
three centuries. I'd estimate maybe 4d6 damage instead of the 
original 8d6 or higher."
He studies the magical pattern. "Dispel Magic would work, but it's not 
guaranteed. The ward was cast at high level originally. I'd say... 
60% chance of success with a standard casting, maybe 80% if I 
ritual cast and take my time."
 
Your observations:
You notice the doors themselves are bronze-reinforced oak-incredibly 
durable. The hinges are dwarven engineering, still functional after centuries. 
The gap between the doors is about 8-10 inches-you can see darkness 
beyond, but not details.
More importantly, your Trident of Warning is not tingling. Whatever's 
inside the Vault, it's not an active threat waiting to ambush you.
 
PHASE 2: DWARVEN COMMAND WORD
"I'm going to try the formal request protocol," Thordin 
announces. "It's a long shot-I'm not Thoradin clan, and the 
Commander's been dead for centuries. But the wards might still 
recognize proper military procedure."
He straightens, adopts a formal military posture, and speaks in clear, resonant 
Dwarven:
"Commander Thoradin, I am Thordin Ironhelm, Master Delver of 
Thorbardin. I request entry to retrieve artifacts of our people on 
behalf of the living clans. I invoke the Right of Recovery under the 
Accords of Stone and Steel. Grant me passage."
 
The wards flare briefly-blue light racing along the runes.
For a moment, everyone tenses, ready for a blast of magical energy-
But then the light softens, turning from aggressive blue to a gentler amber.
The runes rearrange slightly, and ancient magical mechanisms click inside 
the doors.
The wards don't fully deactivate, but they... recognize the request.
A spectral voice-deep, authoritative, clearly dwarven-echoes from the doors:
"REQUEST ACKNOWLEDGED. LINEAGE VERIFICATION... 
FAILED. CLAN AFFILIATION... THORBARDIN, RECOGNIZED. 
PURPOSE... ARTIFACT RECOVERY, ACCEPTABLE."
A pause, then:
"CONDITIONAL ENTRY GRANTED. RESTRICTIONS: NO THEFT 
OF SACRED ITEMS. NO DESECRATION. TIME LIMIT: ONE HOUR. 
VIOLATE TERMS, WARDS ACTIVATE."
The doors swing open smoothly, revealing the darkened Vault beyond.
 
Thordin's jaw drops. "By the Forge... it actually WORKED. The 
ward recognized Thorbardin lineage and the formal protocol. It's 
treating us as legitimate military personnel on authorized 
business."
He looks at the group with a mixture of awe and relief. "We have one hour 
inside. We can take artifacts, but if we desecrate anything or steal 
sacred items, the wards will attack. The Helm of Kharas isn't 
sacred in the religious sense-it's historical. We should be fine."
Kessa grins. "So we just walked into a three-century-old vault by 
asking politely. I love it when the ancient security assumes good 
faith."
Cyrus looks thoughtful. "The dwarves who built this place never 
imagined it would be abandoned for centuries. They built it to keep 
out unauthorized access, not to seal it forever."
 
THE COMMANDER'S VAULT - INTERIOR
You step through the open doors into the Vault.
The chamber is roughly 30 feet by 30 feet, with a vaulted 
ceiling. Unlike the rest of the complex, this room is completely dry-the 
wards have kept water out entirely.
What you see:
Display cases line the walls, made of reinforced glass (or possibly crystal). 
Most are empty or contain items that have decayed (cloth, leather, documents 
turned to dust).
But some items remain intact:
*	A ceremonial warhammer in pristine condition, mounted on the far 
wall
*	Several pieces of jewelry in a case-rings, amulets, pins
*	A shield bearing the symbol of Thoradin's Hall
*	Documents in sealed crystal tubes-maps, orders, personal letters, 
all preserved
*	And on a central pedestal, illuminated by faint magical light:
The Helm of Kharas.
It's magnificent. Dwarven craftsmanship at its finest-steel worked with gold 
inlay, runes of protection and honor etched along the brow, wings extending 
from the sides in traditional dwarven style. It's slightly dust-covered but 
otherwise perfect, as if it was placed here yesterday rather than 280 years 
ago.
Thordin approaches it reverently, removing his own helmet. "There it is. 
The Helm of Kharas. One of the greatest artifacts of our people."
He doesn't touch it immediately-just stands, looking at it with profound 
respect.
 
The chamber is as you were told: one hour time limit, no 
desecration, artifact recovery is permitted.
What do you do?
1.	Thordin retrieves the Helm (that's what you came for)
2.	Examine other items (the warhammer, jewelry, documents-
anything else valuable?)
3.	Document everything (record what's here before taking anything)
4.	Take only the Helm and leave quickly (minimize time in the Vault)
5.	Something else?
You have one hour before the wards reactivate.
The items here are abandoned, right?
Dec 10
CLARIFYING THE SITUATION
Good question. You turn to Thordin for his assessment.
"These items-they're abandoned, right? No one's been here in 
centuries. No one's coming back for them."
Thordin considers carefully, his expression thoughtful.
"Technically, yes and no," he says slowly. "The outpost was 
abandoned during the Cataclysm-everyone either died or fled. For 
280 years, this place has been empty. No one from Thoradin's line 
survived to claim inheritance. No one from Thoradin's Hall ever 
returned."
He gestures to the Vault. "But dwarven law is complicated. These items 
belonged to the outpost, to Clan Thoradin, to the dwarven people 
as a whole. The Helm specifically was a ceremonial gift-it has 
historical and cultural significance."
"So taking them would be...?" Kessa prompts.
"Legally ambiguous," Thordin admits. "From one perspective, we're 
recovering lost artifacts of our people-that's legitimate salvage, 
especially since I'm a dwarf of Thorbardin acting in good faith. The 
ward recognized that and granted conditional entry."
"From another perspective," he continues, "some dwarven clans 
might argue these items should be returned to Thorbardin, to the 
appropriate authorities, not sold to private collectors or kept as 
personal loot."
He looks at the Helm, then at the other items.
"Here's what I know for certain: The Helm is my contract. I'm 
taking it to my client in Palanthas as agreed-that's legitimate 
artifact recovery, and I'm paying you for your help. That's clean."
"As for the other items..." He pauses. "The ward said 'no theft of 
sacred items.' The ceremonial warhammer might count as sacred-
it's a religious symbol. The documents are historical records, not 
sacred. The jewelry... probably personal effects, not sacred."
"The ward will judge based on intent and action. If we're taking 
items for preservation, recovery, or legitimate use-probably fine. 
If we're looting and desecrating-the wards will attack."
 
Cyrus offers his perspective:
"From a moral standpoint, these items have been abandoned for 
nearly three centuries. No one is coming back for them. Leaving 
them here means they'll eventually decay or be lost forever. Taking 
them-especially to preserve them or return them to dwarven 
hands-seems more respectful than leaving them to rot."
He looks at the documents in crystal tubes. "Those historical records, for 
instance, could be invaluable to historians and dwarven clans 
trying to understand what happened during the Cataclysm. Leaving 
them here serves no one."
 
Kessa's practical take:
"Look, we have an hour. We came for the Helm, that's priority one. 
If there are other items that are valuable, non-sacred, and serve a 
purpose being recovered-we take them. If the wards object, we'll 
know immediately and we stop."
She grins slightly. "Besides, the ward specifically said 'no theft of 
sacred items.' It didn't say 'don't touch anything else.'"
 
Thordin's final assessment:
"Here's my recommendation: We take the Helm-that's the 
mission. We take the historical documents-they're records, not 
treasure, and they belong in archives where people can learn from 
them. The jewelry and personal effects... we could take them and 
donate them to Thorbardin's museum or historical society. That's 
preservation, not theft."
"The ceremonial warhammer, though-I'd leave that. It's explicitly 
religious/ceremonial. Taking it feels like crossing the 'sacred items' 
line."
He looks at you. "But you're the commander. What's your call?"
 
So to summarize:
Definitely take:
*	Helm of Kharas (mission objective)
Probably safe to take:
*	Historical documents in crystal tubes (preservation/scholarship)
*	Personal jewelry/effects (can be donated to museums or dwarven 
authorities)
*	The shield with Thoradin's Hall symbol (historical artifact)
Should NOT take:
*	Ceremonial warhammer (likely counts as "sacred item")
The ward will judge based on intent. If you're taking items 
respectfully for preservation/recovery, you're probably fine. If 
you're looting greedily, the wards will activate.
What do you want to do?
Take what is safe, leave the rest
Dec 10
RESPECTFUL RECOVERY
"We take what's safe and appropriate," you decide. "The Helm is our 
mission. The documents and historical artifacts should be 
preserved-they're records of your people's history. The jewelry 
can go to Thorbardin's museums or historical societies. But we 
leave the ceremonial warhammer. That crosses the line into sacred 
items."
Thordin nods with clear approval. "A wise and respectful choice. Let's 
work quickly."
 
ARTIFACT RECOVERY - 15 MINUTES
The team moves efficiently through the Vault:
Thordin - The Helm of Kharas
Thordin approaches the central pedestal reverently. He speaks quietly in 
Dwarven-a prayer or acknowledgment-then carefully lifts the Helm.
The wards flicker briefly-everyone tenses-but then settle to their 
ambient glow. The ward is assessing but not objecting.
Thordin wraps the Helm carefully in protective cloth and places it in his 
pack. "Mission objective secured."
 
Cyrus - Historical Documents
Cyrus gathers the sealed crystal tubes containing preserved documents. There 
are six of them, each containing rolled parchments-maps, military orders, 
personal correspondence, administrative records.
"These are invaluable," he says reverently. "Primary sources from 
before the Cataclysm. Historians will treasure these."
The wards remain calm. Historical preservation is clearly acceptable.
 
Kessa - Jewelry and Personal Effects
Kessa carefully removes jewelry from the display case:
*	3 rings (gold, possibly magical based on faint auras)
*	2 amulets (silver, one with a gemstone)
*	4 decorative pins (military rank insignia, historical value)
"These belonged to officers and administrators," she 
notes. "Personal effects, not religious items. Should be fine."
The wards continue their ambient shimmer. No objection.
 
Johannes - The Shield
You lift the shield bearing Thoradin's Hall's symbol from its mount. It's well-
crafted, ceremonial but functional, bearing the outpost's heraldry.
"Historical artifact," you say aloud, half to the wards, half to your 
companions. "Preserving this honors those who served here."
The wards pulse once-acknowledgment, not alarm.
 
Items LEFT Behind (Deliberately)
The ceremonial warhammer remains mounted on the far wall. Everyone 
gives it respectful distance. It's clearly a religious symbol, and taking it would 
violate the ward's terms.
Several other items that have decayed beyond recovery-rotted leather, 
corroded metal, documents turned to dust-are left undisturbed.
 
FINAL ASSESSMENT - 20 MINUTES ELAPSED
The four of you stand near the entrance, packs secured with recovered items.
Thordin does a final check: "Helm of Kharas, six document tubes, 
shield, jewelry and insignia. All non-sacred items, all recovered 
respectfully for preservation and historical purposes."
The wards remain stable-ambient glow, no hostile reaction. The ancient 
magic judges your actions acceptable.
Cyrus says quietly: "We've honored the intent of this place. The 
Commander who sealed this Vault wanted his treasures protected 
from desecration and theft. We've taken items to preserve them, 
not to loot them. That's respectful."
Kessa adds: "And we still have forty minutes before the ward 
expires. Plenty of time to exit cleanly."
 
EXITING THE VAULT
You step back through the bronze doors. As you cross the threshold, the 
spectral voice returns:
"RECOVERY COMPLETE. TERMS HONORED. CONDITIONAL 
ACCESS CONCLUDED."
The doors swing shut smoothly behind you, and the wards flare back to full 
strength-sealing the Vault once again.
"Well done," Thordin says with genuine respect. "We retrieved what we 
came for, preserved historical artifacts, and honored the sacred 
nature of the place. That's how professional delving should be 
done."
 
TREASURE ACQUIRED
Mission objective:
*	? Helm of Kharas (Thordin's contract, worth 10,000 gp to his client, 
your share is 3,000 gp)
Additional recoveries (split among party):
*	6 sealed document tubes (historical value, can be donated to 
Thorbardin archives or sold to scholars)
*	Shield of Thoradin's Hall (historical artifact, museum-quality)
*	Jewelry and insignia:
*	3 gold rings (possibly magical, need identification)
*	2 silver amulets (one with gemstone)
*	4 military rank pins (historical collectors would pay well)
Estimated additional value: 2,000-3,000 gp if sold, or significant 
goodwill if donated to appropriate dwarven institutions.
 
RETURN JOURNEY - BEGINNING
"Right," Thordin says, securing his pack. "We've got what we came for. 
The way back should be straightforward-the gricks are dead, the 
passage is clear. Let's head home."
The four of you make your way back through the administrative level, past the 
dead grick alpha, through the main chamber, and to the flooded passage.
The swim back through the submerged section is uneventful with 
Water Breathing still active. You pass the dead gricks floating in the water, 
emerge at the entrance level, and ascend through the barracks and main hall.
No additional encounters. The ruins are silent, the threats eliminated.
 
EMERGING FROM THORADIN'S HALL - LATE 
AFTERNOON
You step out of the ancient entrance into late afternoon sunlight. The fresh 
mountain air is a stark contrast to the stale, damp atmosphere of the ruins.
Mission time: Approximately 6-7 hours from entry to exit.
Thordin breathes deeply, grinning. "By the Forge, that went better than 
I could have hoped. Professional execution, no casualties, objective 
secured, bonus artifacts recovered. This is what proper delving 
looks like."
He looks at the three of you with genuine appreciation. "You're good. 
Really good. If I have other contracts that need skilled people, 
would you be interested?"
 
CYRUS'S STATE
You notice Cyrus looks... better. Not fully recovered from the emotional weight 
of Flotsam, but lighter. He's smiling, genuinely smiling, for the first time since 
the storm.
"That was good," he says quietly to you as you walk. "Just... good. A 
challenge overcome through skill and teamwork. No moral 
calculus. No counting deaths. Just solving problems and 
succeeding together."
He adjusts the document tubes in his pack. "And we preserved history. 
That matters. These records will help people understand what 
happened during the Cataclysm, help dwarven clans reconnect 
with their past. That's... that's meaningful work."
There's hope in his voice. Not complete healing-that will take time-but the 
beginning of it.
 
CAMP - FIRST NIGHT RETURN
You make camp as the sun sets, finding the same sheltered valley you used on 
the way in.
Around the fire, Thordin breaks out good dwarven whiskey. "To a 
successful delve. To professional work. And to companions who 
know their business."
You all drink.
"When we get back to Gateway," Thordin continues, "I'll arrange 
payment transfer. Three thousand gold, split as you prefer. And the 
additional artifacts-we can discuss how to handle those. Sell them 
and split the proceeds, or donate them for goodwill with 
Thorbardin. Your call."
He looks at the stars. "We should reach Gateway by tomorrow 
evening, then you can head back to Haven. Three to four days total, 
just as I promised."
 
How do you want to handle the additional artifacts?
1.	Sell them and split the gold (practical, immediate funds)
2.	Donate to Thorbardin (goodwill, potential future favors/contacts)
3.	Mixed approach (sell the jewelry, donate the documents and shield)
4.	Something else?
And is there anything you want to discuss around the campfire? This 
is a good moment for character interaction if you want it.
Wait. If this contact is in palanthas, let's go with Thorbadin as escort, then 
check out the deed we found in the aboleth lair.
Dec 10
CHANGE OF PLANS - PALANTHAS ROUTE
"Actually, Thordin," you say, "your client is in Palanthas, right?"
"Aye," the dwarf confirms. "Private collector there. Wealthy, discreet, 
pays well."
"We'll escort you to Palanthas," you continue. "We have business 
there ourselves-a property deed we recovered from an aboleth's 
hoard. Pre-Cataclysm warehouse. We need to check if it's still 
standing, see what the situation is."
Thordin raises an eyebrow, intrigued. "A pre-Cataclysm property deed? 
That could be valuable if the structure survived and the deed is still 
legally recognized. Palanthas is one of the few cities that 
maintained continuous legal records through the Cataclysm-they 
might honor it."
He considers. "Palanthas is about a week's travel from here, maybe a 
bit less if we push. Longer than the original job, but..." He grins. "I 
wouldn't mind the company. Safety in numbers, especially carrying 
something as valuable as the Helm. And if you help me with the 
delivery, I can introduce you to some useful contacts in the city."
Kessa nods. "Makes sense. Palanthas is a major city-we can 
resupply, gather intelligence, maybe pick up leads on other work."
Cyrus looks thoughtful. "Palanthas is also one of the great centers of 
learning. The Great Library is there. If we're donating those 
historical documents, that's where they'd have maximum scholarly 
impact. And the Temple of Paladine might have resources for... 
spiritual matters."
You catch the subtext-Cyrus is thinking about his own healing, seeking 
wisdom or counseling from higher-level clerics.
 
REVISED PLAN
"So here's what we do," you lay out. "We travel to Palanthas with 
Thordin-about a week's journey. He delivers the Helm to his 
client, we get paid our 3,000 gold. We investigate the warehouse 
deed situation. We donate the historical documents to the Great 
Library for preservation. And we take some time in the city to 
resupply, rest, and handle personal business."
"After that, we return to Haven-maybe another week's travel. 
Total time away from Haven: about three weeks."
Thordin raises his mug. "I like it. A proper expedition with multiple 
objectives. And Palanthas is worth seeing if you've never been-it's 
the jewel of Solamnia, or at least it was before the Dragon Army 
started making trouble."
"Is Palanthas under Dragon Army control?" Kessa asks sharply.
"Not yet," Thordin says. "It's neutral territory, technically. The city 
maintains its independence through walls, diplomacy, and the fact 
that taking it would be bloody expensive. But the Dragon Army has 
agents there, and tensions are high. You'll want to keep a low 
profile."
 
NOTIFYING HAVEN
You pull out your Sending Stone, the one paired with Commander Laurana 
at Haven.
Speaking into it, you say: "Laurana, mission successful. Escorting 
contact to Palanthas, investigating property deed, returning in 
approximately three weeks. All well."
A moment later, Laurana's voice comes through, tinny but 
clear: "Acknowledged, Commander. Palanthas-be careful, Dragon 
Army presence increasing there. Good hunting. Haven is stable."
The connection ends.
 
ARTIFACT DISTRIBUTION DECISION
"As for the additional artifacts," you say, "I suggest a mixed 
approach. We sell the jewelry to fund our operations-practical 
coin we can use. But we donate the documents and the shield to 
institutions in Palanthas-the Great Library for the documents, 
maybe Thorbardin's embassy or a museum for the shield. Build 
goodwill, honor the history properly."
Thordin nods approvingly. "Wise. The documents especially-the Great 
Library of Palanthas will preserve them properly and make them 
available to scholars. That's far better than selling them to a private 
collector who might hoard them."
Cyrus looks pleased. "I'll personally deliver the documents to the 
Library. I want to ensure they're treated with proper respect."
"And the jewelry?" Kessa asks. "How do we sell that?"
Thordin grins. "I know a reputable jeweler in Palanthas. He'll give 
fair prices, no questions asked. The rings might be magical-if they 
are, they're worth more. We can get them identified in the city."
 
THE JOURNEY TO PALANTHAS - OVERVIEW
Travel time: 7-8 days from current position Route: Mountain trails to 
Gateway (1 day), then main roads through Solamnic territories to Palanthas 
(6-7 days) Conditions: Late spring, good traveling weather, roads relatively 
safe (for now)
Thordin knows the route well and can guide you efficiently.
 
ANYTHING ELSE AROUND THE CAMPFIRE?
The fire crackles. The night is peaceful. You've had a successful mission with 
no casualties, you're heading to one of Krynn's great cities, and the mood is 
good.
Is there anything you want to discuss with your companions?
*	Check in on Cyrus's emotional state more directly?
*	Talk strategy for Palanthas (Dragon Army presence, staying low

*	Discuss the property deed situation and what to expect?
*	Just rest and move to the next day?
Or we can skip ahead to arrival at Gateway, or directly to Palanthas if you 
prefer.
What would you like to do?
Skip to Palanthas.
Dec 10
ARRIVAL AT PALANTHAS - 8 DAYS LATER
The journey has been uneventful-good weather, clear roads, no significant 
encounters. Thordin proved to be excellent company, sharing stories of past 
delves and dwarven history around evening campfires. The rhythm of travel, 
the changing landscape, the straightforward purpose-it's been restorative for 
everyone, especially Cyrus.
Now, as the sun reaches its zenith on the eighth day, you crest a hill and see it:
Palanthas.
 
THE JEWEL OF SOLAMNIA
Even from miles away, the city is breathtaking.
Palanthas sprawls across the coastal plain, protected by massive white walls 
that gleam in the sunlight. The city is enormous-easily ten times the size of 
Flotsam, perhaps fifty times Haven's hidden settlement. Spires and towers rise 
above the walls, the most prominent being the Tower of High 
Sorcery (now dark and abandoned) and the great Library of 
Palanthas with its distinctive dome.
The harbor is visible to the east-dozens of ships at anchor, trade vessels from 
across Ansalon. Despite the Dragon Army's rising power, Palanthas remains a 
hub of commerce and civilization.
But there are signs of tension:
*	The walls are heavily manned-you can see patrols even from this 
distance
*	Military camps outside the walls (Solamnic Knights? Dragon Army? 
Both?)
*	Fewer ships than there probably were before the war
*	A general atmosphere of watchfulness
Thordin points out landmarks:
"The Great Library-that domed building near the center. Largest 
collection of knowledge on Krynn, or so they claim. Your 
documents will be safe there."
"The Old City-that's the wealthy district, where nobles and 
merchants live. My client is there. We'll deliver the Helm 
tomorrow-I prefer not to walk through the city carrying 
something that valuable today."
"The warehouse district-eastern side, near the docks. That's 
where your deed property would be if it still exists."
"And see those camps outside the walls? Mixed. Some are Solamnic 
Knights maintaining order. Some are Dragon Army 'trade envoys' 
who are really spies and advance scouts. The city is officially 
neutral, but everyone's positioning for when that changes."
 
ENTERING THE CITY - AFTERNOON
You approach the southern gate. The guards are professional-Palanthas City 
Watch, not Dragon Army or Solamnic Knights. They wear distinctive blue and 
white tabards.
Gate inspection:
The guard captain, a weathered human in his forties, looks over your 
group: "State your business in Palanthas."
Thordin answers smoothly: "Thordin Ironhelm, master delver of 
Thorbardin. These are my associates. We're here on business-
artifact delivery, historical research, personal matters. Three to 
five days, then we depart."
The captain looks at each of you, his gaze lingering on your 
weapons. "Palanthas maintains strict peace within the walls. No 
brawling, no unsanctioned magic use, no causing trouble. Dragon 
Army and Solamnic Knights both have agents here-we don't care 
about your politics as long as you don't bring war to our streets. 
Understood?"
"Understood," you confirm.
"Entry tax: 5 silver per person." He holds out his hand.
You pay (2 gold total for the four of you), and he waves you 
through. "Welcome to Palanthas. Try the Golden Griffin Inn in the 
merchant quarter-clean rooms, fair prices. And stay out of 
trouble."
 
INSIDE PALANTHAS - FIRST IMPRESSIONS
Stepping through the gates is like entering a different world.
Paved streets. Actual cobblestones, well-maintained, with drainage gutters.
Multi-story buildings. Stone and timber construction, proper architecture, 
most buildings three or four stories tall.
Crowds. Thousands of people-humans, elves, dwarves, kender, even a few 
half-ogres. Merchants hawking wares, street performers, scholars in robes, 
soldiers on patrol, nobles in fine clothes being carried in litters.
Shops and businesses everywhere. Jewelers, bookbinders, weapon 
smiths, tailors, apothecaries, taverns, temples. This is a functioning, thriving 
city despite the war.
Kessa looks around with wide eyes. "This is... I've never seen anything 
like this. Haven is maybe 200 people. This is..."
"About 50,000 residents," Thordin supplies. "Plus maybe another 
10,000 refugees and traders at any given time. Palanthas is one of 
the last great free cities."
Cyrus is staring at the Library dome in the distance. "The knowledge 
contained in that building... centuries of scholarship, history, 
wisdom. I need to visit."
 
FINDING LODGING - THE GOLDEN GRIFFIN INN
Following the guard captain's recommendation, you find the Golden Griffin 
Inn in the merchant quarter. It's a well-maintained three-story building with 
a common room, private rooms, and stables.
The proprietor, a cheerful halfling woman named Miri Goldleaf, greets you 
warmly. "Welcome, travelers! Rooms for four? We have space-two 
silver per person per night, includes breakfast. Stabling for mounts 
if you have them, though I see you're on foot."
"Three nights to start," Thordin says, paying. "We may extend 
depending on business."
"Excellent! Rooms 7, 8, 9, and 10 on the second floor. Common 
room serves dinner at sunset. Anything you need in Palanthas, I 
can point you in the right direction-I know this city inside and 
out."
 
SETTLING IN - EARLY AFTERNOON
You claim your rooms, stash your packs (keeping valuables secured), and 
regroup in the common room.
Thordin lays out the plan:
"Tonight, we rest and get our bearings. Tomorrow morning, I'll 
deliver the Helm to my client-Johannes, I'd like you to come with 
me for security. Shouldn't take more than an hour, and you'll get 
your payment immediately."
"After that, we split up to handle our various business:"
*	Investigate the warehouse deed (Johannes + whoever wants to 
join)
*	Deliver documents to the Great Library (Cyrus is adamant about 
this)
*	Sell the jewelry (Thordin can handle this with Kessa if needed)
*	Personal errands (resupply, gather intelligence, whatever else)
"We regroup here each evening, share information, stay 
coordinated. Three to five days in the city, then we head back to 
Haven. Sound good?"
Everyone agrees.
 
CURRENT STATUS - LATE AFTERNOON IN 
PALANTHAS
Party:
*	Well-rested from the journey

City situation:
*	Neutral but tense

5.	Visit a specific location (Library? Temple? Markets?)
6.	Something else?
The afternoon sun slants through Palanthas's streets. The city awaits.
I go with Cyrus, while Kessa goes with Thordin.
Dec 10
SPLITTING UP - AFTERNOON ACTIVITIES
You make the decision quickly. "Cyrus and I will head to the Great 
Library-get a sense of the place, maybe start the document 
donation process. Kessa, you go with Thordin to scout the jeweler 
and get the rings identified. We'll regroup at dinner."
Kessa nods. "Works for me. I want to see what these rings are worth 
anyway."
Thordin grins. "Excellent. My jeweler contact can do magical 
identification-he's got the tools and the expertise. We'll know 
what we're dealing with by dinner."
Cyrus looks genuinely excited. "The Great Library of Palanthas. I've 
dreamed of visiting since I was an acolyte."
 
JOHANNES & CYRUS - THE GREAT LIBRARY
The two of you make your way through Palanthas's streets toward the Library. 
Cyrus walks with purpose, the document tubes carefully secured in his pack.
The walk takes about 20 minutes through increasingly scholarly 
districts-bookshops, scribe services, small academies, student housing. The 
people here are more subdued, intellectual, focused.
And then you see it up close:
The Great Library of Palanthas.
 
THE LIBRARY - EXTERIOR
The building is magnificent-easily the size of several city blocks. The central 
dome rises 100 feet into the air, covered in copper that's aged to a beautiful 
green patina. Wings extend from the main structure, each dedicated to 
different branches of knowledge.
The entrance is a grand colonnade with steps leading up to massive bronze 
doors. Carved into the stonework above: "KNOWLEDGE IS THE LIGHT 
THAT BANISHES DARKNESS"
Scholars, students, and researchers flow in and out constantly. This is a living 
institution, not a museum.
Cyrus stops at the base of the steps, just... looking.
"Three centuries of knowledge," he says quietly. "Histories, 
philosophies, sciences, magics. The accumulated wisdom of Krynn, 
preserved through the Cataclysm. If there are answers to the great 
questions of our time, they're in there."
He looks at you. "Thank you for coming with me. This matters."
 
ENTERING THE LIBRARY
You climb the steps and pass through the bronze doors into the main atrium.
The interior is breathtaking:
*	Vaulted ceilings with painted frescoes showing the history of learning
*	Reading tables scattered throughout, most occupied by scholars bent 
over manuscripts
*	Shelves stretching in every direction, organized by complex systems
*	Soft light from magical globes (not torches-fire is forbidden)
*	A sense of reverence, like entering a temple
A librarian approaches-an elderly elf woman in dark blue robes, her 
silver hair bound in a practical bun. She has the look of someone who's spent 
her entire long life among books.
"Welcome to the Great Library," she says in a soft but clear voice. "I am 
Laurelis, senior archivist. How may we assist you today?"
Cyrus steps forward respectfully. "Honored archivist, I am Brother 
Cyrus, cleric of Mishakal. My companion and I have recovered 
historical documents from the ruins of Thoradin's Hall-pre-
Cataclysm records sealed and preserved. We wish to donate them 
to the Library for proper preservation and scholarly study."
Laurelis's eyes widen slightly-genuine excitement breaking through her 
professional demeanor. "Pre-Cataclysm documents? From Thoradin's 
Hall? That outpost was lost 280 years ago. If you truly have intact 
records..."
She gestures urgently. "Please, come with me immediately. This 
requires the attention of our Chief Historian."
 
MEETING THE CHIEF HISTORIAN
Laurelis leads you through the Library at a brisk pace-deeper into the 
building, past reading rooms and storage areas, to a section 
marked "RESTRICTED - ARCHIVAL PRESERVATION".
She knocks on a door, opens it without waiting for response: "Master 
Aldric, you must see this."
The room beyond is an archivist's workshop-preservation tools, crystal 
storage tubes, magical glyphs for document protection. And at the center desk, 
bent over a manuscript with a magnifying lens:
Master Aldric Brightquill.
He's an older human, perhaps sixty, with ink-stained fingers and a scholar's 
stoop. But his eyes are sharp, intelligent, and they fix on the document tubes 
Cyrus is pulling from his pack with laser focus.
"Laurelis, this had better be-" He stops mid-sentence as he sees the 
tubes. "Are those... original seals? Those markings..."
Cyrus carefully places all six tubes on the examination table. "Recovered 
from the Commander's Vault in Thoradin's Hall. Sealed in crystal 
during the last days before the Cataclysm. Administrative records, 
military orders, personal correspondence, maps. All intact."
Aldric approaches the tubes like they're holy relics. His hands hover over 
them, not quite touching. "By the gods. Do you understand what you've 
brought us? Thoradin's Hall was a frontier outpost-its records 
were thought completely lost. These could contain information 
about pre-Cataclysm dwarven culture, military operations, trade 
routes, even personal accounts of what people knew or suspected 
before the world broke."
He looks at Cyrus with profound respect. "And you're... donating these? 
Not selling?"
"Yes," Cyrus says firmly. "Knowledge should be shared, preserved, 
studied. These documents belong to history, not to private 
collectors."
Aldric nods slowly. "Then on behalf of the Great Library of Palanthas, 
I accept this donation with profound gratitude." He gestures to the 
tubes. "May I?"
At Cyrus's nod, he carefully opens one tube and extracts the rolled parchment 
inside.
His hands tremble as he unrolls it.
"It's perfect," he breathes. "The preservation magic held completely. 
This is a military supply manifest dated three months before the 
Cataclysm. Look-here, this officer is reporting unusual seismic 
activity. And here, a note about refugees arriving from the coast 
claiming the gods had abandoned them..."
He looks up, tears in his eyes. "These are the voices of people who lived 
through the end of the world. Their words, their concerns, their 
last days. This is... this is invaluable."
 
FORMAL DONATION PROCESS
Aldric composes himself, becoming professional again. "Forgive my 
emotion. Let me handle this properly."
He produces a ledger and begins formal documentation:
"Name of donor?"
"Brother Cyrus of Mishakal. My companion, Johannes 
Constantinius, was instrumental in the recovery."
"Location of recovery?"
"Thoradin's Hall, approximately 80 miles northeast of Haven, 
within the ruins' Commander's Vault."
"Date of recovery?"
You provide the date.
"Contents?"
Cyrus describes each tube's contents as best he can determine from cursory 
examination.
Aldric writes it all down meticulously. Then he produces a certificate:
"This document formally acknowledges your donation to the Great 
Library. You will be credited in our archives and in any scholarly 
works that draw from these materials. Additionally..."
He pauses, considering. "The Library offers a reward for significant 
historical donations-both to encourage such generosity and to 
offset the costs adventurers incur in recovery. For materials of this 
quality and historical importance, the standard reward is 500 gold 
pieces."
Cyrus starts to protest-"We didn't do this for money-"
But Aldric raises a hand. "I know. But accept it anyway. Use it to fund 
further historical recoveries, or donate it to your temple, or spend 
it on ale. The policy exists for good reason."
He hands Cyrus a voucher. "Present this to the Library's bursar-first 
floor, western wing. He'll pay you immediately."
 
FINAL WORDS
As you prepare to leave, Aldric says: "Brother Cyrus, Johannes-you've 
done a great service today. Not just to scholarship, but to memory. 
These people who lived and died at Thoradin's Hall... they're not 
forgotten now. Their voices will be heard again."
He smiles. "And if you ever recover more historical materials, 
please, bring them here. We'll preserve them properly."
Cyrus bows respectfully. "Thank you, Master Aldric. It honors them, 
and us, to know their words will be studied and remembered."
 
LEAVING THE LIBRARY - CYRUS'S STATE
Outside, back in the afternoon sunlight, Cyrus is quiet for a long moment.
Then he speaks: "That felt... important. Not just strategically, not just 
practically. Morally important. Those documents will help people 
understand the past, learn from it, maybe avoid repeating 
mistakes."
He looks at you. "The people who died in the Flotsam storm-I can't 
bring them back. I can't undo what happened. But I can do things 
like this. Preserve history. Help scholars. Contribute to knowledge. 
That's... that's a kind of healing, isn't it? Making the world a little 
better, one action at a time."
There's something lighter in his expression. Not fully healed, but moving in 
that direction.
"Thank you for coming with me," he says simply.
 
MEANWHILE - KESSA & THORDIN
(Summarized, since you're with Cyrus)
Kessa and Thordin make their way to the jeweler district. Thordin's contact-

*	Pins: Non-magical, collector value - Worth ~300 gp combined
Total potential sale: ~5,900 gp

EVENING DECISIONS & CELEBRATION

"And tonight," you continue, standing with your ale, "we celebrate

Money is no object-best food, best drink, enjoy the city. We've

Thordin grins broadly. "Now THAT'S what I like to hear! Miri! Your 
finest vintage, and keep it coming!"
 
A NIGHT IN PALANTHAS - CELEBRATION
The evening unfolds with genuine joy:
Fine food and wine. Miri, delighted by free-spending customers, produces 
dishes normally reserved for nobles-roasted duck, honeyed vegetables, 
imported cheeses, desserts with chocolate and cream.
Stories and laughter. Thordin regales you with delving tales. Kessa shares 
(heavily edited) stories of past heists. Even Cyrus contributes, talking about 
his training at the temple, his mentor, the moment he first felt Mishakal's 
presence.
Music. A bard in the common room plays, and Kessa-surprisingly-knows 
the words to several traveling songs. She has a decent voice.
It's good. Simple, uncomplicated good. The kind of evening that reminds you 
why you fight-so people can have nights like this. Safe, warm, together.
But as the night winds down and others drift to their rooms, you notice Cyrus 
has grown quiet again. He's staring into his wine, the lightness from earlier 
fading.
 
OOC - CYRUS'S DEEPER HEALING
Understood. What Cyrus needs isn't just distraction or being told "it's okay." 
He needs something profound-a moment of grace, of being shown (not told) 
that redemption is real, that his burden can be transformed into something 
meaningful, that the weight he carries can become strength rather than 
crushing guilt.
Think The Mission-Father Gabriel's journey from guilt over past violence to 
sacrificial love. The moment where Robert De Niro's character drags his armor 
up the waterfall as penance, and the natives cut it free, releasing him.
Cyrus needs a moment of transformative encounter-something that 
shows him viscerally that his actions, however costly, had meaning, and that 
he can still be an instrument of healing rather than just death.
I have something planned. Trust me. It starts tomorrow, during what seems 
like routine business in the warehouse district, but becomes something much 
deeper.
For now, let's end tonight with you noticing Cyrus's state:
 
LATE EVENING - CHECKING ON CYRUS
Most of the common room has emptied. Cyrus sits alone at a corner table, 
wine mostly untouched, staring at nothing.
You slide into the seat across from him.
"Brother. You seemed lighter earlier. After the Library."
Cyrus nods slowly. "I was. I am. The donation mattered. Preserving 
history, helping scholars-it felt good. Meaningful."
He pauses. "But it's not enough, Johannes. I know it's not supposed 
to be-one good deed doesn't erase 547 deaths. I'm not that naive. 
But I thought... I hoped... that doing something unambiguously 
good would make the weight less."
He looks at you, and there's pain in his eyes. "It didn't. The number is still 
there. The faces I imagine-sailors I never saw, men I killed from 
five miles away. They're still there when I close my eyes."
"I don't regret the decision," he clarifies quickly. "We saved 
thousands. We stopped an invasion. It was the right choice. But 
knowing it was right doesn't make carrying it easier."
He's not asking for answers. He's just... bearing witness to his own struggle.
What do you say?
(This sets up tomorrow's events, where something will happen that gives 
Cyrus the deeper healing he needs. But this moment matters too-your 
response, how you meet him in this pain.)
You're right. Sometimes, the right thing is the hard thing, and there is no way 
to unburden it. The price stays. And you are the only one who can carry it.
Dec 10
JOHANNES'S RESPONSE
You don't look away from Cyrus's pain. You meet it directly.
"You're right. Sometimes the right thing is the hard thing, and 
there is no way to unburden it. The price stays. And you are the 
only one who can carry it."
Cyrus's eyes widen slightly-he wasn't expecting that. No platitudes, no "it'll 
get easier," no attempts to minimize what he carries.
You continue, your voice quiet but firm:
"I can't take this from you, Cyrus. Neither can Kessa, neither can 
Laurana or anyone else. Those 547 souls-you felt each one pass. 
That's yours to carry. That's the cost of wielding that kind of power 
for that kind of purpose."
You lean forward slightly. "But here's what I can tell you: You're not 
carrying it alone in terms of purpose. We made the decision 
together. We stand by it together. And if that weight ever threatens 
to crush you, we'll be there to remind you why you carry it."
"You saved Ak-Thyln. You saved Kalaman. You saved thousands of 
people who will never know your name, never know what you 
sacrificed for them. That doesn't make the weight lighter-but it 
makes it meaningful. And meaningful weight... that's different 
from meaningless suffering."
You pause, then add: "You're still Cyrus. Still a healer. Still a servant 
of Mishakal. The storm didn't change that-it proved it. You were 
willing to take on that burden, to carry those deaths, to sacrifice 
your own peace... for others. That's not corruption, Brother. That's 
love. Terrible, costly, sacrificial love."
 
Cyrus is silent for a long moment. Then he speaks, his voice rough:
"Thank you. For not... for not trying to make it easier than it is. For 
respecting that this is... real. Heavy. Mine."
He drains his wine, sets the cup down. "I'm going to carry this for the 
rest of my life. I know that now. But maybe... maybe if I can find 
ways to make it count-to use what I've learned, what I've 
experienced, to help others-then it won't just be weight. It'll be... 
ballast. Keeping me grounded. Keeping me honest."
He stands, places a hand on your shoulder. "Get some rest, my friend. 
Tomorrow we investigate your warehouse. And who knows-maybe 
Palanthas has more to teach us than we expect."
He heads upstairs, walking like a man carrying a heavy burden-but carrying 
it deliberately, purposefully, not crushed by it.
 
MORNING - THE HELM DELIVERY
You wake early, dress, and meet Thordin in the common room. He's already

"Ready?" he asks. "My client lives in the Old City-wealthy district. 
Shouldn't take more than an hour for the whole transaction. Then 
you get your 1,000 gold, I get my 7,000, and we're done."
Kessa appears at the stairs. "I'm coming too. Three people carrying that 
much gold through city streets is smarter than two."
Thordin grins. "Fair point. The more the merrier."
Cyrus joins you as well. "May as well make it four. I'm curious to see 
the Old City anyway."
 
THE OLD CITY - MORNING
The four of you make your way through Palanthas toward the wealthy district. 
The Old City is a stark contrast to the merchant quarter-wide streets, elegant 
townhouses, private gardens, guards at every corner.
Thordin leads you to a particular mansion-three stories, marble facade, 
discreet but clearly expensive.
"This is it. Lord Varkis Threnody, private collector. Eccentric but 
honorable. He'll pay immediately and in full."
You're admitted by a butler, led through a tastefully decorated interior, and 
brought to a private study where Lord Varkis awaits.
He's a human in his sixties, scholarly looking, surrounded by display cases 
containing historical artifacts. When he sees Thordin, his face lights up.
"Master Ironhelm! You've returned! And you have it?"
Thordin carefully unwraps the Helm of Kharas.
Lord Varkis actually gasps. He approaches it with trembling hands, examining 
it from every angle. "Perfect. Absolutely perfect. Three centuries lost, 
and here it is, as magnificent as the day it was forged."
He looks at Thordin with genuine emotion. **"You've done what others said 
was impossible. Name your price."
"Ten thousand gold pieces, as agreed," Thordin says calmly.
"Done." Lord Varkis doesn't even haggle. He produces a letter of credit-
negotiable at any major bank in Palanthas. "Payable immediately. And 
Master Ironhelm-if you ever recover other items of dwarven 
heritage, I'm always interested."
 
PAYMENT - OUTSIDE THE MANSION
Once you're back on the street, Thordin leads you directly to a bank. Within

*	7,000 gp for Thordin

The bank provides you with secure carrying options (letters of credit,

AFTERNOON - THE WAREHOUSE DISTRICT
With the Helm delivery complete, you turn to your next objective:

You pull out the pre-Cataclysm deed-aged parchment, but still legible,

"Let's see if this place even still exists," Kessa says.
The four of you make your way to the warehouse district-a busy area of

Following the deed's description and asking a few locals, you eventually find 
the address:
Warehouse 47, Eastdock Quarter.
And it's... still standing.
 
WAREHOUSE 47 - EXTERIOR
The building is old-pre-Cataclysm construction, clearly. Three stories, stone 
foundation, timber upper levels. It's weathered but structurally sound. The 
windows are shuttered, the main door is chained and locked.
But someone has been maintaining it-the roof is patched, the chains are new, 
and there's a faded sign: "PROPERTY OF EASTDOCK MERCHANT 
COLLECTIVE - INQUIRIES TO HARBORMASTER"
"Interesting," Thordin murmurs. "It survived the Cataclysm, and 
someone's been keeping it from falling apart. But it's currently 
unclaimed or in administrative limbo."
Cyrus examines the deed carefully. "This document pre-dates the 
Cataclysm. If Palanthas's legal system honored continuity of 
ownership through the disaster, this deed might still be valid. 
But..."
"But someone else might have claimed it in the intervening 280 
years," Kessa finishes.
 
INVESTIGATING OWNERSHIP - THE 
HARBORMASTER
You follow the sign's instruction and head to the Harbormaster's office-a 
busy administrative building overseeing all dock activity.
After some bureaucratic navigation, you're directed to a clerk handling 
property records: Magister Orin Blackquill, a fastidious half-elf with ink-
stained fingers.
You present the deed.
His eyes widen. "This is... this predates the Cataclysm. Where did you 
acquire this?"
"Salvage from an abandoned location," you answer carefully. "We're 
inquiring whether it's still legally valid."
Magister Blackquill examines it with professional scrutiny, cross-referencing 
with thick ledgers. After several minutes, he looks up.
"This is fascinating. Warehouse 47 has been in administrative 
limbo for 180 years. The original owner-one Elias Merchent-died 
in the Cataclysm with no heirs. The property was claimed by the 
city, but never formally processed due to the chaos. It's been 
maintained by the Eastdock Collective as a public warehouse, but 
no one technically owns it."
He taps the deed. "This document, if authentic, represents legitimate 
pre-Cataclysm ownership. Under Palanthas law, such deeds are 
honored if they can be verified. However..."
He pauses. "Verification requires proof of chain of ownership. Can 
you demonstrate how this deed came into your possession legally?"
 
This is a decision point. You could:
1.	Explain truthfully (recovered from aboleth's hoard, legitimate 
salvage)
2.	Claim inheritance (false, but simpler)
3.	Offer to purchase current claim (bypass the legal complexity)
4.	Investigate the Eastdock Collective's interest (they might

But before you can respond, something interrupts:
A commotion outside-shouting, the sound of running feet, a woman's

Magister Blackquill frowns. "What in the-"
You all rush to the window.
 
THE INTERRUPTION - SOMETHING MORE 
IMPORTANT
Outside the Harbormaster's office, in the busy dock square, there's chaos.
A wagon has overturned, spilling its cargo into the street. But that's not 
the problem.
The problem is the dozen people trapped beneath it-dock workers who 
were unloading, now pinned by the massive wooden structure and its load of 
stone blocks.
People are screaming. Some are trying to lift the wagon, but it's too heavy. 
Others are running for help.
And then you see what made it worse: Fire. One of the lanterns from the 
wagon has ignited spilled oil. Flames are spreading toward the trapped 
workers.
People are going to die. Soon. Maybe minutes.
The City Watch is responding, but they're not here yet. Bystanders are 
panicking.
 
Cyrus's face goes pale. Then resolves into absolute determination.
"Johannes. We have to help. Now."
He's already moving toward the door.
 
This is the beginning of Cyrus's deeper redemption arc. What

What do you do?

Cure Wounds (3rd level): 3d8+4 = 18 HP restored
The man gasps, coughs blood, then gasps again-this time actually pulling air.

THE LIFT - STRENGTH AND FAITH
You position yourself on one side of the massive stone block, Thordin on the

ATHLETICS CHECK - CRITICAL MOMENT

SUCCESS
