You and Thordin release the block. It crashes back down with a 
massive THUD that shakes the ground-right where the child had been lying 
moments before.
 
THE AFTERMATH
Cyrus emerges from beneath the wagon wreckage, the little girl clutched in his 
arms. She's crying but alive, conscious, moving all her limbs.
"Mama!" she wails, reaching out.
A woman breaks through the crowd, screaming: "LILA! MY BABY!"
Cyrus gently passes the child to her mother. They collapse together, sobbing 
with relief.
But Cyrus doesn't pause. "She needs healing. Crushed leg, possible 
internal injuries."
He places his hands on the child, and Mishakal's light flares once more.
Cure Wounds (2nd level): 2d8+4 = 14 HP restored
The little girl gasps as divine magic knits broken bones, repairs crushed tissue, 
eases pain. The impossible healing of the gods made manifest.
"She'll be fine," Cyrus tells the mother. "Get her to a proper healer for 
observation, but she'll be fine."
The mother looks at him with tears streaming down her face. "You saved 
her. You risked your life to save my daughter. I don't... I don't have 
words..."
Cyrus just nods, already moving to the next victim.
 
FINAL TALLY - 15 MINUTES LATER
The fire is fully extinguished. The City Watch has arrived with proper 
equipment. Healers are tending to the injured.
Final count:
*	11 people trapped under the wagon
*	11 people rescued alive
*	Zero deaths
*	Multiple serious injuries stabilized by Cyrus
It's a miracle. Everyone is saying so-if those adventurers hadn't been there, 
if that cleric hadn't acted so fast, half these people would be dead.
 
CYRUS - THE MOMENT OF GRACE
Cyrus sits on a dock post, breathing hard, covered in blood and dirt and soot. 
His robes are torn. His hands are scraped raw. He's exhausted, having burned 
through most of his spell slots.
But people keep approaching him.
The mother with the little girl: "Thank you. Thank you. Mishakal bless 
you."
The man whose crushed chest Cyrus healed: "You brought me back. I 
wasn't breathing, and you brought me back."
A dock worker who was pulled free: "I've got four kids at home. Because 
of you, I'll see them tonight."
One after another, they come. Not to pay him. Not to praise him as a hero. 
Just to bear witness-to say, simply and directly: You saved my life. I'm 
alive because of you.
 
And then something shifts in Cyrus's expression.
His hands are shaking. Not from exhaustion. From emotion.
He looks at them-really looks. The mother holding her daughter. The man 
breathing again. The worker who will see his children.
Eleven people. Eleven lives saved. Eleven souls who will go home tonight, 
who will wake tomorrow, who will live and love and laugh because he acted.
Tears start streaming down his face.
"Eleven," he whispers. "Eleven."
Then louder, to himself, working through something profound:
"Five hundred forty-seven died. Eleven lived. The numbers don't 
balance. They'll never balance. But these eleven... they're REAL. 
They're here. They're breathing. I can SEE them."
He stands, looks at the mother and child.
"I couldn't see the five hundred forty-seven. I felt them pass, but I 
never saw their faces. They were... abstract. Numbers. Weight. 
Guilt."
"But this..." He gestures to the rescued workers, the crying child now safe in 
her mother's arms. "This is REAL. This is what Mishakal calls me to 
do. Not to count the dead. To save the living."
He looks at you, Johannes, and there's something in his eyes-not quite peace, 
not yet, but hope. Real hope.
"I can't bring back the five hundred forty-seven. But I can save 
eleven today. And eleven tomorrow. And eleven the day after that. 
For the rest of my life, I can SAVE people. That's what this power is 
for. Not to calculate costs. To preserve life."
 
The little girl-Lila-breaks free from her mother and runs back to Cyrus. She 
throws her small arms around his legs.
"Thank you, mister healer man. You were brave."
Cyrus kneels down to her level. His voice breaks: "No, sweetheart. You 
were brave. You held on. You trusted me. You're alive because YOU 
were brave."
She hugs him again, then runs back to her mother.
 
Cyrus stands, and for the first time since the storm, he looks like himself 
again. Not undamaged. Not without scars. But whole.
"Johannes," he says quietly. "I think... I think I understand now. The 
five hundred forty-seven will always be part of me. But so will Lila. 
So will these eleven. And every life I save from now on. The weight 
doesn't disappear-but it becomes... bearable. Because it's 
balanced by purpose."
He takes a deep, shuddering breath. "I'm still a healer. That's who I am. 
And that's enough."
 
THE CITY RESPONDS
The City Watch Captain approaches-the same one who let you through the 
gates. He looks at your group with new respect.
"That was exceptional work. You saved lives today. Palanthas is in 
your debt."
The City Mage who contained the fire joins him. "Agreed. That was the 
most efficient rescue operation I've ever seen. Are you affiliated 
with any temple or guild?"
Before you can answer, the Harbormaster himself emerges from his office, 
having witnessed everything. "You were inquiring about Warehouse 47, 
yes? The deed?"
He looks at Cyrus specifically. "That man just saved eleven dock 
workers-people I'm responsible for. Consider the deed verified. 
I'll personally expedite the paperwork. Warehouse 47 is yours. No 
questions asked."
He extends his hand. "Welcome to Palanthas, Brothers. We need 
people like you."
 
OUTCOME
Mission complete (unexpected):
*	11 lives saved
*	Zero casualties
*	City authorities grateful
*	Warehouse 47 ownership secured through goodwill
Cyrus's state:
*	Profoundly changed
*	Not "healed" of his guilt, but transformed by it
*	Now sees his power as calling, not curse
*	Purpose restored: Save the living
Party status:
*	Slightly depleted spell slots (Cyrus used several)
*	Minor injuries (scrapes, bruises)
*	Massive goodwill with Palanthas authorities
*	Unexpected property ownership
 
It's now late afternoon. What do you want to do?
1.	Inspect Warehouse 47 (it's yours now, see what you've got)
2.	Rest and recover (return to inn, let Cyrus process)
3.	Follow up with authorities (formalize the deed transfer)
4.	Something else?
The dock square is returning to normal. People are clearing debris. The 
rescued workers are being tended to.
And Cyrus stands among them, tears drying on his face, looking lighter than 
he has in weeks.
3, then 1.
Dec 10
FORMALIZING THE DEED - HARBORMASTER'S 
OFFICE
The Harbormaster-Master Devin Stormcrest, a weathered human in his 
fifties with the bearing of a career naval officer-leads you back into his office 
personally.
"Magister Blackquill," he calls to the clerk you'd been dealing with 
earlier. "The deed for Warehouse 47. These people have just saved 
eleven of our workers' lives. I'm invoking emergency municipal 
authority to expedite ownership transfer."
Blackquill looks startled but immediately pulls out the relevant ledgers. "Sir, 
the standard verification process requires-"
"I'm aware of the process," Stormcrest interrupts, not unkindly. "And 
I'm overriding it. That cleric crawled under five hundred pounds of 
stone to pull out a child. I watched it happen. If he's willing to risk 
his life for our people, we can damn well process some paperwork 
quickly."
He looks at you. "The deed you presented-pre-Cataclysm, legitimate 
construction, unclaimed for 180 years. Under Palanthas law, 
salvaged historical documents of clear provenance are recognized. 
You recovered it legally from an abandoned site. That's sufficient."
 
THE PAPERWORK - 30 MINUTES
Magister Blackquill, seeing his superior's determination, works with 
remarkable efficiency:
"I'll need your names for the official registry."
You provide them: Johannes Constantinius, Kessa Darrow, Brother Cyrus.
"Ownership structure?"
"Equal three-way partnership," you decide quickly. Everyone nods 
agreement.
"Purpose of property?"
"General use-storage, operations base, commercial rental, to be 
determined," Kessa answers professionally.
Blackquill writes furiously, stamps multiple documents with official seals, has 
Master Stormcrest countersign as authorizing authority.
"There," he says finally, handing you three copies of the formalized deed-
one for each partner. "Warehouse 47, Eastdock Quarter, officially 
registered to your partnership. Current property taxes: 50 gold per 
year, payable to the city. Any commercial use requires appropriate 
licensing, but storage and personal use are unrestricted."
He pauses, then adds quietly: "And for what it's worth-thank you. My 
cousin was one of the workers you pulled out today. He's alive 
because of you."
 
Master Stormcrest adds: "The Eastdock Collective has been 
maintaining the building in the city's absence. They've done good 
work-the structure is sound, the roof is patched, the foundation is 
solid. You're not inheriting a ruin. You're inheriting a functional 
warehouse that just needs some attention."
He hands you a key-old, iron, but well-maintained. "This opens the main 
door. The Collective's foreman has been holding it. I'll send word 
that ownership has transferred."
"One more thing," he says, his tone becoming more serious. "You've 
made a good impression today. Palanthas needs people like you-
competent, principled, willing to act. If you're staying in the city, or 
if you return in the future, know that you have friends here. The 
Harbormaster's office, the City Watch, even the Lord's Council-
word will spread about what you did today."
"Just... be careful. Palanthas is neutral territory, but the Dragon 
Army has eyes everywhere. If they learn about skilled resistance 
operatives in the city, they'll take an interest. Keep your heads 
down when necessary."
 
WAREHOUSE 47 - INSPECTION
Armed with the key and official ownership documents, the four of you make 
your way through the dock district to your newly acquired property.
Warehouse 47 sits on a reasonably prominent corner lot, with access to both 
a main street and a smaller alley. The three-story structure shows its age but 
also its quality-pre-Cataclysm construction means it was built to last.
You unlock the main door (the chain was removed by the Collective after 
Stormcrest sent word) and step inside.
 
INTERIOR - GROUND FLOOR
The main level is a large open space-roughly 60 feet by 40 feet, with a 20-foot 
ceiling. Support pillars run down the center.
Current state:
*	Clean and dry. The Collective has been maintaining it well-no leaks, 
no rot, no pest infestations
*	Empty. Whatever was stored here was cleared out long ago
*	Loading dock on one side with large double doors opening to the 
street
*	Smaller side door to the alley (for discrete access)
*	Stairs leading up to the second and third floors
Thordin examines the structure professionally: "This is solid work. 
Dwarven-influenced construction techniques-see those support 
pillars? That's proper load-bearing architecture. This building 
could stand another three centuries easily."
 
SECOND FLOOR
Up the stairs, you find the second level is divided into rooms:
*	Four medium-sized chambers (could be offices, private storage, 
living quarters)
*	One larger open space (could be meeting room, workshop, barracks)
*	Small water closet with a (currently non-functional) pump system
Windows provide good light and ventilation. The rooms are bare but 
serviceable.
Kessa's assessment: "This could be converted to comfortable living 
space. Or kept as offices and secure storage. We've got options."
 
THIRD FLOOR
The top level is another open space, though smaller than the ground floor 
(maybe 40 feet by 30 feet). The ceiling here is only 12 feet high, but there 
are skylights that let in natural light.
Current state:
*	Empty except for some old crates and forgotten equipment
*	Access to the roof via a hatch
*	Good views of the surrounding district
From the roof, you can see the harbor, the city walls, major streets. It's 
actually quite a strategic location for observation.
 
OVERALL ASSESSMENT
Thordin gives his professional opinion: "This is valuable property. 
Not mansion-level, but in a major city like Palanthas? This is worth 
at least 5,000 gold, maybe more depending on market conditions. 
The fact that you got it through salvage and goodwill rather than 
purchase? That's exceptional."
Kessa adds: "It's also defensible. One main entrance, one side 
entrance, both easily secured. Upper floors provide height 
advantage. If we ever need a safe house in Palanthas, this is ideal."
Cyrus looks thoughtful: "It could also serve the resistance. Secure 
storage for supplies, meetings space, a base of operations away 
from Haven. Or we could rent it commercially and generate income 
to fund resistance activities."
 
POTENTIAL USES FOR WAREHOUSE 47
You discuss possibilities:
Option 1: Personal Safe House
*	Keep it private, use it when you're in Palanthas
*	Secure storage for equipment and valuables
*	Emergency fallback position
Option 2: Resistance Operations Base
*	Coordinate with Haven to use it for intelligence gathering
*	Store supplies, weapons, documents
*	Meeting space for resistance operatives in Palanthas
Option 3: Commercial Rental
*	Rent to legitimate merchants for income (50-100 gp/month)
*	Maintains cover, generates revenue
*	Less secure for sensitive operations
Option 4: Mixed Use
*	Ground floor: Commercial rental or legitimate front business
*	Upper floors: Private resistance operations
*	Balances income with operational security
Option 5: Leave It
*	Pay the 50 gp/year taxes, keep it maintained but unused
*	Option available for future need
 
Thordin says: "Whatever you decide, I'd recommend hiring a 
caretaker-someone to maintain the building, handle any 
commercial arrangements, and keep an eye on things when you're 
not in the city. The Eastdock Collective could probably recommend 
someone trustworthy."
 
Current status:
*	Time: Late afternoon, approaching evening
*	Party condition: Slightly tired, Cyrus depleted spell slots but 
emotionally restored
*	In Palanthas: 1 day, probably staying 1-2 more
*	Property secured: Warehouse 47, yours to use as you see fit
What's your decision about the warehouse?
And what do you want to do with the rest of your time in Palanthas?
*	Resupply and prepare for return to Haven?
*	Explore the city more?
*	Rest and recover?
*	Something else?
The sun is setting over Palanthas, painting the harbor in gold and orange light. 
You own property in one of Krynn's greatest cities. And Cyrus-Brother 
Cyrus-stands beside you, looking more like himself than he has since the 
storm.
1.	Allow Haven to take on the maintenance of the location as a staging 
area for their activities, with the understanding that the upper areas are 
reserved for our personal use.
Dec 10
WAREHOUSE 47 - DECISION AND 
ARRANGEMENTS
"We keep it as a safe house," you decide. "But we make it available to 
Haven as a staging area for resistance operations in Palanthas. 
They handle maintenance and operational costs beyond the base 
taxes. Upper floors remain reserved for our personal use when 
we're in the city."
Kessa nods approvingly. "Smart. We get a secure location in Palanthas 
without ongoing costs, Haven gets operational infrastructure in a 
neutral city. Win-win."
Cyrus adds: "And if Haven uses it for legitimate resistance work-
intelligence gathering, coordination with Solamnic Knights, supply 
distribution-it serves a higher purpose. That matters."
Thordin strokes his beard. "I can put you in touch with the Eastdock 
Collective's foreman-a dwarf named Grimbold Ironfoot. Solid 
fellow, discreet, no love for the Dragon Army. He could serve as 
caretaker and cover, handle legitimate merchant inquiries while 
keeping Haven's activities secure."
 
IMMEDIATE ARRANGEMENTS
Before leaving the warehouse, you take some practical steps:
Security:
*	Change the locks (Kessa handles this with her tools-30 minutes, 5 gp 
for new hardware)
*	Identify best entry/exit points for discrete operations
*	Note structural vulnerabilities that need addressing
Marking territory:
*	Leave personal items in the upper-floor quarters (establishing legitimate 
occupancy)
*	Place a few crates and supplies (gives appearance of active use)
Communication plan:
*	When you return to Haven, you'll inform Laurana of the asset
*	She can send operatives to establish operations
*	Grimbold will serve as the on-site contact
 
MEETING GRIMBOLD - EVENING
Thordin takes you to meet Grimbold Ironfoot at a dockside tavern. He's a 
stocky dwarf in his seventies, with a gray beard and sharp eyes that miss 
nothing.
"Thordin Ironhelm," he greets your companion warmly. "Heard you 
were in town. And these must be the folk who pulled my workers 
out from under that wagon."
Word has spread fast.
"Aye," Thordin confirms. "They've just acquired Warehouse 47. Need 
someone to maintain it, handle commercial inquiries, keep it 
secure. Thought of you immediately."
Grimbold listens as you explain the arrangement: official caretaker, legitimate 
front, but also understanding that the building serves... other purposes. You 
don't mention "resistance" directly, but Grimbold's no fool.
"So you want someone who can keep his mouth shut, handle 
legitimate business, and look the other way when necessary?" he 
summarizes.
"Exactly," Kessa confirms.
Grimbold considers, then nods. "30 gold per month, plus I get a room 
on the second floor for my own use. I maintain the building, handle 
rental inquiries, keep watch, and I don't ask questions about who 
comes and goes at odd hours. Deal?"
"Deal," you agree. It's fair-360 gold per year plus the 50 gp in taxes means 
the warehouse costs you 410 gp annually, but Haven will likely cover most of 
that through operational funds.
You shake hands. "We'll be leaving Palanthas in a day or two. When 
we return to Haven, we'll send word through appropriate channels. 
Expect contact within a month."
"Understood," Grimbold says. "And listen-what you did today saving 
those workers? That matters here. Dock folk remember. You ever 
need anything in Palanthas, you ask for Grimbold Ironfoot. I'll 
make it happen."
 
EVENING AT THE GOLDEN GRIFFIN - FINAL 
PALANTHAS NIGHT
You return to the inn as darkness falls. Miri serves another excellent dinner-
the four of you have become valued customers.
Inventory of Palanthas accomplishments:

*	Goodwill with Palanthas authorities
 
CYRUS - THAT EVENING
After dinner, Cyrus sits with you on the inn's balcony, looking out over 
Palanthas's lights.
"I want to thank you, Johannes," he says quietly. "For everything. For 
not trying to make it easier than it was. For letting me carry the 
weight. For... being there when I found a way to bear it."
He looks at his hands-the ones that crawled under stone to save a child.
"I'll never forget the five hundred forty-seven. They're part of me 
now, forever. But today I learned something: I don't have to let 
them define me. I can honor their sacrifice by saving others. Eleven 
today. Eleven tomorrow. As many as I can, for as long as I live."
"That's what a healer does. We don't count the dead. We save the 
living."
He stands, clasps your shoulder. "Thank you, brother. For helping me 
remember who I am."
 
THE NEXT DAY - PREPARING TO LEAVE
Morning brings final preparations:
Resupply:

Magical item distribution:

*	Ring of Feather Falling: Offered to the group. Who should attune?
Thordin's farewell: The dwarf is staying in Palanthas for a few more days

"It's been an honor working with you," he says sincerely. "If you ever

He hands you a contact token-a small stone carved with runes. "Show this 
to any dwarf in Thorbardin or send it with a message. I'll respond."
You shake hands all around. A professional partnership has become genuine 
friendship.
 
DEPARTURE - LATE MORNING
The four of you (you, Kessa, Cyrus, and your packs) head for Palanthas's south 
gate, the same one you entered through.
The guard captain recognizes you. "Safe travels, friends. Come back 
anytime. Palanthas could use more people like you."
You pass through the gates, leaving the great city behind. The road to Haven 
stretches ahead-about a week's journey through Solamnic territory, back to 
the hidden resistance base where Laurana and your companions wait.
 
THE JOURNEY HOME - SUMMARY

Seven days of travel, camping under stars, the rhythm of the road.
 
ARRIVAL AT HAVEN - ONE WEEK LATER
You crest the final ridge and see the hidden valley that houses Haven. The 
resistance base looks the same as when you left-small, concealed, but alive 
with purpose.
Scouts recognize you immediately and signal safe passage.
Commander Laurana meets you at the entrance, flanked by her staff. She 
takes one look at your group and smiles.
"Welcome back, Commander Constantinius. Brother Cyrus, Kessa. 
You've been gone three weeks. I trust it was productive?"
"Very," you confirm. "We have much to report."
 
DEBRIEFING - THAT AFTERNOON
In Haven's command center, you lay out everything:
Mission outcomes:
*	Thoradin's Hall delved successfully (no casualties)
*	Helm of Kharas recovered and delivered (3,000 gp earned)
*	Historical documents donated to Great Library (goodwill established)
*	Pre-Cataclysm property secured in Palanthas (Warehouse 47)
*	Caretaker hired, facility available for resistance operations
*	Goodwill established with Palanthas authorities through rescue 
operation
Laurana listens carefully, occasionally asking clarifying questions. When you 
finish, she sits back with an impressed expression.
"Exceptional work. You went for a simple artifact recovery and 
came back with strategic assets in Palanthas, financial resources, 
and-" she looks at Cyrus specifically "-renewed purpose."
She addresses Cyrus: "Brother, you look... different. Better. Are you 
well?"
Cyrus meets her eyes steadily. "I am, Commander. I won't claim to be 
healed-the weight of Flotsam will stay with me. But I've learned to 
carry it as purpose rather than just guilt. I'm ready to serve again."
Laurana nods, satisfied. "Good. Because we have work to do. The 
Dragon Army has been quiet since Flotsam-regrouping, 
reassessing. But intelligence suggests they're planning something 
significant. We'll need everyone at their best."
She looks at all three of you. "Take a few days to rest, resupply, and 
settle back in. Then we'll discuss next steps."
 
EVENING AT HAVEN - FULL CIRCLE
That night, sitting around Haven's communal fire, you realize how far you've 
come:
Johannes: Level 8 warlock/fighter, commander of resistance operations, 
owner of property in Palanthas, bearer of a demon's curse but still fighting for 
freedom
Kessa: Trusted companion, skilled operative, partner in multiple successful 
missions, survivor of impossible odds
Cyrus: Healer, servant of Mishakal, bearer of terrible knowledge but renewed 
in purpose, no longer defined by what he destroyed but by what he saves
The campaign continues. The Dragon Army remains a threat. Johannes's 
patron still demands tribute in nine months. The war is far from over.
But tonight, you're home. You're safe. And you're together.
